O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O you, most dear sons, I have completed this book which is the end of the science of medicine assembled from its employment, and I have finished it by its expositions and declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it occurred to me that I would complete this treatise with this surgeon, which is part of the work of the hands, namely surgery
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of the hands is difficult in our region and is strange to all, if the science is lost and forgotten, and nothing remains of it except for the small descriptions in the books of the ancients which the hands have followed
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this has come the error and the idleness, and the understanding is closed and the science is disordered.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	Or it seems to me that I shall give life to this treatise in its entirety according to the way of exposition and declaration and of abbreviation; and I shall join together the forms of the instruments of cautery, and of the other instruments of this work with the arrangement of the declaration and preparation of it, as it is necessary
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it befits him who meddleth in this work to be well acquainted with the science of anatomy, as Galen saith, so that he can judge of the members, and the forms and the joints and the separations of things, and have knowledge of bones and nerves and limbs and the number of bones, and the movement of the veins and the rest.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And thus Hippocrates taught us that the non-moving limb is useless, and the moving limb is useful; and in the art of healing the hand is like the other.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We are told in the beginning of this book that anyone who is ignorant of the things that lie before him, if he stirs up trouble and harms others, will learn many things of this science that he will abandon from lack of sense and understanding.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa .i. apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I have seen a madman who, having copped a scrophule or the head of a woman, has coped the arteries of the neck; so that so much blood flowed out that the woman died between his hands.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens .iij. jors.	And thus another time a stone of a bladder was extracted from a man, and the stone was great; it carried away with it a piece of the bladder, and remained in his belly for two days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And thus I have already been called to treat, and I saw the condition of the patient and the greatness of the stone, and I knew that if it were pulled out, he would surely die.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui prist en cure .i. duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi .i. termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And thus another time a man of our land took charge of a fracture of the limb and with splints made an incision; and the physicians were ignorant and stretched the fracture above the wound as if by strong binding, and left the wound without any bleeding, and left it thus until the limb was completely healed and the bone and flesh were lost forever
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I heard him call out and hurried to him; and when I arrived I found the limb dislocated without pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But in every way it was already corrupted or limb was unsound; and I could not cure it; and the dislocation continued to grow until the limb was completely lost
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And thus another malady which engulfs the abdomen and encloses the veins, and then inflates because of the malice of its lord.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For cancer, when it is caused by melancholy humor, does not suffice to touch it with iron except in cases where it can remove everything that is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en .ij. divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And thus, therefore, very heed the fact that the work of the hands has become divided into twelve parts: that is to say, huevre or there is peril in various situations; and I shall show in each part of this book where there is doubt and peril.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	For you must always bear in mind that if the fools speak badly of you, you should not take it to heart.</start_of_turn>
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	If you take your arms in custody, and undertake your patients calmly and firmly, and use the better way so that by the grace of God you may come out well; and let the dangerous diseases be banished by means of health; and stay away from those things which make you doubt, and have confidence in what you can do so that you may come from this world to the other in glory.</start_of_turn>
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.»	The physician's words hang in the air: "Do not seek medical attention for minor ailments, for only fools neglect their fate."
J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc .iij. chapitres.	I have devised this treatise in two chapters.</start_of_turn>
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapter deals with fire cautery and medical leeching, and this chapter orders from the head downwards; and the forms of instruments, and the materials for cautery, and everything that is necessary for the work.</start_of_turn
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter deals with amputation and incision, and wounds and abscesses, and the extraction of arrows, and cutting into stones, and similar things; and this chapter orders and the forms of instruments.</start_of_turn>
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter deals with restoring dislocations and fractures, as well as other similar matters; and it orders from the chief physician to have the limbs from the armpits downwards, and to form the instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	As we have remembered from our work, it is necessary to say what is the quality of the aid and the danger of great complexion.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the quality of the aid, and the danger, is the most long speech and subtle science and the greatest secret response; and about these things they speak more often than others, and they agree among themselves; and I find that their words are often too long.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que .ij. complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that the fire cautery helps universally for all complexion or matter, for as much as .ij. complexions: that is to say complexion is hot with matter, and complexion is dry with matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In complexion chaude et seche, assembled matter, some say that cautery is of great aid; others say that cautery is of no avail in disease except when it comes from heat and drought.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is hot, and must not be used to cure heat diseases by heat, nor by drought; and thus those who say the opposite that cautery does great aid in heat and dry diseases that arise from the humours of the body.</start_of_turn>
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body and its moisture to the complexion of fire, you find the body cold.</start_of_turn
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree to this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have never found it to be otherwise by experience.</start_of_turn>
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And all the way, there stands between me and fire no one but he who has experienced it, and who knows by long observation the chapter of cauteries, and the diversity of people’s complexions, and the dispositions and causes of their diseases, and the issues and means to prevent them; for other complexions we have no fear, even in cold and moist diseases.</start_of_turn
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all of them yield and agree to the cautery.</start_of_turn>
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know this, children, that fire cautery is better than any secret medicine or burning salve.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and brings no harm to any member other than the one being treated.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	Burning medicines come from one member to another causing grief and disease; and sometimes bring about the disease of the patient.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Fire by its height and for the goodness of its substance does no harm, if there is no excess
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And thus I have learned through experience and the length of my service and study in this art, that it is true about things; and for this reason I apologize for the length of my words, for it does not please me to withhold the secret which is returned or the fire, and the quality of work, as it explains the healing of diseases of the body, as the philosopher demonstrates; or you may consider it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	Know then, son, when it comes to making cauteries, they must be done at a suitable tension and with caution.</start_of_turn>
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	I say that the cautery is useful in all tensions, because the harmful effects which arise from it are overcome by the aid of the cautery; and even though the cautery is for necessary pains that are urgent and cannot wait for a greater tension, more serious harm does not arise from the member.</start_of_turn>
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And think not, dear son, that because fools make light of this; for the disease which is cured by cautery never returns; and he says so. But it is not so simple, for cautery is but a medicine which changes the complexion, and dries up humors which are the cause of pain, and is worth more than medicine for its promptness, and for the excellence of its work and its lordship.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And indeed it is known that the disease does not arise at all according to the complexion of the patient and the nature of the disease and its virtue; and there are assembled in him the superfluities by the acquisition of flesh and other things, if indeed cautery is administered in vain or if there is much superfluity and moisture, for in such a case the pain does not return; but this is often the case.</start_of_turn>
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand indeed that cautery is called the last of medicine, and indeed; but they do not believe that cautery is better than medicine, but their understanding is false, and indeed cautery is the last of medicine because when we administer other remedies in no illness and they do not help, then we administer the cautery, and it is worth more.</start_of_turn>
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore, although cautery is behind medicine, it does not agree with the intentions of the foolish masses.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that gold cautery is duller than iron, and they do not say that fire is useful for aught other reason than the quality of the gold and the fineness of its substance; and they say that the bloodletting of cautery does not make much difference, but this is not true, for I have proved it, and I have found that it is seen in many people; and gold cautery is worth no more than iron, as they say.</start_of_turn>
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And indeed, whenever you burn an instrument of gold, you do not know how it is blackened by the color of gold, and when it has cooled down; and if you burn it too much; if there is too much fire; and thus there is enough impediment.</start_of_turn
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this reason we use our fire cautery, as we have observed in our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Or you have commanded this chapter from the head down to the feet, because for this reason the way is easier to find.</start_of_turn>
dou cautere olivaire	olive cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	These olive cauteries are useful for moisture and cold on the brain, and there are two things that cause it: a disease called "soda," and many humors that descend from the head downwards, causing swelling in the eyes, ears, and throat, and for many dreams and pain in the head and neck, and even for all diseases that come from cold, such as paralysis, soda, apoplexy, and similar diseases.</start_of_turn>
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief .iij. nuis ou .iiij., selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	When the patient is purged by means of a medicinal solution modifying the head, iij or iiij, as the physician deems necessary and as the patient's condition permits, then make the patient spit out the head again.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses .ij. eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	Then sit the patient comfortably between your hands, and put his hands under his armpits; after that place the root of your thumb on the root of his nipple between his two armpits; and there will come out his two middle fingers, if it bleeds from the root then pull out the cautery which is called "olive", for this is the form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os .i. sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren .i. poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse .iij. jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And put out the sign of ink, and do descending and extracting your hand back and forth; then hold your hand loosely, and restore the limb if you see the bone even a little; and if you do not see it, repeat the cautery until you see the bone as I have told you; then take out one’s thumb, and place cotton wool around and under, and then take out the limb, and leave it for two days; after that put on a warm compress and cover with a bandage, and leave it as long as the swelling has gone down. Then cure the wound which is called "tetrafarmaçon", until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And they say the elders, that the more time that passes over a wound, the more it purges; and for this reason help is needed.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And they say none of these that we must leave the cautery on for so long that any part of the bone is scorched, and then we must renew what is scorched from the bone, and it must be cured.</start_of_turn>
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme .i. vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And they say others that we must leave the cautery on for so long, and press so hard that we break off as much bone as a woman puts in her fuse for the sake of these humors that come out too much; and we must leave the wound open for a long time; and then we must cure and bind it.</start_of_turn>
Et ces .ij. manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two methods of cautery do not seem to me to be of much use in all cases, for in some men or when there is danger; and I believe that I must leave it; for the pain of the patient is often excessive from the continuing solutions of nature, as we can see in other members; and even when the pain of the patient is slight by nature, the first sign of the cautery is more beneficial and more soothing for me, and for this reason I will use it in these cases.</start_of_turn
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	From ancient times, pain in the head.
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When chronic pain persists in the head for a long time, the physician should use leech therapy, pills called "cochie," and purgatives for the head, oil and poultices; and if the fire cautery is done as we have said, it is of no avail.</start_of_turn>
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take care if the patient's condition is very severe, and do not burn too deeply; for otherwise the cautery will be of no benefit.</start_of_turn
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai .i. cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est .i. leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After you have cauterized up to the bone of the head as we have said, do cautery of the vein which is called "vasselz"; and keep your hand still so that you do not move until you reach the bone: the patient feels much greater pain in this cautery than in others, and I will speak of it later; and it is better to cauterize the corners than the middle of the head, for the latter is how it is formed:
dou cautere dou chief	Dou cautere dou chief
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc .ij. manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When sudden pain occurs in the chief [shoulder], and the disease extends to the root, and the head of the shoulder is expelled by medicinal means, and other cures have been made as mentioned in the division of diseases, and all this has not helped: then make cautery in two ways, namely by means of medicine and by fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope .i. poc as .ij. chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi .xij. houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi .ij. jors ou .iij.; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The medicinal cautery is to take an alexanders root, and extract the bark and scrape it; if there are two heads of the shoulder, then make the temple where the pain persists as much as you can until the alexanders root is withdrawn from the skin; and when it is withdrawn, if you bind and constrain it well and leave it for fifteen hours; then remove it and treat the root with vinegar and leave the wound for two or three days; then put on a compress soaked in oil until it covers the whole part.

Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	And know that when you treat fistula as we have said in the division of diseases, and your treatment does not profit, then you must burn it according to this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to put his head in order; and hold his head between your hands in such a manner that it does not move, do not move his head; then put cotton wool soaked in egg or in vinegar on the oil; then burn the cautery that is partly: and let it rest on the head as if it were a feather of wool, gather up what is around it so that it is the cautery; if you see, if there is a point of the head that has bled from the other, and if you see that there is as much as a tendril; but all this is worth as much as your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After pressing the fistula, it swells out, and in going through the swelling, and the dryness; and if it closes, if the wound, and go out violently the hair; afterwards put on the hot cautery, and hold your hand over the cautery at the part where there is no feeling behind the oil, that your hand does not move foolishly; and put the cautery in the fat of the oil, and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien. Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse .iij. jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se .xl. jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If you come at the beginning of the cautery up to the bone, that would be good. If this is not the case, repeat the cautery once more, and if you have done this twice, and it has not healed, leave it for .iij. days; after that put on wet cotton in the wound and apply an astringent ointment until it is healed, and if forty days have passed and it has not healed, put on corrosive medicine until the bone is discovered; and leave as the chapter directs.</start_of_turn>
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent. Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure .i. camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	And there is a method of cautery for fistula that none of the ancients mention. In the fistula, and open the vessel; after that put in the cleft one camel hair of this kind, which is the form:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	And I do it in the amount of a third of a palm; and keep your hand or bandage firmly, and do not move the patient in any way, except that the melted wax runs down to its oil; and it is recommended to put above the oil to the patient a wet cotton pad in the bin of urine or in awe: the wax is so apt to flow like a fistula, and the rest for a marvel of health.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin. Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	And if the fistula is healed by the cautery that we have said, that is good. If not, if it is recommended to administer a purge to the spleen, and to bring the fistula back to the root as it should be in its proper place.
des crevaices en levres	from cracks in the liver
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times there arise cracks in the limbs which are called "hair", and even in the limbs of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe .i. petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these cracks in the way we have said in the sections, and the cure does not help, then you must perform a small burn cautery according to this fashion:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And hold the burn firmly in those cracks until it is healed; after curing the limb until it is whole again.
de l’aposteme de la goule	from the armpit of the shoulder
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies .i. cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou .ij., aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When the root of the tooth comes loose from the gum, or from the eye, or from the palate, or from the root of the teeth, after that it causes decay and pain and becomes swollen and becomes a fistula; and you must cure it as we have said in the divisions, and it does not help: therefore you must cauterize according to the quantity of the fistula; after that drain or pierce the fistula, and hold your hand until the blood stops flowing from the wound; and do this once or twice, after the cure of what we have said in the cures, until it is healed; and if it is healed once, it is good; and if it is not healed, you must uncover the bone and remove the corrupted bone, as you will find it in this chapter.
dou movement des dens	When the root of the tooth comes loose from the gum, or from the eye, or from the palate, or from the root of the teeth, after that it causes decay and pain and becomes swollen and becomes a fistula; and you must cure it as we have said in the divisions, and it does not help: therefore you must cauterize according to the quantity of the fistula; after that drain or pierce the fistula, and hold your hand until the blood stops flowing from the wound; and do this once or twice, after the cure of what we have said in the cures, until it is healed; and if it is healed once, it is good; and if it is not healed, you must uncover the bone and remove the corrupted bone, as you will find it in this chapter.
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you have cured it by medicine and this does not help, then put the patient’s head in your hand; after that remove the cautery which formed previously in this part as much as you can without causing pain; put some ointment into the cautery while it is still hot, and hold your hand until the patient feels the heat coming from the root of the tooth; after that release your hand and repeat the cautery as you please; after that fill the patient’s mouth with salt water, and keep it there for an hour and rinse thoroughly.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in part of the manner in which it was moving, if it is confirmed, and the joint becomes soft and restricted, and moisture becomes dry and corrupted.
de la dolor des dens	And in part of the manner in which it was moving, if it is confirmed, and the joint becomes soft and restricted, and moisture becomes dry and corrupted.
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc .ij. manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When pain of the teeth comes from cold, or there is cold or heat, and the remedies of medicine do not suffice, then it is necessary to cauterize according to two methods: cautery of the burr and cautery of fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus .i. fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	If the burr is like that which is taken from the navel of a calf, and the end is put in a spoon of iron or lead; after that take cotton and wrap over the point of a needle, and the soft matter in the burr is bulged out, and put on the aching tooth immediately and hold until it is cooled; and do this often until the virtue comes to the root of the tooth, and if you see if soft matter slips out and cotton in the burr is rough, and put on the aching tooth, and put on the iron again until the flesh comes to the height of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain. Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	The fire cautery must be so strong that you grasp a iron or a thorn with your hand; and if the fire does not reach the patient’s mouth, burn the cautery beforehand, and place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery is cool; do this often, for the pain will be great either today or tomorrow. And remember that the patient should fill his mouth with saliva in the haste of this cautery, and then withdraw it forcefully; and that is the form of the cautery.
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	Burn as much as you please, and according to what you desire; and that is the form of the burn.
des scrophules	pimples
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait ij. aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou .ij. se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi .iij. jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When scrofula is caused by phlegm and cold moisture, and is not subject to digestion by medicines, then eschew the cautery chest. For after this comes the form of the disease; and there are thereby two wounds on the other side of the body; and place the cautery hot upon the abscess once, or twice if necessary, until it reaches the front of the abscess. If the abscess is small, place the cautery according to the quantity of the abscess and leave it in place for two days; and place upon it a wet compress until the swelling is ossified. Then cure the wound of the abscess and the swelling until it is healed.
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc. Aprés li fai .i. autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	When moisture prevails over the channels of the pores and the same comes from a cold complexion, then it is expedient that the patient be first relieved by soluble medicines. Then perform the cautery at the root of the throat, and keep it so that you do not go further down to the throat, and do not linger there more than necessary. Then perform another cautery at the joint of the neck to the chest, and the one which is called the "clavicle" is like this; and cure the wound as we have said above until it is healed

de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	De la dislocation de l’ajutoire.
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement. dou cautere de pleuresin	of a pleuraisy.
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize .i. cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et .ij. petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et .ij. cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et .i. cautere emmi le pis, et .i. autre sus l’estomac, et .i. entre .ij. espaules, et .ij. as .ij. costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre .ij. espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The old folk said that we must make at pleasure cauteries of elder root, and in part thus: take an elder root long, the greatest that you can find, and be dry, and be as thick and long as your thumbs; and moisten in oil, and stamp on the fire, and cauterize. i. cauterize between the nipple and the belly, and ii. a few cauteries one inch in descending in the part which is below the beard; and iii. cauterize between the fifth rib and the twelfth, declining behind one inch. i. cauterize the spleen, and i. another upon the stomach, and i. between two ribs, and i. two ribs as many costae as go before the cautery that is between two ribs; and do not press me your hand, but open thus as when smelling.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a .i. raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie. And they say no ancient man uses a fire cautery resembling a razor, and puts the eschaufant and puts it between the ribs, until it comes to this incision; and the pain leaps out of him, as we have said in the incision of the liver. de ydropisie	After that, if the burn is not completely inflamed, perceive the burn from the other side; then draw out the cautery, and you will have three. The cautery is not effective for hydrophobia, except for the manner which is called “asclytes”. Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les .ij. ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	After leaving the cautery open for a long time to drain the infection, do not remove the dressing from the patient after the cautery; and healing will be expedited, and the two intentions will be reunited with the help of God.

de l’enfleure des piez	of the swelling of the pieces

de la menoison	After having made two incisions in the thigh, two cautery irons are applied to the knee joint at the base of the patella; let the cautery irons be long, one above the kneecap and the other below, in the middle of the thigh; and leave the cautery irons on for as long as is necessary to stop the bleeding; then perform the other treatments that we have mentioned.
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai .i. grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et .iiij. cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout .i. cautere clavile subtil, et .ij. cauteres sus les hainches.	When a solution of the womb comes from cold and moisture, as the retentive and digestive virtue which is the stomach and intestines is emptied, and cannot be cured by any means of treatment; and you see the patient well suffering and very pale, if you make a great burn on the stomach according to what has been said above or a burn of the stomach, at the burn that circulates; and three burns around the spleen at all times, one burn at the umbilical cord and two burns on the flanks.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et .i. cautere sus chaicun yle, et .ij. petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	If you see abundant moisture and the patient suffering, make a cautery on the navel, and indeed cauterize on each side, and two small cauteries on the stomach below the large one; for the cure is beneficial when there is good aid.
de la cure des emorroydes	If you see abundant moisture and the patient suffering, make a cautery on the navel, and indeed cauterize on each side, and two small cauteries on the stomach below the large one; for the cure is beneficial when there is good aid.
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: .iij. sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et .i. cautere desoz la boude. ij. dois;	When hemorrhoids are deeply rooted, or several, and are old and are composed of thick cold humors and moist pus, they are cured as we have said in division; it does no good to make cauteries: indeed, two on the backbone below the shoulder blades, which is all that is necessary to remove the pain immediately and permanently, and one below the buttock.
et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on .i. grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et .i. autre sus le foie, et i. autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens. And if you think the stomach is chilled, and the meat is not cooked, and you see swelling in the face, then you must make a great cautery upon the stomach, as it is said above, and another upon the liver, and another upon the spleen with all the nails of the cautery; and leave the cautery open for a long time. Then cure the wound until it is healed.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	And if you think the stomach is chilled, and the meat is not cooked, and you see swelling in the face, then you must make a great cautery upon the stomach, as it is said above, and another upon the liver, and another upon the spleen with all the nails of the cautery; and leave the cautery open for a long time. Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you deal with the thelulus, if you burn off the cautery that seems to scrape, and then put it all ablaze upon that thelulus that has been copied; and leave it there until the burn has reached the birth of the vein, without cutting; do this once or twice. If there is any remaining thelulus, if you burn them as we have said; after that, cure the wound with beneficial ointments until it is healed; and if you burn with a great cautery upon the belly, it will have more great help.
de plaie mal curee	Of a wound badly cured.
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot endure the size or opening, as we have told in his book, if there arises some disease that cannot be cured except by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont. Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou .ij. ou .iij., selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes. se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	When there is no wound, and it is swollen and emits putrid and moist excretions, if the physician has any hope of saving it, and he keeps that he must drain it completely. After he has drained the cautery seems to have raised; he should place the cautery into the fistula to the extent of the attempt that was made. He should repeat the cautery until the flesh becomes firm and corrupt, once, twice, or thrice, according to the quantity of blood that is required; and he must beware of nerves and large veins that are nearby. If the fistula is close to the bladder or intestine, he must be careful of these structures and only perform the operation in a calm state of mind. Think that it will not be lost; after curing the flesh until it is healed, if the structure is dry and the matter is ossified along its tension, then drain that it is healed entirely; but if the matter is not ossified, drain that the structure is broken and the bone is corrupted by it; and do this as we have said in our book.
de la maladie des reins	Of the kidney disease.

de la vessie	Of the bladder.

de la marris	De la marris.

de la hainche	When the hair is long and even,
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When viscous moisture descends into the hip socket, and because of this the limb becomes displaced from its place, the sign is that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and it is found that the nail of the great toe is displaced, so you must cauterize the patient over the hip socket, that is, cauterize like a circle, and mark in front of the limb around the hip socket so that the socket is within the circle; and if it is not so, cauterize as much as you cauterized the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If this cauterization does not suffice, make two olive-sized cauterizations, and do them as well as all the others; and cure as long as it is necessary.</start_of_turn>
de la dolor de la hainche	for the pain of the hip.</start_of_turn>
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes into the groin, from cold and moisture, and the patient is cured of that which we have said in the division; the cure is not worth it, for the disease is ancient: therefore it is expedient that you purge the patient of the gross humors with foul pills, or other solid pills like these.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu. Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche .iij. cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a .iiij. selonc ceste forme:	After that, make the cautery; and do the cautery as is right. That is to say, with mixed medicines and fire cautery. Fire cautery is done as is right by mouth, as follows: you cauterize upon the groin twice; you cauterize in a triangular form as is this, and do good depth and great, and put between each cautery a space equal to the thickness of a thumb, and let the cautery be olive oil; never make the cautery in the middle of the groin, for there are three according to this form.
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars. Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe. And thus is done in scatology when the pain lingers in the groin and does not reach the thigh or leg. And when it comes to the thigh and leg, if the patient says that the pain persists, then three cauteries are made; on the left side one; and either the cautery is fine or the swelling is great. And if the patient feels that the pain extends to two toes or almost as far as the knee, then the cautery is made at the place where the pain is felt.
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if the limb is stiff, if the patient says that the pain is from the groin to the thigh, then one cautery is made at the lower cautery or circular, and you must take great care in all your cauteries not to burn the nerves and great arteries, and not to cause the patient any greater discomfort and spasm.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez. Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	I myself have seen many people who have cauterized the ankle bone over the toe, and left it until the leg was entirely limp, and the bone was fractured, and corrupted all the bones. After a solution of the belly from which there was death.

de la dolor dou dos	From the pain of the back.
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether from sitting or from percussion or from too great an evacuation, or from similar symptoms of cold matter spread, neither of these signs is worth cautery, except for what comes from the infusion of cold matter.</start_of_turn>

Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	Many times this disease comes as a small wound, and the sign of its beginning is that it hurts the skin when it is struck, and fear; and you find in the lower spine of the back and in us the appearance that comes after the others.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you witness its cure, if you cauterize with the fire according to this form.

de la dolor des jointes	of joint pain.
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When joint pain arises from moisture that has spread throughout the limb, and when pain originates from a wound, the sufferer cries out "podagre" thus; when the cause is cold and the disease does not yield to medicines, it may be cured by cautery in part: make the mouth of the cautery around the joint of the limb, and let the cautery be of olive oil in this fashion.
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point». Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if it is necessary to prick the face of the limb, if you do cautery throughout the entire area you call "point". And if the pains arise up to the knees and to other joints, and this occurs many times, if you do cautery on each knee twice or thrice, with olive oil throughout; if you must do more, do so, but do not keep your hand firm for longer than necessary until the colour of the burn is as red as blood.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre. Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile .ij. lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines. Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	And if the pains descend to the knees and back, if you administer the cautery as we have said in this chapter. And if the pains are in the hands, if you prick around the ulna.ij. lines; and if there is no longer any pain, if you prick on some joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come down to the buttocks or to the shoulder blades, if you cauterize some part, and make the patient take good medicine and apply salves. For if you make him take good governance and purge phlegm, he will be healed with the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	Of the root of the scapula.
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When the scapula is fractured, and the bones slip downwards as in a wound, this is new; if you see that it is cured, do not move it immediately; and do not use things that leave your belly open, so that the intestines descend from your belly; afterwards make it sit on its belly between your hands, and command that it hold its shoulder tight until the bones are repaired, and keep it fixed at your sides, and mark an indentation of the nail on the scapula at the level of the collarbone, and as much as a half circle below the ribs; then withdraw the cautery as it is.
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles. Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui .i. cussin et .i. serjant sus les cuisses, et .i. autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Until it is soft and feels painless. Then reattach the bones to their place; and the minister holds his hand over so that they do not slip back; and care well for the wounds of the patient, and put some lint and some silk on the wounds, and another on his hand; then put the cautery on the sign at your whole hand, and hold it straight and hold it until you have grasped the bone, and if you do not grasp it the first time, do it again until you have reached the bone; and take care cautiously that the bones do not protrude when you make the cautery; that you do not burn them; and by this means the patient will not die, or anything else bad.</start_of_turn>
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien. Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés .iij. jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides .xl. jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And if you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work is in vain. It is proper that the cauteries of small people be subtle in measure and those of great people also great in measure; after two days the cure of the burn is finished as long as the scab is bony; after that the cure of other matters is finished when it is healed, and keep the patient lying down for forty days on his back until the wound is well closed; and make sure his movements are restful, so that the swelling does not emerge when he moves to his bed.
Et aprés .xl. jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse .xl. autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement. Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And after forty days, when he wants to rise, let him be given a well-made bath, and keep him for forty other days; and give him good rest, let him work moderately and be wary of eating too much drink and eating too much meat; and when he has followed these instructions, he will be entirely healed. And I will speak of the cure of the tail in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the evacuation of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai .j. cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a .iij. angles selonc ceste forme:	When other routes come into other bellies and are recognized, and you see that they no longer grow, then you shall make the burn cautery as much as it is necessary, and be three-fourths of the way through; after which, cure as we have said. And none of the old men have said that it should be cauterized with the burn cautery at two angles according to this fashion.
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile. de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old pain in no limb.</start_of_turn>
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor. s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence .i. autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	When pain arises in any limb, whether from sitting or injury, and the pain persists, and medical treatment is of no avail, then it is expedient that it be cauterized with the cautery which is called "points," or with other cauteries according to the length of the limb, its smallness and its weakness and its virtue and its location of torsion and its pain. If it is healed after the first cautery, that is well; if not, repeat the procedure once more, for it is customary to burn the surrounding area until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	When pain arises in any limb, or from sitting or injury, and the pain persists, and medical treatment is of no avail, then it is expedient that it be cauterized with the cautery which is called "points," or with other cauteries according to the length of the limb, its smallness and its weakness and its virtue and its location of torsion and its pain. If it is healed after the first cautery, that is well; if not, repeat the procedure once more, for it is customary to burn the surrounding area until the patient is healed.
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie. Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai .v. cauteres sus lou chief: .i. emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et .ij. sus les .ij. cornes, et .i. derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	The mesentery is never aided by cautery in great aid, and the same ailment that comes from the corruption of phlegm and melancholy. Can you see it being cauterized? Take warning if the ailment is at its beginning, and if it is cured according to what we have said in the division, and do not linger, and you will doubt that the corruption does not spread throughout the entire disease, then make five cauteries on the head: that is, one on the crown, and one at the front of the ears to the end of the cheeks; and two on the two corners, and one behind the earlobe; and leave the hand as long as the cauteries are coming out until the flesh is burnt out and the pus escapes, so that the vapors of the humors can escape. Cauterize the mouse according to what is before you.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the moisture is sparse throughout; and it is clearly visible, if you deem that you must cauterize from these cauteries which we have mentioned or chief, namely: one on the crown of the head, two on the shoulder blades, three on the spine of the neck, four on the buttocks, five on the groin, six on the elbows, seven on the wrists, eight on the fingers, and nine on the toes; and beware of the nerves that are behind the calcaneus, do not burn them; and never make the cautery on the bones of the heel or the stomach or the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus. Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers. Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	And as many times as you make the cautery, as much the more it helps, and makes him feel better; and as many times as the patient does not feel pain from the cautery as when he feels it, for the flesh is already corrupted. And you must know that the cautery must be great and small according to the limbs and joints, as you do in managing wounds. After treating the wound with flour several times with honey and other remedies until it is healed.
de enfleure	of swelling
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez. Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	When swelling occurs in any limb and is cured by medicines, oils, and plasters, and is not completely healed, then it is ordered to perform cautery on the limb according to the extent and degree of the swelling; and let the cautery penetrate deep into the flesh as much as possible. Then treat the wound until it is healed. And under no circumstances shall cautery be performed on the hand, foot, or back, at the risk of damaging the nerve that moves the limb, or if the swelling is bony. And in all cases, do not interfere with the swelling unless you are familiar with the limb and the course of its moving nerves and bones.

And under no circumstances shall cautery be performed on the hand, foot, or back, at the risk of damaging the nerve that moves the limb, or if the swelling is bony. And in all cases, do not interfere with the swelling unless you are familiar with the limb and the course of its moving nerves and bones.
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" is present, and medicine is of no avail, then it is ordered to cauterize with a needle a little deep, according to the amount of flesh, until the marrow is white and solid; and then treat with flour of times and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, with colon and alum, a part of each; mix them all together, and bind with a bandage, and keep it at rest until healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The cure for chancre by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble .i. cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.  Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	When the chancre first starts, and you see it stop, if you cauterize at the cautery that seems like a circle, all around the circumference of the chancre. And all the wise men say that one must cauterize also in the middle of the chancre; and all of them do not seem to me to be right, for I fear that it will become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already seen several times that this is the result; and the right thing is to cauterize around the circumference, at the cautery which is called the "circle", as we have said concerning cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling that cannot be measured
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi. Car elle se hastera de meureir.	When anyone has a disease which is called "adubelati," and it lingers in its death or through excessive production which the patient makes or through the decay of the patient when he is decrepit (that is, too old) and there is much blood, or for fear of tension; and you see her haste to death: then cauterize around the mouth of small cauteries by pricking; after that leave her alone. For she will haste to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see her perish with all the cautery, if she is burning too much, make the cautery less: for this is its form:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis. li cure dou feu par fer	The fire cautery. Instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches. Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.
