des porrelz qui vienent as piez	The fire cautery. Instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet. Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc .ij. manieres. C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude. Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe .i. cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi .iij. jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines. Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times it happens that when a piece of flesh has departed from its bone, a disease arises which is called "clos" according to our understanding, and is a great thing feared which swells the limb. And the cauteries of this disease are two in number. That is to say, fire cautery and hot water cautery. Fire cautery is when one bites like a thumb a pin of wool, and is made of good iron to the measure that it can penetrate the clot of all parts, and there must be subtle margins; after that put all around the clot, and hold the hand quite around the clot until it comes to the front of the clot; and leave it there for two days until it begins to bleed profusely; then make an embolus of wild mallow seeds bruised with oil, and leave the embolus on all night, and close the wound tightly and will root from its roots. Then cure the wound by applying charcoal as long as it is sane.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines. Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	And if it is converted by boils, and many times it happens in the hand and in the foot, if you must bring cautery of hot water; and this is in part a manner: take a splinter of spider or iron, or a thumb of wool, and put on the clot and the heel, that is to say, put nails of nails; and put the splinter on so that it covers all around, then put a little of hot oil, and hold your hand firmly, and press your hand by turning so that the margin of the splinter comes to the root of the clot, and you can find the hot water going deep down to the root; and give the patient a little of the hot water an hour; then leave it like that, and it will discharge all at its roots. Thus do another, until you have removed all of those which are at the bone, and then cure the wounds which cause charcoal.
li cure dou trembler	you cure the tremor.
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When anyone trembles from cold, or from a quartan fever, or from any other cause, if you shall make for him three or four cauteries on the spine of the back, one cautery between the shoulder blades, and one cautery on the flank and one on the stomach at the olive cautery, he will recover from the cold sickness.
des pustules puans	When anyone trembles from cold, or from a quartan fever, or from any other cause, if you shall make for him three or four cauteries on the spine of the back, one cautery between the shoulder blades, and one cautery on the flank and one on the stomach at the olive cautery, he will recover from the cold sickness.
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues. si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire. Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	Whenever pusules filled with blood appear, or swellings, which come from corrupt matters, if you see them at the first time, make a cautery on each head of the swelling: a subtle cautery of fir of Myrtle, or when the point is grasped by fire, or of long aristole root, or of the lenticular cautery. And never should you cauterize before they appear, following this method, for it does not cause the blood to flow forward, but ruptures the superfluousness from which they come, and they are healed; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	When the artery is severed.
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times there are great discharges of blood from the artery that is severed at the wound that comes from the surgeon, or at the incision of the abscess, or at the cautery of the limb, and similar things; and it is a great grief thing to extend it.</start_of_turn>
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And whenever this happens, if you are in a hurry to put your thumb on the wound of the vein, and you strain it too much without calming it down, and no blood comes out any more; then take the olive cautery and make it small or large according to the wound and the limb in which the artery is severed, and put the cautery on that vein or hold your thumb there, and hold the cautery as long as it is necessary until it is fixed.</start_of_turn
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it spurts suddenly when you remove your thumb from the vein, and the cautery is finished, take hold of the cautery immediately.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease to perform this one after the other until the limb is completely stretched out; and beware that you do not damage the nerve that is below, and that no other harm comes upon the patient; and keep your hands steady so that when the artery is large, you can adequately fill it up again yourself, except in the three ways that we have said: or by cautery, or by extraction when it is not otherwise treated, or by tightly tying a thread, or by medicines placed upon it that have power to restore blood flow.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever brings about the restoration of the limb with great care of cloths or of placing things burning upon it, or other similar things, if it does not profit, it is to no avail.</start_of_turn>

Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Ci encourag le second livre des cures de taille.

We have already spoken or first chapter concerning every disease in which it is necessary to perform cautery with fire, or applied medicine, and the methods, causes, instruments, and forms of cautery; and in this chapter we will speak of the hairs from the head to the toes, and I will go through this chapter by the same way as before, since we find it more conveniently in this way.</start_of_turn>
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And thus, as I begin this chapter, it is necessary to say, my friend, that there is more danger and fear in this chapter concerning the cautery than in all the others, and for this reason it requires greater caution.</start_of_turn>
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie. Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures. si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	And I warn you that you should not be rash. For many people have come to cures in such a way that, when their illness is severe and they feel great pain, they grow weary of their suffering and become reckless; and from this we must be wary.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse. Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	And there are those who will tell you: "Wait, I am well enough"; and the illness is serious. It is better for you to take more caution in your honour than in your cowardice, and do not rashly do anything but what you are certain of, and what you can safely take and use; and use prognosis and indication in the treatment of your patients so that salvation may be either achieved or abandoned. This will help you to recover renown, glory, and lasting memory.</start_of_turn>

Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen such a fierce disease except in childhood, and among those whom I have known; and for this reason it seems to me that it is worth leaving the work in parts for cures.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I once saw in childhood that the head of the shoulder was dislocated, and the bone grew so large that it could not bear its weight; and there was such an abundance of moisture that it filled the cavity between the bones above the scapula, between the shoulder blade and the upper arm; and when such moisture is collected between the scapula and the arm, and the incision is small, the head of the shoulder must be made wide open. As long as the moisture remains between the scapula and the arm, the limb will be deformed like that of a splay.</start_of_turn>
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is greater and the incision is larger, make two incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	If moisture softens the bone, and you see the edges of the bone split widely over the greater part, and it becomes acutely painful when you press it with your hand from within, and this does not return: if you suspect that the bone is fractured, make two incisions as follows:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers. After the incision, drain out all the moisture. Then tighten the edges of the skin and fat, and put in wine and oil, and leave it for five days. Then remove the dressing, and cure the wound with stitches and ointments, and leave the limb elevated, and feed the patient dry food until the limb is comfortable and healed.</start_of_turn>
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	Another way of making an incision is to look at the opening of the abscess and the accumulation of fluid; for never is it before; never behind; never to the right; and never to the left.

de reume	When the shoulder or the armpit is open, and the filling of the liquid, and you do as you please; but beware that you do not cover the artery; and let the vein flow blood, for if the patient dies from excessive bleeding and evacuation of moisture.

Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	For it is necessary to extract the arteries, for they are filled with much fat and put on tight bandages; and when they are loosened, if there be no cure for dry medicines that cause the hair to grow and nails to harden, until they are healed; and if without restraint of the artery as much as you do with the work of your hand, if you haste to cover with cautery, or if you use the hand of vitriol and strain it at your hand that it does not stain; and if you do not have this present, if put out the hand must be much as it does not freeze, and rise the hand of cold water until it stops, and be strained as it should be; and what is milder and lighter in the extraction of the artery is that you cauterize the vein of this cautery cutting through a third part, but that the cutting be well spaced to ward off more length of time the heat.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instrument is too tense, it holds less heat.

Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai .iij. fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com .ij. doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres .ij. as .ij. costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as .ij. costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des .ij. mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de .iij. dois au traver joins;	And they call it the ancient "cure contuse"; and you shall make at the patient who has this disease the hairs that he has above or below, then make two incisions or as many as are equal in length according to the length of the front; and whether one of the incisions is like two thirds of the way down the front swallowing down saliva until it reaches nothing, and the others as many as are two thirds of the way up from the papers, and keep the incision of the arteries that are as two thirds of the way up from the papers; and hold your hand from the continuation of the two mandibles, and be careful not to make too great an incision.

si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If in the first incision the instrument which is called the "cultellaire", and which is very well cut on one side and slightly blunt on the other, is not sufficiently cutting, it is like this:

If in the first incision the instrument which is called the "cultellaire", and which is very well cut on one side and slightly blunt on the other, is not sufficiently cutting, it is like this: take the handle of the instrument and incline it towards the armpit at the shoulder, and incline the blade towards the bone, and keep it like that until it reaches the middle of the incision. And take all the blood vessels that descend from the chief as long as the incision is continuous until it reaches the armpit, and then do the same from the middle of the incision until the other end; then draw out the blood equally, express the vessel for the blood taken; then put in the incision a little piece of cotton wool, and put on moist cloths soaked in wine and oil and vinegar, and keep that the postulations do not move; and after three days remove the dressing, and mix in plenty of bruised plants of rue, then cure with basic ointment of oil of rose, and other cures which are used for wounds, until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	since the evacuation of blood
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When no acute cautery is done, and you see the eyes tense and small, and the pupil dilate, and the papers burn; and the hair cries out, and where it has been pricked, it causes acute pain, and the patient coughs; then there are discharges from these accidents except for those of matters and catarrh that come from many veins, and it brings relief that it is so.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large. i. poc. de l’estoupement des oreilles	From the swelling of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Whatever is causing the swelling of the ears is one of three things: grains, or pus, or a stone or some other object like iron; or semen, like in the case of lice, beans, peas; or something that flows downwards like blood and pus and other things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel. Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus. Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	When there is a stone or other foreign body in the ear that does not fit into the ear, do not put anything into the ear. If you see the stone, if no violet oil or sesame oil comes out, then remove it; and let him spit out the vomit, and stop up the nostrils when he spits, and put around the ear pieces of cloth or wool; and press the ear downwards. Many times this cure comes out by itself; and if it does not come out, it is necessary to remove it with fine tweezers. This is the form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes out by itself, that is good; if not, remove it with fine tweezers. And if it does not come out by this method, make an incision at the root of the ear, or cut away a part of the ear, and stop up the hole with wax if necessary; then the pain will go away, for often it comes out by itself as we have said; and if it does not come out in this way, take hold of the ear and press on the stone or whatever it is, and the pain will go away.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If these things do not suffice, if you are in haste to make an incision at the earlobe as at the base of the thumb, and spasm, and the method of the incision is that you make first the chief sufferer endure the pain of the cephalic region, and draw out blood according to the measure of its virtue; then seat the sufferer between your hands and turn the ear downwards, and make a small incision at the root of the ear at the fatty tissue or bone depending; and make the incision as wide as a crescent moon, as long as you live to the bone, and the bone according to your ability, and extract the pus promptly from your mouth; and cure until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is grains that are swollen and it swells, if you administer extraction; and if it cannot be extracted, if you advise .i. sponge held tightly according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain. Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	but do not make this incision until you think that the grain is moistened by the moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces of it; then extract it with tweezers and with suction, as we have said, so that the extraction is aligned.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton. Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est. s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin. se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent .i. jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	When the ear is acutely painful, let the patient place a poultice beforehand on the ear, and fill the ear with cotton wool. And whether the pain is above or below that ear, if it bursts from this, it is good. If not, take many pins according to the length of the ear must stretch and lighten, and push them one by one into the fire; and put the patient’s ear one or two fingers into the fire, and pull out from the other side, and push another finger against the finger that is in the ear; and do this until the pain is all gone. And if you see, take hold of one of the pins and burn the other as long as the pain remains; then do the rest of the pins until the pain is all gone, as we have said concerning the pin.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the ear, if it is of small size, as a flea and the like, cure it as we have said in the division; but if it is of large size, we must feel it, and its extraction is necessary; that is the easiest thing to remove from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms from the ear, when you have cured as we have said in the division or performed distillations, and the cure does not help, if you must look at the ear in the sun: if there are no worms visible, if you have seen subtle scars, and if there are none, take the tweezers that are like this: (the author describes the shape of the tweezers).
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus. Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent. Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And let the dressing be broad and soft. And as for the most subtle head of the ear according to the quantity of the patient’s suffering, do this often until you see them all issue. And if they do not obey to issue, if I push into the cotton around the ear as I have said concerning the stone; and if they do not emerge forcibly as we have said, give distillations that the ancients have proved useful in the incision of worms, and you will find them or treat them with distillations; and if you distil your oils and medicines into the ear with all these instruments, this is the form as you see.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And let silver or gold be spread out from the outside to the inside of the ear, i.e. a few losses; and on the outside pour distill. And for pressing from the instrument of lead which is well made for this, and if you see take a scraper and wrap around the tip immediately cotton; then pour out your oil or juice, and what you see of your medicines in the cannel, and the cannel be in the ear; then pour out from the scraper into all the cotton, and press your hand moderately until the oil is distilled or until the ear is almost numb; and the patient will feel it within, and let the distillations be neither too hot nor too cold, for the medicine will not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	because of the swelling of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without some imperfection in their ears; and the same happens among adults by the bursting of a wound or by a foreign body entering the ear. Such bursts never happen without leaving some mark in the ear, if we do not see them; and never happens without some loss of hearing.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	That which leaves a mark in the ear, if we do not see it, is a sign of serious illness in various conditions, and in this one it is clear that you put the diseased ear in the sun; look inside: if you see the swelling, if the swelling has filled the whole cavity, like this is the shape:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And be cautious both front and back all around, if it does not bleed the ear; if the swelling is of a foreign body in the ear, if you see small incisions, and if you touch it lightly, as long as the foreign body is entirely bony.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren .i. raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille. Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	And if swelling is perceived in the ear, take a small blunt instrument and burn a small hole in the ear, then insert a piece of lint. If you feel the swelling which the patient complains of is pressing in the ear, pierce slightly, and keep that you do not damage the nerves of the ear; then insert into the ear a wick according to the size of the perforation, and fill in the cavity Egyptian style.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this without delay until the wound is healed, or take a wick and fill it with pink liquid, and powder upon vitriol broth; and if you see it flee from the ear, it is likely that you have torn the wick and move another wick filled with grease which is made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling is bony; then cure it until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if there is discharge of blood comes, if you soak a sponge and drape it with cold water, and put it on the ear, and use other treatments which are useful to stop the discharge of blood which are either to apply distillations.</start_of_turn
de la char des papieres	De la char des papieres.
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	From the heap of papers
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if it is not well cured, if the fire cautery is applied too late after the incision is made, it is of no use; and often the roots are burned and do not recover again.
de la gresle	De la gresle.
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope. se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	Many times come papers of blood from things that seem greasy in their form and in their hardness; and for this reason this disease is called "granulomatosis", and is an assembly of great moisture in the substance of the body; the work is like this: take guard if the granuloma moves from one side to the other, and that is a light thing to know; then do the incision of a large part, then peel off the soft part lightly, then take hold of the tweezers, and grasp. If you do not grasp it in a sense to perceive a little of the body, if it does not grieve the patient; and if the wound is great, if the assembly has a costure, and cure until it is healed; and if it is small, do not make force, for it will return by itself and cause harm.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the granuloma descends downwards from the ear towards the upper part, if you reverse the body, and pull out the granuloma with tweezers, and press from one side and the other; and if the body is loosened by the incision, this does not grieve; and when the granuloma is grasped, if it leaves oily water, cure the body of that which causes harm until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the blood
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil. Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	The greasy exudate is enclosed in paper tissues, and this happens more in women than in men, and brings grief to their eyes, and they come to discharge at dawn, and do not dare to look at the sunlight for this reason, because the tears hurry away from their eyes; and because they lie down with their faces downwards, and sleep, and their paper tissues are wet with their tears which swell and appear to cover their eyelashes with the exudate that comes out in oil. And when you press their body and feel the exudate between the bones.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	If the patient places their head in its proper place; then take one drape of linen and make a loop in the manner of a circle according to the quantity of exudate from the lower part of the body, and put it on top; and press on the body from one side and the other, so that the exudate is gathered into the circle; then make a small incision at the edge of the moisture trenching a wound not larger than the wound made to the vein; and make the skin taut as much as you see to the exudate; and in various situations there comes exudate from the wound, according to the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Pull out the fatty substance from all around your thumbs between your shoulders, and twist your hand to the right and to the left as much as necessary; and keep that you do not insert anything into the wound, that you do not go too far up to the oil, that you do not stain it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if it does not open at the beginning of the wound, if you cut a little around the wound slightly until it opens; then take out the foreign body as we have said, then moisten the bandage and water, and put on the limb, and strain it carefully.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree. Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez. Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there are such thorns which break and put on to prevent the moisture which has gone dry. Then cure it until it is healed. And if it comes to the limb at the abscess, if you cure the abscesses that are surrounding it as much as it is healed.</start_of_turn>
des poilz des papieres	of hair papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When papers are born with hair growing other than its natural way, and are overgrown, if they prick the eyes, they cause tears and bring on various diseases like common tears and softening of papers and gum, up to the point of destroying the eyes; the cure for this is in three ways: either by complete fire cautery, or by medicine according to what is before or alongside fire cautery, or by incision and suture or by ligature, according to what I shall say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You must place the patient’s head in your left hand, and move the paper from the oil to your right hand; if it is converted, it is good; if not, if there is a thorn at any point of the paper, either cut the edge of the paper or the hair will grow out from these hairs; and take out one thread from the underside of the paper, and stretch out the paper from the underside, from the great to the small; then take out the one thread, and put some small lint and bandage on the paper, and make a mark on the paper like the spur of a myrtle, and when you have made the mark it is understood that the paper that was destined to you is no longer there.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les .ij. lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des .ij. angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout .i. fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les .ij. sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a .iij. jors ou .iiij.; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	And if there is a part that has been affected with a great quantity of paper according to what the paper is softened; then do everything from the line that you have marked, and from the great to the small tear; and if there is one of the incisions close to the natural hair at the thickness of a root, then insert the ointment in one of the two angles of the wound, and pull it out whole; then gather the two layers with a suture of a needle with a thread of silk, and wipe away the blood, and leave the surplus of the thread on the two corners of all things that are glued, as you see; and if you do not see this, if there is no cure, then leave the suture and the thread for two or three days; and then cure the wound with things that are dry and constricting, because the paper comes back to its place at the bottom of the wound and the gathering of it, but the suture is useless (as the old people say), and that is work without fear;
et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a .iij. oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if in another way: if you mark the mark of a figure which is just like the flame of a myrtle, as we have told, then you must evacuate two ounces according to the shape which is like this:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then hold back what is above with small forces equally according to the shape which is like this
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait .i. fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute .i. autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	And if you cannot hold the pins and the thing is not even, if you take a needle or if there is some thread, and you bind the mark with the needle; and you take another thread of more length and another thread of less length, and you assemble between your two thumbs the two threads equally; then hold your hand equally, and hold all the skin over which you have marked, as we have told, then assemble the two layers of the wound by suture, and cure until it is healed; and if there is an abscess at your incision, if you apply grease and some similar soothing compresses.
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And never has it happened that the hair of the armpits is converted: if you use what we have said of incision; but the costure in one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure for armpits is as follows: convert the hair and fat according to what has been said, and then make three incisions by art, and three threads as long as the hair and expand with space; and take three hairs or hold the threads; then assemble the one and the other securely above what rests on the oil of the hair. Strain the three hairs from the three parts forming; and leave it like that for a few days, and the skin which has been strained will become wrinkled and necrotic and will swell, until it comes loose by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope aunes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des .ij. cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it is late, if the incision has force, then cure until it is healed; and when the wound has healed, and if the hair has been pulled out, they will no longer prick; and this is the form of the three incisions that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The work is such that you grasp a subtle needle, and there is in it a thread of silken stuff; then assemble the joints and do not leave one without the other, and let the length of the threads be a palm in length; then command in the chase another thread of silken stuff briefly, and do not leave the head of the thread; then put the patient's head in its place; and let there be daylight if the work is done carelessly, for it is a subtle and small work; then withdraw the needle to the very root of the hair, and make it pierce in the flesh until you have driven it as much as the natural position of the hair; then withdraw the hair until it is gone from the chase, and bring back into the chase that hair, if there is one or two or three or more; then withdraw your hand until the blood vein flees to the very chase in the flesh with the natural position of the hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	If the chase is treated and the hair does not come out with it, if you drive the chase from its end to the very thread that you have commanded, until the chase blood comes out through the wound and you see it by the sight of the oil; then if you drive the chase and the thread, close the oil and leave it closed for two days or three, until the hair has regained its place and the swelling has gone down.
de la porriture de l’oil	From the putrefaction of the oil.
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de .ij. manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.  Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	When this ailment which is called "aleacrati" or the porerty comes to light, if there are two ways in which it presents: one natural, and the other unnatural. And it arises from a wound, or from a burn or cautery, and from similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent. Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	And the way in which this work proceeds is that you make this suture, dry the layers, put in stitches of linen, and leave it until it is healed; and do not do anything else except use in the treatment of this things that dry and restrain. For if you do this, if the disease returns it will be worse than before; but there are things that are softening, such as fennel; and vinegar or alum and flaxseed being cooked, and melted beeswax, and it covers a bandage, and treats this.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your treatment is that you must take care that it does not heal differently from the way it was before; and this work that we have mentioned is not fierce except for addressing this disease, that it does not return differently from the way it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	From the cauldron which comes in the oil.
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens. Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait .i. fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en .ij. chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a .i. spatumile large.	This sickness which is caused by a wound which is violent is called “axacrati”, and is natural and accidental. The accident comes from injury and from cautery and from things which are similar; and the way of work in this chapter is if you take an arrow, because it has two threads, and the thread is in the cauldron, and it makes the left eyebrow bleed so that the thread of the vein is in two inches of the cauldron; then the cauldron is taken away from all the arrow, and the head of the arrow has one span wide.</start_of_turn>
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren .i. raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent .ij. fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des .ij. fendures des .ij. angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «.j. griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les .ij. parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the head of the arrow returns as it should, that is good; but if not, take one needle and put it into the wound, and turn the arrow, and make two incisions or cost the inside of the arrow; and if there are two incisions from two angles of the incision which you have made, and make one angle so that when they are assembled, the figure is as if it were the letter which has not “j griesche”; then break that cauldron, according to the quantity of its cost and disease, of that which teaches the arrow, then join the two parts which are severed, and join them with a thread of linen; then treat this with the medicines which we have said are mollifying and soothing, and with bandages, until it is healed.</start_of_turn
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	If the malady comes from a fracture, sprain or cautery, if you must make an incision, make a full incision around the hairs of paper; then stretch between the two leaves of a tent as I have said; and must be made according to the form of the malady, for it is diverse in form, and the wise masters perceive very well all sorts of things how to make return to their natural shape; and the patient himself, according to what must be done of work and instruments in various dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	If the malady comes from a fracture, sprain or cautery, if you must make an incision, make a full incision around the hairs of paper; then stretch between the two leaves of a tent as I have said; and must be made according to the form of the malady, for it is diverse in form, and the wise masters perceive very well all sorts of things how to make return to their natural shape; and the patient himself, according to what must be done of work and instruments in various dispositions.
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this suture has to be done at home in a rather clumsy way as when the patient’s limb is soothed with oil, and cannot move or perform its natural functions, if you must therefore drink the tip of a needle from the wound and hold it high; and as soon as you see bruising, as long as you can keep within the limit of the sensitive area, which is not too deep and not too shallow, so that the patient does not suffer too much from the bruising or from the oil; and your incision, which you must make with care, so that the tissues are not too tight or too loose, so that the limb returns to its natural shape; and when all the tissues are stitched up again, do not put in any more salt-water, but rather water that is soft and soapy; then put between the limb and the oil a bandage of linen, and cover the oil with thick wool; and after that use a bandage of wool and other soft things until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	De l’ungle de l’oil
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Saiches that the nail is according to two methods: it is nervous and seems like tough wax, and another which is not very nervous, but seems like pale moisture congealed, that when one touches it with iron and boils it, it does not move; and both seem to begin towards the great tear, and twist about as much as they cover all the eye and the light and the movement of the oil.

Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And keep that the sponge does not touch the thick cloth and break it, and that the needle does not pierce through; and after the incision, pour oil a spoonful of bruised oil into the wound, and sprinkle it with alum, and leave it until the other day; then cure what is left until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nervous, and you cannot push the needle, and the thread cannot enter, many times this semblance of a nail is cured; and as I have said in the division, if you see it covered, if the patient suffers, pour oil the patient’s body, and take the sponge lightly as required in this fashion:

And withdraw the nail subtly, and if you see that it has diminished point and the edge is pressed, if you distill from your mouth into the oil alum, and sprinkle it with red alum and bruised oil, and squeeze out the oil until the other day; then repeat the other work as required in this manner.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing opposes you, if like an abscess you have opened, then milk, and first close the wound thoroughly while it is healthy, and afterwards resume the work as before, while it is healthy.

de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the seed that grows on the plum.

et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance. des voines des eulz	From the veins of the eyes.

Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And be doubled in degrees by degrees in a circle according to this form:

de la fistule de l’oil	And if you are unable to collect all this in that hour, if you make a poultice upon the oil of soothing things to ease the pain of the eyes, and leave it until the pain is appeased and is secured after the cautery, then begin again according to this method as long as you are well; and this is the way of forces: from the fistula of the oil.
