de la bowe de l’oil	De la bowe de l’oil.
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de .ij. pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit. si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee .i. poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	The disease called "alcunnati" is not fierce except for the swelling which is made in oil, resembling descending water, and it is not actually water; and the manner in which it appears is that if you make the patient sit in a chair which appears and is straight, then take hold of his head between your hands at either side, and move him until you see the swelling come down to your eyes; then either bind him, and do not let him descend and loosen the light, and see the patient do the same things as before; and if it does not descend by itself, give him vinegar that is as strong as water, and when it descends from the swelling it is not apparent as we have said. If you make the patient sit between your hands, then take the sponge and put it on the corner of the eye. That is, by the continuation of the conjunctiva with the corner and the crown, as long as the swelling is there; and when it is evacuated, distillate in the warm oil mixed with honey, or vinegar or fenugreek is boiled and honey, and then be cured of other cures until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	From the oil bowl.
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit. Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre. se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit. Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis serre l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre. se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.
Aprés repose .i. petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens. Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.  Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	After a little rest, if the water comes back down the second time, put the force with the instrument, and when it is firmly fixed and does not move, remove the instrument slightly by circling your hand back and forth; then put back a little of the water and leave out that oil. Then put on greasy oil or linsey cloth soaked in rose oil and covered with eggs, and tie with the oil again.  Thus, and those who are with us, put on a bandage with plenty of eggs.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almagda cannot enter the oil because there are too many hair roots, since there are parts of the body which have too tightly closed the hairs, it is necessary that you take the instrument which is called the «alberit», which is like this:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai .i. leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide .i. dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en .j. leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And pierce then the conjunctive only, and do not linger too long, but make a slight incision, then put in alum. As we have said; and when the work is finished, the patient will experience sleep coming upon him; while he sleeps on his back for one and a half hours; and let him be immobile, and take nourishment of lean meats, and do not move his head to the right or left, and keep him bound as before; then release him in this same house, and make him cough up his sputum, and let him see nothing, and then return his eye to its socket, and keep him quiet for seven days. Do not do this in the midst of the cure or after the incision, but see that you give him food, for in this way the pain will subside.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice .i. orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse. Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	When the swelling has gone down, remove the oil before the seventh day, and address this to what relieves the abscess; and when it is calmed, remove the eye and put on its face a little ointment to cover the wound, and keep it in this same house. And then go out of the house and enter again, and he will recover in his case; and his wounds that no disciple must interfere with in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us from Iraq who told us that in his peace he had seen alum put into the eye, when the water had succeeded the pain, but we have never seen or read of it in our land or in the books of the ancients; and it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the signs of the forms of an almond, for those who do not know them; and they are like pearls properly:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And their heads are of this same subtlety, and their backs in two angles like a bow.</start_of_turn>
de la char sor le neis	like the almond from the pear on the stone.</start_of_turn>
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color. En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; puis cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	Sometimes almonds or various peas do not emerge from the stone; for there are some that look like scorpions with teeth; and if there are such or if an almond is pierced with a sharp stone, and if it has a gray flesh and a white bone color. In those in which this almond is white and not pierced, it is necessary that you make the patient sit between your hands and expose his nose to the sun; and cover his nostrils, and spit out the almond at those peas, and pull them away; then grasp what you have put under the thumb of your right hand, until you are sure that the almond is entirely broken.</start_of_turn
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	If nothing remains to be done, if the incision has reached its utmost extent, if nothing remains to hold; and if without delay you do not sew it up or ligate it, or if you delay too long, or if it is a malignant abscess, then hasten and cauterize it while it is still unstained, and remove all the purulent matter. Then spit out or drain the wound immediately, with ease and without delay.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, acoi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes .i. fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice .i. doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil. Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu .iij. jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	If the wound does not discharge, and moisture comes up to the throat, discharge the purulent matter that is still sane; and if moisture does not break through as it should, discharge the purulent matter from the bone below, because the instruments will not come through without tearing: therefore you must drink a large thread, grasp it with your hands, and leave about an inch of space between each knot; put the patient’s hand in the hole at the root of the tooth, and stretch outwards until the tooth comes out through the hole in the mouth; and do this several times, for the child will have learned to do it; then keep the chief that comes out through the hole with one hand, and the other chief that comes out through the mouth with the other hand, and remove the purulent matter alternately as we have said that should be done; do this until you are sure that the root has been completely removed; then stretch out the thread, dry the wound, and moisten the thread with Egyptian balsam, and put it back in place as before; do this for two days or more, until the pus has rotted away all that remains of the root; and then put in or remove a sponge for several days until it is healed, and if there are any sedative medicines, use them if necessary; and this is the form of the instrument for purging the tooth, from which we distill oils and medicines or the like.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it may be of silver or lead, resembling a large lamp, if like a sponge; and guide it thus; and if you see it, make a closed sponge, and hold the instrument level for purging the tooth; and put a hand on the tooth to hold it when we are pouring oil or no liquid.
de la char sor le neis	From the shoulder joint downwards on the neck.
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times there arises in the neck a disease which is called «telul», and it grows and becomes great again, so that it is seen; and for this reason it is necessary that you commence to apply the cautery or burning medicine at once, and extract the bone thoroughly, then bring forth the hair or scorched matter; and if you delay in covering it while it is great, if there is any hardness, of foul colour, or loss of sensation: if you do not touch it with iron, for it is a dangerous abscess, for whenever it is touched even once, there results great harm to the patient; and if the abscess is of soft touch, not of foul colour, you will see that you can cover it completely, if you leave the patient and cover it without pain, and cure the limb of dry and restraining things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the neck is cut and bound over.
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes. Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les .ij. levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	The wounds which, when the liquid of completion comes into one of these cartilages, are useful for the most part, for in some homes. It is therefore necessary that this should not happen to any, if one regards whether the wound is fresh throughout its extent; and therefore one must join the two layers at a costure, and then cure until it is healed; and if the layers have already separated from one side and the other, one must guard all the parts of their circumference until they bleed again, and then reassemble the two layers at a costure, and strain, and sprinkle with powder of dragon’s blood, and incense; and put upon the powders a piece of dressing of great or another dressing that will adhere, and leave it until it bleeds by itself, and then cure until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of stitching is as follows: if you assemble the solution: or with needles, as we have said in the costure of the belly; or with thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	of the separation of the layers of the skin.
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	At home, in the hands of the patient, are placed the apices of the thumbs, resembling grains of wheat, minor and major; therefore it is to be known that you must turn the thumbs, make incisions upon each nail, and grasp them with tweezers and press them into the flesh; then apply the leech after the incision of the vitriole broth, until the wound is no longer bleeding; then remove the leech easily, and cure the wound with dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	Concerning the pain of the jaws.
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times it happens that on the teeth of the jaw, which are called “albulus” by the ancients, there is pain; if you support it, grasp the root and leave the socket or the blood out; then put out the vitriole broth or other restorative and drying powders; and if the tooth comes out again after the incision, and this happens many times, if you grasp it a second time and cauterize: if it does not come out again after the cautery; these are the forms of the instruments to cover.
des sordens	Des sordens.
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	The teeth are often gathered at the root of the jaw, between the gums, which are rough and biting; and never are the teeth black and yellow and turned towards, until the corruption comes to the gum, and the teeth are biting; if it is thought that you make the patient sit between your hands, and his head be steady, and open the jaws or the gums, until nothing remains; and thus make black and green, and yellow and other spots, until they are whole; and if we did that from the beginning, that would be good; if not, if you repeat it twice or three times, until you have done everything. And the teeth that have been mixed with various forms of instruments to redden them, as it is shown by the work, for those that remove the teeth have other forms than those that are used between the teeth; and these forms and others are seen with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is appropriate when you cure the tooth of its pain that you also delay a little so that it does not hurt too much, because it must not be done carelessly; for it is a high-quality substance, so we have no excuse for making it suffer
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant. Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	When the patient is constrained to endure, if you are certain that the pain will depart, many times the pain will vanish from the patient, whether it is acute or chronic, and make the limb move. And though the pain does not depart entirely while the mischief persists, as we have already done for these scoundrels; and when you are well certain that the pain will depart, you must tightly bind around the limb with strong thread to keep the joint firmly in place; then press your thumbs deeply into the flesh at the first and second joints, while making them well rounded; and then firmly bind the thread around the limb. Keep the head of the shoulder firmly in place between your knees until it ceases to move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier. Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	Then draw the limb directly toward you, and if it does not move, grasp none of these instruments and pull it slightly inward; and move it as you did before. If the flesh is seen to be tense and bruised, if you are certain, fill it with cloths, either coarse or fine; and if the thread is tightly bound, do not break it by pulling; and you must smear ointment around the joint to soften the bone
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere. Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And take care that you do not break it, and leave a part of it, and return to the patient with the greater pain of the first. And take care that you do not do what the ignorant layman do, who break the limb every time without reason, and do not bring about anything but these things that we have told you; but cause another great disease from the roots that remain, or from the limb that is broken, as we have often seen; and when the flesh is gone, wash the wound with wine or vinegar and oil; and if it comes to that, use powdered vitriol; if that does not work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments, so that they may remain silent at first, shall be long pointed and broad-handed, so that they do not double in number when you draw the tooth; and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And be of great size if they do not bend when drawing, and be of fine iron well made, and be toothed so that they may hold firmly.</start_of_turn>
de la racine des dens	of the root of the tooth.</start_of_turn>
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre .i. jor ou ij., tant que li leus soit amolis, puis i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	When the root is drawn out, if you must put in the moist cotton ball in the hole. That is to say, as much as it is softened, then withdraw the forceps that are named “algefri”, so that the head of the tooth seems like a beak of a bird; and be made as with a file and this is the shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	If the roots do not suffice to hold all these tensions, if you must uncover the marrow throughout the root, and put in the instrument which is called "althali", namely a palatine, for this is its form.
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And be strong and large if it does not break me, and if the root jumps by this, that is good; if not, if you support all the instruments, for in this way the shapes will come after:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you use this instrument which has two rains, for this is its form
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	And other instruments which are before the teeth, and this instrument which appears like a great clamp, of which this is the shape:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	Or other instruments which are before the teeth, and this instrument which appears like a great clamp, of which this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	Or other instruments which are before the teeth, and this instrument which appears like a great clamp, of which this is the form:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When a tooth appears irregularly, its form is unsightly, even in women of gentle character, if it is known that it will not emerge fully from its socket and is not properly aligned, it should be extracted. If it is affected with the tooth, take hold of this instrument which has a small beak-like projection, and be careful not to break the bone.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And when the tooth persists in the gums and hands are clasped for a long time due to the duration of the tooth, and because you do not move the others, if it appears, it can be limed, if you are using a file similar to this one which has the same shape.</start_of_turn>
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	It is also like the file which we use for nails; and while gently gripping the tooth and hands for a while, if it does not move as much as it aches, then at the end we can remove all the roughness, so that it is even, so that it does not hurt the tongue or corrupt the speech.</start_of_turn>
quant li dent lochent	When the teeth loosen.
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les .ij. dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a .i. ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper. Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des .ij. dens sains, et des .ij. meus, si com tu vois:	When the teeth loosen, whether by percussion or biting, and the patient cannot press upon what is between them without pain, you shall cure them with restrictive medicines, which is of no avail; if you command them to be restrained with a gold thread, for the silver thread turns green and falls off, but the gold does not move; neither too thick nor too thin, according to the quantity of space between the teeth; and if you see the teeth to be uneven, take hold of the thread and double it between the two front teeth, then put the teeth between the front teeth, if there is one or more, as long as you see it clearly up to the sound tooth on the other side; then repeat the covering up to the part where you began, and strain your hand subtly and clearly, so that it does not move; and either tie the thread to the root of the tooth if it cannot escape. Then close the teeth with the thread and assemble them, and put them back between the sound tooth, and keep them so that they do not touch the tongue; and then leave them so tight as they can remain stable, and if they loosen or the thread breaks, tighten them with another thread; if it should remain and serve their purpose, and that is the form of the teeth and the arrangement of the front teeth, and of the front teeth, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth aches, if you put it back in its place, fresh from fresh, as we have said; and let nothing intervene except what is wise and soothing, and never make the form of a tooth like a bone spur, and put it back in the place where the defect is, and strain it as we have said, and keep it so tight as we have said, for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	De coper lou liien de la lengue.
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder. Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	The tongue hangs limp; sometimes from sleep or natural cause, or by deep wound; and the work is such that you must open the mouth of the patient, and hold his head firm, and keep the tongue still; then grasp the large nerve of the tongue, until the tongue is freed from its abode, and if there is delay or if it does not go, and this is from the healing of the wound, if one lets it remain, and grasp the same; and keep that the incision is not too deep, for the artery which is beside it; and when you have done this, if you lift the pale pink fluid and easily, or cold fluid, and put out the tongue a little, and hold the patient’s hand close, that the tongue does not swell. And if blood comes, if you take out the glass vial broken; and if it does not go away, if you cauterize with the lentiginous cautery, which is good for this; then cure in another way until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see a reddish or black or hard swelling, if the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is abscess; and if it is declining with moisture, if it is spitting out pus, and there is a little spittle, and you deliver from both sides; and if it does not go away from your work, if you put on a broken glass vial until it is stained, then return to your work until you have finished all the work; then lift the pale liquid easily and softly, and cure in other ways until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	From the throat apostemes.
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les .ij. amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer. Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez. Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	From the throat, there sometimes comes blood clots which are called "godath", and these are properly the almonds of the tonsils. And when you cure them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, take care: if these are soft and of little sensation and of a pale color, do not touch them with iron. And if they are red and the root is large, do not touch them with iron, even for the evacuation of blood; but leave them as long as they are painful, and then you will take them out, or they will burst by themselves. And if they are of a pale color and the root is slight, if you have brought the instrument to cover them, but look first if the clot is resting and is appeased. Then make the patient sit in front of the sun, and his arms be at his sides, and cover his mouth and grasp his hands between his, and press the tongue downwards towards the instrument, because this is the form; and let it be of silver or gold like a needle:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	...press the tongue downwards towards the instrument, because this is the form; and let it be of silver or gold like a needle. Can you press the tongue against all this instrument? And you see the clot, take the sponge and hold it in the almond, and pull it out forcefully more than you wish; and do not take hold of any of the cloths with your hand, then close the instrument against the instrument, because this is the form, that seems like a force; and all the time the head is bent, and one place the other, and is very painful, and is made of iron or tin.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, if you have only a pair of tongs, know that this is the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And if you do not have this instrument present, if you have only a pair of tongs, know that this is the form: grasp one of the nipples with one tong, and the other with the other hand; and when you have grasped one nipple, grasp the other in the same way, and then make an incision and gargle the patient with hot water, hot and easy, and when blood appears, if you gargle the patient with hot water, or wash out grapes or millet, or similar things, until the wound is washed clean; then close the wound when it is healed. And never again will there be any other abscess in the throat except for the two nipples, if you grasp them just as you grasped the two nipples originally.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir .i. aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi .i. jor ou .ij. Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis .ij. rains par les .ij. pertuis dou neis. Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un .i. oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that was in her throat, namely a small abscess; and she could neither breathe through the passage that was blocked, nor eat or drink, and died because of it. And the abscess was so high that it had forced out two grains through the two holes that were blocked. I therefore put one finger in one hole and the other finger in the other hole, and when I had put one finger in, I closed the other hole and put in a great deal of pressure; then I put the other finger back in the other hole that was blocked, and I closed the mouth and pressed the tongue; then I put the ointment in these abscesses, and I squeezed out a part, and only a little blood came out; and when I had squeezed out the blood, I removed the obstruction from the throat and she could now drink water and wine, and she stopped spitting blood for a long time; and the abscess gradually reappeared, filling the cavity that I had evacuated, until it became large; so I bound it and cauterized it inside the throat: the abscess closed steadily; and I left these parts, and only God knows what happened to her afterwards.
de l’uve	De l’uve.
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve». Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li. Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide. Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a .i. des .ij. estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres. Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor. Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague. Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	From the navel.
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And take either a bandage or hold the medicine, as with the nails of a spoon, and put the instrument on all the medicine on the navel; and the patient should remain calm on his chest, so that he salivates and the mucus drips from his mouth onto the medicine, if it does not reach the throat and the spasm; then keep your hand on all the medicine and press it on the navel, for the amount of half an hour, until you see it is limp and the bites of the medicine are appeased; and if you see that, take hold and cover it with any instrument, and moisten the bandage in the medicine, and hold the instrument at full length over the cotton in the navel, until the cotton has dried on the navel; and do this often, until the cautery is perfect, then leave it to dry, and cut off after three or five days. And if you have to restart the cautery of the medicine, if you restart it, and after the cautery wipe around the navel with cotton wool, and pack it in butter, and bandage what is around the medicine; and be raised from cold water, and be cured of hiccups until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This treatment is safer than incision, for the cautery; if it is cured by fumigation as described in this manner, take alum, isop, origanum, rue, chamomile, avron, and similar herbs, and assemble all of them together in one pot, and put them in, and boil; and the pot should be well sealed with strong earth, and in the middle of the pot there should be one instrument that chews as described in this manner.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut. Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And be it of silver or of gold, or one of the cheeks is beaten into the patient’s mouth until the vapor rises to the eye by the scent, until the eye is mortified; after that it must be repeated often, until the eye dries, and keep that you do not do this at the beginning of the outbreak of the fiery cautery, for many things happen; and do not do this except at the decline of the fiery cautery. And if this instrument is not present, take a sponge and put into the mouth of the patient a chick of egg, so that the patient’s mouth does not get too hot; for the chick of egg does not make the vapor grow over the mouth, and that is a good cure altogether.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times it has been seen at the throat bone or thorn of fish, or no thing; so it is therefore necessary that you prove this that you see, and press the tongue to the sun with all the instrument, so that you see the thing; and that which does not appear to you and is returned to the throat, prove that you make the patient vomit the ailment while the meat is cooked in the stomach; for by chance if it is ejected by vomiting; or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a lettuce root, or a piece of dry bread; and that you tie the sponge with one thread, and then transfix it; and when it comes back, if it has been ejected, then draw it out again; and if it does not come out of this that we have said, take one instrument of sponge as described above:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instrument curve at the head if it can enter more easily through the throat, with the head raised up; and guard that you do not touch the epiglottis, for all will pass over it, do not push the bone inwards; and must it be known that the patient has held the instrument, for it is either that the thing is loose or that it is crooked; if the tongue swells, or if it is forced with all the instrument equally, as much as it is forced.
de la sansue de la gorge	And let the instrument curve at the head if it can enter more easily through the throat, with the head raised up; and guard that you do not touch the epiglottis, for all will pass over it, do not push the bone inwards; and must it be known that the patient has held the instrument, for it is either that the thing is loose or that it is crooked; if the tongue swells, or if it is forced with all the instrument equally, as much as it is forced. From the absence of the throat.
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit. Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout .i. petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu. Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine .i. fer chaut, et fai ce sovent. Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor. puis pren plein .i. voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Never is medicine good for this without medicine; as I have said in the division, by the treatment of medicines; and when this does not help, then look in the throat of the patient to the sun, then press the tongue to the instrument that I have told you of. And if you see the absence, if the tongue swells to the instrument, or if there are soft clamps that are worth as much. And if this is not worth it, if take a barley corn, and put it in the throat of the patient, then withdraw or bite the barley corn; and do this often. And if the patient has acute pain, then take a full look at cold water, and cover the mouth and the throat, and let the patient swallow frequently; and if he feels the absence, spit.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier. Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes .i. pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And if she does not subside as we have said, if you fumigate the patient with asafoetida, with the instrument mentioned in the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, for it will make sense. And the method of fumigation is that you take one pot or there are charcoals visible, and let the pot or charcoals be covered with a gauze perceptible in the middle, and in that hole put the head of the instrument; then pour the fumigation, and the patient puts the chief of the cane in his mouth, closes his mouth, so that the smoke does not escape, but comes out only through the nose; and the nose will now be clear, and if it does not subside, repeat the fumigation many times; and the patient will suffer thirst, and will eat dirty and foul things, and will not drink water; and then he will surely vomit due to this government.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument, as we have mentioned, is like tongs with corbels to enter the throat; and it looks like a beak of a sparrow, and has the roughness of lime, so that whatever it grasps, it cannot let go; and thus is the form:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapter on abscesses.
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en .ij. manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor. Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors. car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en .ij. manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor. de squinance	When the limb has been restored and is stable, and all other parts are in their proper place, and there is no longer any swelling or pain, and the wound is not draining properly, then it is necessary to reduce the swelling and pain by applying counter-pressure. Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division the signs of a boil, and how it should be treated with medicines, and how it should be avoided; and we say that a boil swells in the marrow, and has great caution in its cure, and that the old men say that when a boil is in the bone or can be pulled out like a boil that is in marrow, and in the flesh, and similar things, and that it must be removed when it is in its beginning; and when it is great and old, if you do not approach it, for I do not know that it can be cured; nor has anyone ever cured it before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when it is in the bone or can be pulled out, as we have said, purge no more times the black bile; then make it healthy if there is obvious repletion; then remove the bile. That is to say, give a good drink of liquid to make the work; then draw out your ointments or boil, and the head of all parts, and the bone of all parts around nothing to leave; and let the blood flow freely, and expect well the limb with your hand or with anything, and if it comes out contrary to the incision of the artery or vein, if you cauterize as much as you can without it being stained; then cure it of another cure until it is healed.
de ydropisie	De ydropisie.
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces .ij. semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation. We have said above concerning the signs of dropsy, and that when the collection of water is made, and the signs of swelling resemble those of a hernia, and the cure effected by medicine, and that which is effected by iron: if only the fever is alight; and one must not touch iron in these two signs: that is to say, tympanites and hydrothorax, for it is a deadly thing; therefore when medicines show this sign of dropsy which is called "fever" of medicines, and the cure does not benefit, if you see the patient is weak, or if there is another disease besides dropsy, as in most cases and solution of the belly and similar things; if you do not touch iron, for there is doubt; and if you see the patient is of great strength, and has only dropsy, and is neither too young nor too old, then you must operate.
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme: Et soit trenchans de .ij. pars. a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	Believe the patient right on your hands, and press the abdomen downwards pressing the liquid to the lowest part of the belly, then take the spinous process according to this form: And let it be cut through three parts at the point, and do not let it be so deep that it can come up to the intestines when it is grasped.
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude .iij. dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude .iij. dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	Then look if the dropsy is confined to the intestines: if you make an incision two fingers’ breadth to the right of the navel; and if the dropsy is caused by liver disease, make your incision to the left of the navel; and if it is caused by bile, make your incision to the right, and do not allow the patient to rise from the incision except for the essential need.
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme: Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz .i. petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, .iij. pertus; et .ij. d’autre part, et .i. d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	Then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and grasp the gut, and keep your hand over the entire area between the skin and the muscle as if guiding the quantity of a nail or an anchor; then pierce the muscle until the area of the gut comes out, and that is the cause of the pain, then draw out the instrument, and there is the shape: It is similar to a silver nail, and is of spider or spider’s leg, and has at the end a small hole; and where it costs once, twice, or three times on one side, and three times on the other, and the nail is cut as if with a penknife, and that is the shape of the incision that the writers make with the penknife:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	At the top of all this is the wound, so that when the instrument comes to the pain, if you immediately put your hand over the instrument; evacuate half or a third of the wound, for if you evacuate more than that in this hour, by chance the patient will die from the resolution of his spirit from the wound, or he will bleed, or he will approach death;
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	But in an empty state, according to the quantity of its virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the virtue to the patient signify, and his pains; then take the instrument and hold the water, and it is retained now by the hook which is stamping the part which is above the socket, as I have said; that you pierce according to this manner. Then repeat the instrument the other way, if you see the patient suffering this, and take out a small quantity of water.
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue. Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	Do nothing more, and keep using it until it no longer stays put. If you doubt the patient, and you give him too much water, if the physician of the burial or sand burn, and by giving him to drink, sweat or bathe in the sun, and abstain from drinking; and let the physician of drying medicines remain until he is healed, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of the water, as I have said before
de l’estopement de la verge	of the belly of the maiden.
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu. Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout .i. spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme: puis met ou pertus .i. clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi .iij. jors ou iiij. et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Never were children born without a mark on the belly, or the mark was small, or it was not in its place. If the physician suspects that there is no mark at all, notwithstanding that there should be, according to this fashion: then let him put or make a mark, that is, a mole of pigment, and bind it and keep it for two or three days. And when he wants to urinate, let him keep the mark closed, urinate, and then restore it; for by chance it will not be closed, because the urine that comes out will not leave it closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera. Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	If the mark is small, if it is medicine with a mole of pigment, as we have said, and it swells. Those who do not have the mark in its place are pale, for no one is born with the mark at the head of the belly, for they cannot urinate before lifting up their belly; and they cannot restrain themselves for that matter because the matter does not reach the navel, and this is an evil disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the way of the work is that if the patient lies supine on his back, with the head of the shoulder and the scapula as wide as a thumb, if the mark pricks in the middle, as it should; and you keep from discharge of blood which comes many times, and if it comes, if the stain of this blood which stains blood, and cure the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	Des pustules de la verge
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times come these boils to the groin, and are an appearance of foul matter; and in them are malign and non-malign; if you take them at once [with a sharp instrument], one should anoint subtly, and cut and drain them all, then put on Egyptian lint; then cure with diafinicon until they are healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere. Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer. And if the boil is malignant, with pus and discharging, if you must bring a cautery. Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme: Li cauteres si aide as .ij. dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a .i. estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars;	And if discharge of blood comes, if you wish to use the lunar cautery, do so in this fashion: The cautery will aid in these three things together: at the discharge of blood, and at corruption; and if the root of the limb is corrupted and withdrawn, if you bite or draw out the root a bundle of hair, and make the patient urinate among; and when the hair has emerged at the head of the limb which has not been circumcised, or there is wound or incision, if you wish, then you must burn it with the cautery until the ligaments are loosened and the root of the limb is freed from all parts.
et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a .i. spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre .ij., et i met .i. subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	If it is a grievous thing to divide this, if you wish, you must burn it with the cautery at the root of the limb and the head of the limb; then carefully separate between the two, and put in between a soft bandage of wet linen with cold water, so that it does not move again.</start_of_turn>
de la circoncision	from the circumcision.</start_of_turn>
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not merely a continuation of the other wounds; however, when we perform this work of our own will, and do it properly, if we are careful, it is the best work and the lightest to health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not teach us circumcision, for they did not use it in their law, and we have learned only what we have learned through experience
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have seen the greatest part of masters and physicians who performed circumcision in this way: with force and with a new instrument; but if the testicles escaped, because there were two layers, and by chance if we cut through these and left out that below.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Or the wound covers itself again, and there is double pain, and with the support which is too slight to secure the end of the limb; and by the support of the nail by chance escapes the thread, and straightens the work, and many times it is born again until it has no need of support and I want it.</start_of_turn>
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en .i. tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	For when you press your hand, if you hold it equally from all sides in.i. all tension; but if the thread be well twisted around the leather; and if the manner of the first work be such that you make the child think, if he understands, that you do not make him endure more than to bind the thread around the limb just so much, and then let it go in all the ways that you can.</start_of_turn
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz .i. poc a .i. autre liien; et la tien as .ij. dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les .ij. liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	Then grasp your hands straight out, and restore the forces between your hands or withdraw your fingers so that the fetus does not see them, not any of the instruments; then place your hand at the root of the navel and breathe in or out, and pull up as much as the head of the fetus is in; then thoroughly mix in the ordure that is gathered, then tie the navel cord with a double thread, then tie the other end with another thread; and hold the two threads together by the second loop and the index finger, and press between the two threads, then release the index finger and pull the head of the navel cord down gently.
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre .i. drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then let the blood flow back in and out, for that is the medicine; and put powder on and over the powder put a greasy cloth glued with a sponge soaked in rosewater, confirmed with rosemary oil and balsam, and leave it on until the other side is healed, and treat it with another dressing until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the forces at the wound is like this: the two fingers should be tense and firm, and the fingers should be as great as the thumb equally:
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The wound of civilization is when the cord of urine escapes at the incision; therefore it is necessary that you extend it to your nail, even though it makes an incision; and keep it even, and if you do not keep it held to your nail, if you let go, and then take hold again.

dou retenement de l’urine	The retention of urine.
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	The retention of urine is caused by the obstruction of the stone, or of blood congealed, or of a tumor, or of worms, or similar things, which we mentioned in the previous section.
et se li urine n’est desliie, et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	and if the urine does not flow freely, and you see that the retention is caused by the stone which is in the bladder or at the neck of the bladder, then you must make the patient sit upright on his knees; place the hand pieces on the back, and extend the patient’s abdomen from the part under the loin, and restrain the patient so that he does not move as much as possible; and then press the neck of the bladder towards the expression of the stone at the top, so that the urine is released.
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	and if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you must administer extraction with all the instruments which are called “syringes,” which are made like this: either of pure silver with a leg that is slightly curved downwards, like the beak of a bird; or of fine steel, or of silver with a head.
