puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	Then put the catheter firmly into the bladder until it reaches the root of the bladder; then double the bladder downwards towards the buttock; then drain the bladder before it reaches the bladder, and feel the patient urinate until it is empty; this must not be done except in this order for it is dangerous; then withdraw the catheter gradually, and the urine will follow the catheter, and remove the catheter when it is done, and correct the urine.
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	and restart the catheter until the bladder is empty, and align the patient.
des maladies de la vessie	Des maladies de la vessie.
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When urine or blood comes into the bladder, or if pus is accumulated, and you see urine and medicine distilling, if you do everything that is called the “clepsedre,” which is its shape:
Elle est close, et si a .iij. pertus: .ij. d’une part, et .i. d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	It is closed, and if it is ruptured: half from one side and half from the other, as you see; and it should be grasped by the edge so that the medicine be as thick as possible, in order to drive out the moisture, and push as much as possible.
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	And when you see your medicines going into the bladder, put the chief of the catheter into the moisture, and draw out the urine that is inside; if you draw out the moisture at the catheter, and then push strongly the catheter inside; if the moisture enters inside, and comes to the bladder now, if the patient feels it
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	And this is the form of a subtle blister from which we will clip the bladder: if this is the case:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a .i. sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les .ij. seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe .i. poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie;	And this is the form of a subtle blister from which we will clip the bladder: if this is the case:
et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai .i. cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute .i. fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble .i. dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie. de la piere	From the stone.
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already spoken in this division about the methods of dealing with stones, and their extraction with medicine; and I have mentioned the difference between a stone that is incarcerated like urine and all the signs, and in what case a stone must be opened of a certain size; and in the bladder, and in the kidney; and I will tell you openly and concisely about it.</start_of_turn>
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that a stone that is incarcerated in the bladder often causes vomiting, which is a sign that the stone is pressing on the bladder almost as much as in its entirety; and there is frequent vomiting, gravel in the urine, pain in the side, and many times the patient is unable to urinate, and then becomes constipated; and from these vomiting attacks the foundations are loosened.  The cure for these vomiting attacks is more gentle in young people than in old people, and is more effective in those between youth and old age; and the cure for those who have a large stone is more gentle than for those who have a small one.</start_of_turn
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines. Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	And when we come to the treatment, if it is necessary first to cleanse the patient by vomiting, in order to drive out all the poison that is in the intestines. For it never hinders to inquire about the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche ded ens;	Then take the patient by the limbs, and loosen and move towards the belly, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and does not remain at any high point; then make him sit between your hands which are clasped together, and his hands rest on his thighs, so that the bladder is completely relaxed downwards; then inquire and feel inside.</start_of_turn>
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere. Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	If you feel the stone in the space, if you hasten now to touch upon the stone. And if it does not prick when you touch it all around, if you think the patient is pregnant, take your left index finger, if the patient is an adult woman, or your middle finger, if the patient is a young man complete; and push downwards to the bottom of the stone, and inquire the stone, and when you feel it on your finger, if the bladder is full at the neck; then press upon your finger, and the stone will come out or you will see it retreat.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend with his right hand the intestines upwards, and with his left hand to grasp the skin that is between the intestines in the part where the size is made; then insert the spatula covering the shape:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	And command the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend with his right hand the intestines upwards, and with his left hand to grasp the skin that is between the intestines in the part where the size is made; then insert the spatula covering the shape: and be between the intestines and the foundation, do not go into the middle but along the left side; and be two above the bone, and two either adhered or foundation, and be the size through if it be wide by going over, and within narrow, according to the quantity of the stone, do not go too large.
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	and by chance press if two bones which are or foundation, that they leap forth in the work; and the threads that are part of the bone or that are angled, and margins: if it is grasped to irritate; and if there is part that is sweating, similar to a gland, round, from which issue is slight.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li .i. estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge .i. poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	If there are angles or margins, make the size larger; and if it does not slip, know that you must grasp the nails which are as sharp as a lime at the tip, for it must grasp the stone if it does not escape; or you may pour water on it. A curved instrument with a blunt tip should be used for this purpose, and if you do not manage to engage it, it will be too wide. If it slips without restraint, it is like straining vitriol.
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors. Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie. Car .ij. choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	If there are more than one stone, grasp the largest at the belly of the bladder first, then hold, and pull the others afterwards if there are any. And if the belly is large, if you hold it with silk, make the wound larger. For in these things two things happen to the patient: either he dies, or the urine comes out alongside the blood, which cannot be bound up; but whatever you do, try to drain, or remove the nails, until you have separated it piece by piece
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus .i. drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	When you have completed your work, apply incense, aloe and dragon's blood to the wound, and hold it in place. Then put upon it a moist cloth soaked in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water, to soothe the burn; then raise the patient up to his collar and do not loosen the bandage until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you loosen it, if there arises much blood from the wound of oil and water, then treat with the salve of Dijon and balsam, as long as it is sane.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	And if pus comes out of the wound and corrupts, and swelling of blood in the bladder, and either by this the urine is retained, which is known in part as without jumping with the urine: then withdraw your hand from the wound, and drain that blood, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder and bring it about

Then lift the wound of water and easily and gently and bind it, and give him every possible aid, as long as it is sane; and be sure that all the times you treat it, that you bind the edges together, and assemble the medicines above the limb.

Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take one loop of wire according to this shape and be at a right angle with two loops fixed in one space.</start_of_turn>
puis pren .i. fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge. Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	Then take one thread and loop it around the base of the stone, so that it cannot come back into the bladder; then tighten the loop lightly around the stone, until it reaches the stone; and turn the loop back and forth in the stone as much as you can until you can pierce the stone from the other side; if the urine comes out then press your hand on what is remaining of the stone that is in the bladder. If it breaks, and spurts with the urine, and is stained with blood;
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie .i. fil desoz la piere et .i. autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les .ij. liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez. de la piere des femmes	If you are unable to do this, take hold of the limb at the bone and another above, then insert the thumb between the two joints, and grasp firmly, withdraw the thumb and loosen the limb, and congeal the blood which is in the wound; then cure as before.
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	If there is only one bone in the limb, which is the thumb, and if it is dislocated, if there is no other dislocation, it is a grievous cure, and is defended by two things: the first is that in this case the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a woman who knows how to manage a household, even though she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a.	And the third method, if by chance one cannot find a woman who knows this art of hands; and the fourth method, if the woman’s stone is more prominent than the man’s, for in that case one can make a deeper size, and greater fear has it.
Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier .i. caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	And if this is necessary, if you can take a maiden who knows it well, and prick the root firmly, and if you cannot find one, no matter. Take whatever humble maid there is; and present a woman who is wise in life, or a woman who knows some part of the art, and command her to do what you command with the inquiry of the stone.
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	and see well if the woman is a virgin: then you must press her breast or foundation and inquire the stone; and if she finds it, if you constrain her from below her breast, and command her to hold her hand left on her belly, and push and press her hand gently.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	If it be true, if you must move it from groin to groin from the entrance of the bladder until it reaches the root of the thigh; then place your thumb on the bone at the root of the thigh where it is usually hidden, and feel the bone in that place; and do not move it above the bone or below, and let the size be small at first.
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains. si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	Then tighten the thumb to the size you wish, if you feel the bone is too deep in the wound until the bone can rest firmly, and that many different kinds of stones are: that is to say, small and large, sharp and blunt, long and round, and which have round corners. If the stones resemble each other, it is likely that they are discharged.</start_of_turn>
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	And if it does not go away, if you put at the limb a bruised vitriol, and hold it for an hour until it is dry; then return to your work, until the bone is firm, and have the instruments that I have mentioned in the extraction of the stone are at your home to help you in your work.</start_of_turn>
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	If he does not move from there, it is the artery that is cut. Put powder on the wound and strain it with needles and thread, and do not attempt to move it again, but leave the wound and do not touch it, except by chance the patient dies; then cure the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	When the chill of blood has subsided and the limb has bled, if you return to your work while the wound is still open, until the bone is firm.</start_of_turn>
de hernie carnouse	of hernia of the belly.
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Ramice aquouse is nothing else but an assembly of moisture or white mucus, which is as dense as the seeds of coriander, that contains the egg; and it is called "syfac", and never is it truly in the yolk of the egg, if we take care that this is not the case; and it is the skin of the seed between the white mucus that we have mentioned.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this seed is from weakness and comes from the seeds, and it is spread throughout that matter
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	And never does it come from percussion on the seeds, and this mucus has many colors: or it is pale yellow, or it is without red, or black, or pale blue, and there is more
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, .i. poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And these are the signs of impending collapse of this assembly, for if it is pale and white as we have said, if the abscess is round like a bow and does not open, because it is filled with moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	And if there is moisture in the flesh itself, if the abscess is round with a part of the egg, and for this reason it is thought that it is another egg;
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if the moisture is between the skin of the limbs and the white part, if you feel it well; then when you see the color of the moisture, if it extends to the whole circumference, from this it is known
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to this, therefore, that which comes after the introducer, judge of that which is within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz;	And when we bind them with iron, if it is judged that the patient is well according to the sum of his power and the swelling of his body; then we bind them upon his back, upon something a little high, and put a cloth over his face;
puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des .ij. costelz dou keur des coions;	then we sit on his left side, and command the minister to sit on his right side, and extend the limb to one of his ribs as far as the joints of the ribs;
puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir;	then take the sponge wet, and sew the skin of the ribs among them as far as the loin of the loin, and make your incision straight by dividing the skin of the ribs until you reach the white marrow, and scorch it sparingly as desired.
puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a .i. large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	Then pierce the face deeply with a large hole, and drain out all the water, and then put on your gloves, and extend the face upwards; and do not touch the nails of the toes, but only the face itself; cut through everything or in pieces immediately the cost of his marrow, for if you do not cut it well it will return the water.
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les .ij. leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the urine spurts forth from your work, if you leave it in its place when you have finished the work of the face; then join together again the joints of the toes to their natural position, and cure it as you would any other wound, until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the urine corrupted by another disease, if you must tie up the vessels that are suspended, doubting the decay of blood; then cut the limb throughout the suspension, drain the urine, and cure it as we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et se aigue est assemblee en .ij. parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont .ij. ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	And if it is acute, it is composed of three parts assembled together, with six roots; if one part is cut as the first one was made even, then wipe the blood, and put lint soaked in rose oil in the wound.
et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les .ij. coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	put on the other lint soaked in wine and oil, and put on the six nails, and put on doubled bandages, and bind all around according to this shape:
Puis pren .ij. drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les .ij. angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier;	Then take two bandages, and use coarse wool according to this semblance and assemble them with stitching in the armpit, and one of the nails grasps on the foundation up to the back, and the other at the part of the armpit; and the other two at the two angles, and be everything assembled so that the restriction is in the loop of the armpit.
et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes .i. cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers;	And never is this branch of cautery sufficient in size for iron, and only take one cautery of the culter type, and grasp the hair of the nails, and if necessary eschew as we have said, so that the white substance which contains the liquid is discovered.
si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	If you take the cautery as we have said, and pierce that membrane as we have shown, and burn with this subtle cautery:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille;	And grasp in every way that you wish, until you have cauterized all; and keep the fire from touching the egg; and remove that egg when this work is finished; and keep blood from draining, and keep moving that it does not dry out.
et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	If nothing else hinders you, or an abscess bursts or blood flows from a wound, or any other adversity, if it is possible, remedy that which hinders you, as has been previously said.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai,	If the patient is fearful and does not wish to undergo this work due to its horror, if you suspect perforation, as I have said, and are certain beyond doubt by the significations we have mentioned that the aquous humor is limpid,
si fai seoir le malaide sus .i. siege leveit; puis perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer;	If you make the patient sit in a comfortable position; then pierce the abscess at the lower part with all the surrounding fat; and make the perforation deep enough so that all the pain is expelled
puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee;	Then put on cotton on the limb, and bind it, and leave only the remaining pain to flow; then cure it until the wound is healed.
et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge .i. poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés .vj. mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	If the white cloth does not stop the pain at the edge of the wound, if you must, drink a spoonful or the instrument used to treat the pain of hydrophobia; for in this case the form is as aforesaid; and enlarge it, that is to say, loosen the wound, and drain the wound until it is healed, and when it is healed as before, and when it is put together like before, the patient will be well again.

et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars;	and can easily make the size above this semblance, and on the other limbs;

et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If it is exposed at the surface, or within the vessels, you must deliver all that is tense, and the wound must be rounded off.

de la routure dou syfac	then they are dry and do not require aid.

des hermofrodites	of hermaphrodites.

de la tentigene	Hermaphroditism is according to two methods: one if between the two testes opens as with the figure of a woman, or if there is hair, and sometimes in the urine it flows out. And the other method if in women, and has on the navel as with a beard and two testes. And the cure of the spleen and envy if it is that you cut out all the fatty parts; and it is cured like other wounds. In the second method, of men whose urine spurts through the skin of the testes, if there is no other cure.
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure. Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee». Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Tentigene is a fatty growth on the natural part, as long as it is too lazy to see; and many women have it as much as a hand. And the cure is that you hold the excess of the tentativeness at your hand or wrist, and grasp it lightly; and do not be too rough, for blood does not come from there, then it is cured by other cures as long as it is healthy; and there is another burden that comes from the mouth of the marrow, and the spleen, and by chance spurts out, and is according to the likeness of a cow, and for this reason it is called the ancient "cowardly disease". If you can grasp that, as we have said, and cure it while it is healthy
de erratique	De erratique.
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile. Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait. S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as .ij. leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes .ij. dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les .ij. leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder. Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte. Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.  Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez. Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	When something is out of its proper place. When the nature of a woman is not rightly perceived, or if the birth is small; this is by nature, or by disease that comes from it; or by injury from a foreign object, or from a wound or swelling, and is made worse by moisture, or in the armpits, or the breasts, or the belly, or the feet; and if the knowledge of this is from the regard of the dance. If the swelling is close to the genitals, if there are two thumbs or at the root. If it is from a swelling in the armpits, and it is close to the testicles, if you are in a hurry, and the testicles are turned inside out: put your two thumbs together, and let the woman be on her back, spreading out her legs; then the testicles will form, as long as the swelling in the armpit is round, and is over the swelling. Then take oil, and pour it on the wound, and put it on the place, and keep the woman still at home. And if the swelling is hard and thick, if you can do no more than cover it with the thumb resembling a holly leaf. If the swelling comes from a wound, if you can cover it up according to this manner, except for an embolism. For an embolism that is in the belly must not be touched with fire.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids.
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation. Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer. Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer. Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai .i. emplaustre sus son dos. Et se il estainche, c’est boin. Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.  Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a .i. chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Emorroids are tears in veins which do not usually heal without treatment; and when they are old they become black. We have already mentioned the signs and symptoms of such ailments, and I will now tell you of those which resolve the cure. I say that emorroids and blackheads, when pressed into the marrow, are not felt, except by the physician. It is therefore necessary that you put the woman in a cold house, then stretch the blackhead and press it into its roots, then sprinkle on medicines which restrain blood, such as alum and dragons blood and incense, and the like; then leave it for an hour, then put it in cold water; and if there is still blood, let her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate seeds and barley and the like, then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and cheese, and make a plaster of it. And if it swells, that is good. If not, make her vomit at the back and give her vinegar with wine vinegar, and make her vomit. And when the abscess rests, if it has cured the limb of its swelling as long as it is sane; and the one which is called "albathir" is red, and is like a rough beard, if you cover it as I have said the blackhead. And then it will heal as long as it is sane.

Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division. Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.  Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege, et ait .ij. petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument. Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés .ij. jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.  Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division. de l’enfantement	From infancy.
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment. Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	From infancy. The midwife is first at the delivery when she knows the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs are when you see the woman press down below and desire to smell the head: then the child is eager to be born; then his head and shoulders are in their natural position, and the issue is soon after his head, and he follows with his tail; and when you see these signs, if you press lightly on his belly, if the child comes out head first, it is well born; for when he comes down on his head, if he follows with his tail, and the mother has borne his superfluities by natural birth; and this is not otherwise. For it does not come at any time from his feet, nor from his limbs or hands, or from his belly or buttocks, but from an accident from his collar and from other harmful figures; if the midwife is at the delivery that she is wise and discreet in these matters, and she avoids error and deception, and I will show you all the figures in which we must help her.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	When the child comes down naturally on his head and the woman gives birth groans, and her strength is weak, if you make her sit on a chair, or the women hold her; and as soon as her nature is overcome with oil or rue or fennel, which is customary, then lie down between her thighs the little cushion from which this is made:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.Et se les .ij. mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus .i. siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	Et fende la secondeine, et cope à son unguile tant que li moistors qui est en-dessus fuers; et preint le ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisteriser la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai prendre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son nez une heure: si istra maintenant l’enfes. de l’enfant mort	De l’enfant mort.

Then take your hand and apply it to all the instruments, as if you had previously held them equally, according to the quantity that you see opening the mouth of the mare, until she makes what she wants.

These instruments are all messy, and their appearance is multiplied; and when you see them appear, the work is done more quickly, and the higher the houses are for their quantity.</start_of_turn>

Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis;	When the secondine is retained at birth, if you command the patient to retain its alaine, and then make her vomit with force, and hold your hands to the mouth and nose;

de la fistule dou fondement	of fistula from the bowels
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des .ij. parties,	Fistules that arise from the bone are nodulation, and those that arise from below the bone deviate or are displaced in the space of the two parts.
si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe,	if there is one fistula or several; and when that nodulation is old, if it persists, and is accompanied by moisture that softens white or yellow bile,
et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	and never are these fistulas permanent; and they are known by the fact that they cause vomiting or diarrhea when the patient vomits, and by chance when some of them go away.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe. Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant:	And thus we know of the fistula that persists at the foundation and does not go away:
et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus we know of the fistula that persists at the foundation and does not go away: that you bite your thumb or the foundation and insert a subtle needle or iron hook into the fistula when there is no swelling.

saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	The hairs that they do not pierce through; if you are in a hurry to cure.

des emorroydes	Des emorroydes.

et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	Or you cauterize them as it is said or as the fire cautery chapister, and then treat them with other cures while they are well; and if the foundation cannot be moved, if you clench the patient’s biting and grasping hand, do so until it can move freely.
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	You cannot prevent the patient from suffering, and if the limb is fixed to the foundation, if it is a slight cure;
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	and that you take hold of his nail or grasp it, and press them, and then cure as we have said, while he is well, and that he avoids the incision by fire.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren .i. fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les .ij. chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille,	If you are certain that you have restored the dislocation in this manner: take one thread and pierce it with a needle, then pass the thread downwards and withdraw the needle from the other side. Then pass two threads through the eye of the needle.
et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse .i. por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	If it is broad; then hold the thread taut, and pass the needle, and knot the thread, and draw out the needle, and do this with all of them. Leave one to correct the excess of blood
puis met sus le fondement .i. drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	Then put upon the foundation one moist bandage in rose oil or cerate, and put upon the foundation, and command the patient to rest;
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then leave it until it shrinks, and when it does, if the treatment of oil and other remedies is applied while it is still healthy.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	when it is dry of fire or foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is drying of the bowels by the intestines, and by constriction of nature, and when the disease is old and medicine is of no avail.

dou fremit	immediately.
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Formice is a small appearance which appears before the limb, and goes out from under the skin; and never does it cause pain, and it is felt as if death were imminent, and comes throughout the limb, and more so than in any other part.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the cure for it is that you take a bundle of rue from a goosefoot, or a bundle of rue from a strong vulture, and put that salve on the wound, until the circle turns blue all around the wound
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	then turn your hand all the way around until you reach the bottom of the wound, and put it out from under, and scrape the wound from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if thou seest, if thou do this of a wasp or of iron in this fashion, and be silent and restrain thy hands:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	And if thou seest, if thou do this of a wasp or of iron in this fashion, and be silent and restrain thy hands, do not perceive, for it must hold still, and press and if thou seest, if thou cauterize the edge, if it is before or alongside the cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	and be silent and restrain thy hands, do not perceive, for it must hold still, and press and if thou seest, if thou cauterize the edge, if it is before or alongside the cautery.

Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those who are feeble and painful in the treatment of children are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	Their limbs are small and large if they are too wide, or their belly is tied up in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez .ij. pertus, et en l’autre .i.;	and if their side is pierced or broken on one side and on the other; or if their rib is pierced or broken, and one of the ribs is fractured or broken on one side and the other on the other side.

et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And when the medicine is inside, if the thread has in front of it a strong thread, then clip; and this is the form of a circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	And let the medicine neither too hot nor too cold, and join the top of the clip with oil or ointment of egg, or something similar, then bind it lightly;
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses .ij. mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit,	Then grasp the patient with his two hands together, until it is seen through, then withdraw the clip, and let the patient rest his legs at the edge,
et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	If the physician sees that the limb is stiff, if he can stretch it as much as he can; and if he sleeps throughout the night, it is a greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	If he limps with a disease of swelling of the belly, and the physician hasten to leave, if he returns as long as he is well.</start_of_turn>

des plaies	wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already mentioned the treatment of wounds in the previous section; or you may say the treatment of hands and medicine, according to their completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse depending on how they are made, and depending on the limbs or wounds that are made, and from what they are made
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things from which wounds are made are by biting of stone, and the size of spear and limb, or of lance or fist or seat, or similar things;
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	Or that they are made according to the custom of the lords, if as wound that pierces on the neck, or on the head, or on the arm, or on the belly, or on the liver, or similar members.
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	Or I will tell you of the cure for a wound, and I will begin with simple head wounds, for the memory will come to you in this chapter.</start_of_turn>
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans,	I say that when a simple wound comes or head wound, and the bone is not broken, if you take care that there is no fracture of bone or other things, and the skin is entirely torn and the wound is great,  </start_of_turn
et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	And you doubt the wound itself: if you do it too soon after the wound, it may come to bleed more from the wound than from the head; or the blood may flow in the opposite direction to the part affected.
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and listen to the patient's swelling of wine and fat foods.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if he does not see improvement, if he is to vomit his food, and does not drink wine, does not eat meat;
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and put out the wound, if it is oozing, cover it with a soft cloth soaked in rose oil only, or in astringent wine;

et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the blood has been moved, put on some ointment, as long as it is healthy.</start_of_turn>

And if the wound is large like the size of a needle and similar, and the lips do not reunite by tension, if you reunite them by stitches, as I will say for wounds of the belly, of stitching.</start_of_turn
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir,	If the wound is uncovered from the bone, and is wide open, and holds only at the edge; then cure the wound with medicine, and restore flesh in place of skin.
et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	And instruct the patient to eat raw flesh, such as testicles and barley, as well as poultry, and similar things.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find or see decay of flesh, and there is no bone exposed, if you grasp it firmly and pull it out, then cure;
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	And if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which cannot be stayed by medicines, if you see the artery, and if you dislocate it, if you bind it with a thread;

Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon .ij. parties; chalz vive .iij. parties, et le poudre subtilment,	The manner of the powder is: take incense one part; dragon's blood two parts; and chalk three parts, and grind them together finely.

Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	Never do we make this treatment solely, when there is neither incense nor blood of a dragon, but only when the wound has not moved.</br

de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	Wound comes from a tear and is simple, if there is no difference between the root and the top of the limb, but if the root or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If the root [of the limb] is not cut, if there is no other injury except to leave the wound open, and do not put anything restrictive, for it is night and makes the wound shrink

dou derrompement dou ventre	dou derrompement du ventre
