se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	If you are in doubt, for this matter is worth attempting.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre,	When the wound is large and is in the lower part of the abdomen,
si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos,	you must consider that you should manage the patient on their back
et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	and raise their legs higher than their head;
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre,	And if it is in the lower part of the belly,
si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz,	and if it is in the lower part of the belly, if you put the head and the heel higher than the lower parts,
et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des .ij. parties	and if it is in the lower part of the belly, and if the rupture of the belly is in one of the two lower parts.
si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	and if it is in the lower part of the belly, if you put the tenture in that which the upper part is higher than the other;
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	And thus it is appropriate to administer what I have said in great and gaping wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet,	Small wounds require what has appeared to you.</start_of_turn>
puis aies entre tes mains .i. ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main,	then hold between your hands, that is to say minister tenderly what holds all the way through.</start_of_turn
et assemble les levres;	and gather the limbs together;
et c’est la maniere commune de costures,	And this is the common method of stitching.
et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie,	and take a needle or several, according to the quantity of the wound's size,
puis laisse des le chief de la plaie .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. boin fil fort;	then leave some space at the edge of the wound, i.e. about the thickness of a nail, and pierce a needle or put in strong thread;
et perce les .ij. chiés dou cuir avec les .ij. chiés dou siphac,	and pierce the leather with the needle through the edges of the wound,
qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie,	Who is soaked in the leather from within, so that when you make a cut in that part,
et assemble les .ij. chief dou siphac les .iiij. ensamble;	and gather together the hair from the armpit, the beard and the hair of the genitals;
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de .ij. pars,	then strain it with a double thread around the needle of two parts,
puis assemble les .ij. chiés de la plaie avenanment,	then gather together the hair of the wound evenly,
et puis laisse .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	Then leave some space there, and insert another hook.
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille,	Then leave some space there, and insert another hook just as you did with the first one.
et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles,	and do the same with the following hooks as you have done with the first one.
tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	until all the wounds are held together;
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses,	And let the nails be blunt between the thumb and the great toe,
car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	for the blunt nails catch all the hair, and the long ones cannot enter properly.
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	therefore it is recommended that they be blunt;
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir,	and must not push the nails too far into the hair and skin,
k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	They do not hold and open the wound before the suture;
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir,	and then hold the head of the nails, so that they do not harm the patient at night.</start_of_turn>
et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir,	and put tents or cloths over the head of the nails to hold them,
et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and leave them until the wound is sutured.</start_of_turn>
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies,	And this manner of stitching with needles is more suitable for small wounds.
car il i soffist une aguille ou .ij.	because there is often a needle or two involved.
Li seconde costure si est commune,	The second suture is often used,
et est que tu assemble les .ij. chiés dou cuir et les .ij. chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait .i. fort fil moien;	and it is that you assemble the hair of the skin and the hair of the flesh together with a needle or there is a strong middle thread;
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz .iiij. ensamble,	And when you have perceived these things altogether,
si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	if you remain calm at the part or where you have begun, in the manner in which it is customary to cause scars.</start_of_turn>
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and put between each stitch the thickness of a lesser bean.</start_of_turn
ceste costure sevent li home,	this stitch will hold the home,
et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre,	And I closed a wound with a sponge that had been in the armpit or the belly,
qui estoit navrez d’un coutel,	which had been cut with a knife.
et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant,	and the wound was more than a palm wide.
et issoit des intestines bien .ij. palmes de grant,	and there were intestines well almost two palms wide,
et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	And it was the wound in the middle of the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit .xxiiij. houres fuer,	And I returned the intestine when it had been out for twenty-three hours.
et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a .xv. jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	And the wound was sutured for fifteen days, and healed, and was well.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the master had judged that he would die, and this was a miracle;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en .i. leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	And do not be afraid of oil, for I am in a place where it is neither found nor used, no medicines.
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel .ij. fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And thus more above the wound I shall apply oil three times a day, and wash it with honey until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Or vos dirai les .ij. propres manieres de cousture:	Or you shall tell me the two ways of dressing:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	Take the needle and pass it from the lower part up to the chest;
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille,	When she has perceived the right shoulder in its place, if the head of the scapula is displaced or twisted or if the needle has pierced her,
et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	and makes her pierce from another side of the inside until it escapes.
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz,	thus you must do just as the cobbler does with the leather when he sews it
et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and that you leave one side of the scapula out once, and take hold of it again from the other side, until the dislocation is completely mended.</start_of_turn>
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement,	The second method of stitching, that Galiens does discreetly,
si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les .ij. parties ensamble naturelment,	if it is as if no one does it, which assemble the members naturally.
et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	and join one of the ends to the other end, in a partial manner:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement,	keep a needle or a splinter nearby, and make a hole only as wide as necessary,
et laisse les .ij. chiés dou syfac;	et laisse les cheveux douce sur le visage;
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens,	then prick at their base, and hold the eyes steady until they grow to this depth.
as .ij. chiés dou syfac;	as the hairs on the face.
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en .ij. autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	then prick at their base, and hold the eyes steady until they grow to this depth, as the hairs on the face that are on the other side of the face;
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	And this is the commonest and most painful mode of cure.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent,	And thus this word is often spoken, and no one testifies to it,
c’on doit coudre le ventre a .ij. aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	we must suture the belly with two needles, or there is thread in the flesh;
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and we must push one needle from one side and the other from the other side, in the manner of those who sew wounds;
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre,	And so that when the rotation is inward toward the belly,
si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	if it is more tender than other parts of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	We judge the wound as being similar to other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee,	and when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, as if it had just happened,
si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char,	If you reset the intestine and the gut; then put on the greasy powder.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	And if the gut has moved, if you put on no other dressing except what is present, until the wound heals
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and hold the gut firm, and be bound to the abdomen, and mix;
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then cure the wound as well as the others, until it is healed.
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel,	And if you have no medicine, if you put it on, as soon as it begins to swell, cotton wool,
et le remue .ij. fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	And if you have no medicine, if you put it on, as soon as it begins to swell, cotton wool,
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For in many cases simple wounds do not require other medicine besides these provisions.
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz,	and if you doubt that the wound will not heal by itself,
si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset,	If you must soak linen cloth in boiling oil, or in rose oil,
et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	put it on the wounds and bandage the abscesses.
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient,	if there is pain or gangrene in the bowels, and it happens many times,
si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	if the clusters of black wine swell and the same gangrene comes up to the intestines;
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	And the spleen and intestines, when they are large, if they are more fluid to heal than the small ones.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez,	The large intestine, which is called the “jaundice,” cannot heal when it is swollen,
et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	because of the swelling of the veins and the lightness of the whole body, and the approach of its nature to nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	If the wound spurts blood, if you reset it backward as the intestine, while it is still fresh;
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne,	And if it is black and turning towards black, it is certain that you must bind the black limb, and do not remove blood, for it does not come.
car il i a voinnes et arteres;	for there are veins and arteries.
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien,	and if there is something between the limb,
et met les .ij. chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	and if the bone breaks through the skin, hold the limb still so that the wound can be aligned when the bone is extracted, and the wound will bow.
de la routure dou boueil	Of the root of the boil.
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite,	When the intestine is round and the wound is small,
si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes,	if it can be restored in its natural place,
por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	because I have seen that a bone has been fractured or the belly of an arrow has been pierced;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac,	And it was the wound on the right side of the stomach.
et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	And it became filled and formed a fistula, and in this there was evacuation and vomiting;
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I put it to cure according to what I could, and I did not cease to relieve it until it was healed, and I bound it up
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw it bound up, I doubted that the patient would be well in his belly;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	And there is no harm, but it remains in many good arrangements, meals and drinks.
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	And they say that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it should be closed in parts slowly:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie,	then take forceps from great tests, and gather the layers of the wound,
et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les .ij. levres,	and when the forceps have opened the mouth, if you put on the two layers,
si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	If her mouth is strained above.
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier,	and then she bites her head, and this lasts if she cannot loosen it.
puis met .i. autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	then put another remedy afterwards like before, until the wound is completely healed;
et cout la plaie.	and bandage the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide,	If the head of the shoulder is dislocated in the intestine, and causes no trouble to the patient,
et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste,	If the head of the shoulder is dislocated in the intestine, and causes no trouble to the patient, and one can tie the intestine with a fine thread which is cut from the intestine of a beast.
en teil maniere:	in part.
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez,	take the head of this thread of intestine so that it is freed from the discharge,
et puis lie au chief de cest fil .i. fil de lin subtil tort,	Then he is bound to the head of this thread, namely a thread of fine linen twisted.
puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	Then he binds the thread to the needle, and sews through the intestine, and holds it in place in its course;
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this method of stitching is not strong except according to the way of the vein and the hope;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if there is great and wide wound, even if it is in one of the great intestines, if there is no remedy, except for subtility.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	Of fistula or that it be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule»,	From fistula or that it be, such as any wound or incision, when it breaks, it is called universally a fistula.
et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	and immediately when it is closed or broken
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor,	and the fistula is always a strong and white nodule, or one does not feel pain,
et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	And it is just as painful as the quill of a bird.
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	Never in a clear fall, and sometimes wide open;
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	Never in a clear break, and sometimes wide open; never in a slight case, and sometimes enough;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char,	and I have spoken of this in the division of wounds, that every wound that is not sutured, and there is scar,
ce n’est fuers que par une des .viiij. causes:	This is not fire but by one of the eight causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	namely, by the smallness of blood or bone.
ou por sa malice;	or by its wickedness;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because there is hard matter inside, and on the eyelids, that does not allow new growth to take place.
ou il i a trop de bowe;	Or there is too much swelling.
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	Or the limb is swollen, and the matter is of poor quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	Or the medicine is not good in the cure;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	Or because the corruption is like pestilence;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	Or for its property in that region is late the digestion, and late the healing, and flees by nature.
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	Or there are veins or bones:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already mentioned these causes, their signs, and the cures of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Or I must tell you the cure for fistula, which is made by the work of the hands.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Hair that has become fistula arises in all members of the body due to pain.
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners,	for there are fistulas which come from great veins, and arteries, and nerves.
ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes,	or at the surface of the skin, or in the intestines, or in the bladder, or at some of the bones,
ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	or at the spine, or at any joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	If part comes to the property of the main limb, and there are similar ones.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	All fistulas of this kind are grievous to heal, and there is nothing but toil and ignorance.
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure,	and if there is no fistula that does not go away except as I have said, and you have undertaken to cure it,
et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	you must know it is vain, if you attempt to drain or burn it if the fistula is straight;
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc,	And if the fistula is tortuous, if the circle of a vein tries to slip,
car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	for the swelling swells inward toward the curvature;
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes,	and if the fistula has holes and you do not close it well with attempts,
si la clisterize par l’un des pertus,	if the swelling bursts by one of the holes,
car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	For the moisture is short from a pierce to another, and the world is filled with it.
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont,	then when its sense is at your side, you know if there is bone or nerve, and is shut in a wound,
et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	and ask the patient well about the pain he feels at the pressure of your hand, and the limb or place where he feels it;
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine,	then when you know truly the limb or place where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or nerve, or artery or vein,
ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit,	Or in some cases that I have mentioned, if the limb follows what I have said,
et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and the bone is forced out of its place and the flesh is corrupted that is within.
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee,	and then the limb must be treated until it is healed,
et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues,	and if the fistula is well deep from the right place, if you must, you must pierce it as much as you wish.
puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule,	Then I make soft compresses in medicine, and I hold them until the head of the fistula.
tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	until the medicine softens the superfluous matter that is decomposed at the bottom.
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then I put greasy ointments on the wound until it is healed;
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit,	and if it is not healed by this, if I must cauterize as we have said,
et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And if the bone is corrupted by fistula, if possible.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If the vein or nerve does not trouble you or the principal limb, as we have said.
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee,	and if the bone is discovered, and there is corruption and blackness, if you can wait until the corruption is entirely bony,
puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	then cure it with gentle means until it is healed;
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant,	If he is not well, and returns bowed as before,
saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	if he is not well, and returns bowed as before,
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons,	stay still until he feels well again,
et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	and then restore the limb;
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	And if it is still sound, that is well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If not, take note that corruption has already progressed too far, and you will be unable to do anything about it.
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	unless there is some other remedy save for us to yield to nature;
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles,	and if there is any small bone which is corrupted, and you wish to treat it with tension,
si l’estrai a .i. estrument covenauble a ceu,	if the extraction has been made with a suitable instrument,
et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	if the extraction has been made with a suitable instrument, and if there is any bone remaining, if the threads are torn, do not leave any of it behind;
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour,	and if moisture opposes you, and there is no fault or fear,
si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	if pain and moisture and heat, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture,	And if you do not drive them out at once, if you put something above the wound that is prone to putrefaction,
et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os,	leave them as long as the bones are exposed.</start_of_turn>
et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	then there will be greater damage to the bones.</start_of_turn>
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse,	or if it is a large bone, such as a limb or thigh,
si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee,	If the hair is so long that the corruption is as great as the blackness of the bone,
puis restoure la plaie;	Then restore the wound.
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is great corruption, and it comes up to the marrow of the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	if you can cover and protect all the corruption, and then cure it until it is healed;
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint .i. home en sa jambe,	And I shall tell you of a fistula that occurred in a woman’s leg,
si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	and if you take it as an example and help in your work.
Il fut .i. jovencelz entor .xxx. ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors,	There was once a young girl around .xxx. years of age, who had a pain in her leg due to something inside the body,
tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	so long as the matter came to the limb, and there was an abscess which did not have any known cause until it was opened;
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri,	But the mire grows more violently above than below,
et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	But the mire grows more violently above than below,
et maint mire i mirent cure entor .ij. ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains,	and remains cured for a year and a day, and there is no skill in the art of hands,
tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit,	so long as I recall it, and came to see it and the medicines with which they were cured,
et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	And what was right was pierced by a great force.
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	And became red the limb of the youth, and had the color of citron.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus,	I bound a bandage in one of these wounds, and then encircled all the wounds,
et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	and found that one vein ran into the other from all parts of the limb.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os,	I have seen it now, and I grasped in one of the holes until I uncovered a part of the bone,
et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	and I found it broken and split, and the pus came up to the bone inside.
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I saw what appeared to be a fractured bone, and I believed there was no other corruption, except for this which I saw.
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and I began to restore the wound with long stitches of medicine, but I could not make it stay closed.
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant,	And then I recommenced, and I discovered the bone just as before.
et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	And I found the corruption continuing in the bone, and the marrow, and then the bone itself, and I pondered about soldering the limb.
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole,	but I could not do anything except that I grasped a palm of the bone, and the traitor forced me to all his might,
puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment,	then I restored him with medicines; and he was healed and restored quickly,
et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir,	And it will not be necessary to renew the work for the weakness of the patient, who cannot bear it.
et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and by fear of death which I avoid for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement,	For often there is the evacuation of blood, but he remained whole and sound,
et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	and there issued from the bone a hard scale, which was well placed and caused no discomfort or contradiction in any way, neither in its height nor in its depth.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if a bone is fractured in no part but by force, if you must suture it in this manner:
pren .i. liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert,	take hold of one end, and strain at the head of the bone that breaks open,
et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	and command that it does not extend upwards;
et met .i. autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os,	and put another layer of linen more substantial than the first, and bind it over the edge of the bone that is protruding,
et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz,	And the head of the shoulder, if you pull the corrupt flesh away from the socket,
et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and discover the bone on the socket or you see marrow, that the bone does not break the flesh;
et met .i. tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	put a cushion or a board below the bone to cover the corrupt flesh;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and cover as much as you can see and feel the corruption, and do the same again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie,	And if the bone is corrupted, and does not open wide, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part,
si descuevre la char toute; puis met .i. tison desoz,	if the fracture breaks through the skin; then put one finger of lead on it.</start_of_turn>
et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption .i. poc, si com nos avons dit;	and then hold the corruption from one part to the other, and if necessary for a length of time as we have said.</start_of_turn>
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in the joint, if you join the fractured bone and hold the bone that contains the other part.</start_of_turn>
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des .ij. jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	And if the corruption is in the continuity of the two joints, if there is no other angle except the round one;
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose,	And if the corruption is or hangs from the arm, or hangs from the leg, if that is strong in that matter.</start_of_turn>
mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	but always inquire about that corruption, how it happened to you.</start_of_turn>
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and take care of it in all ways that you can, but that the vein or nerve does not hinder you;
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous,	and the nails which he incisions and the threads to cover these bones are many, according to the position of the bones and the appearance of swelling.

et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	And the testimony of the manners of diseases.

dou feu	fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The shoulder joint dislocates due to moisture, or by pressure, or by force;
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	And when you have treated that corrosion with medicines, and it has not profited,
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	if you must cover that limb until the corrosion disappears.
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	or if the patient escapes by death, or by malice, which is greater, the fault of the limb;
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	and the limb appears black, as if burned by fire,
et porrist aprés la noiror, puis va celle corrosions de membre em membre,	And thus after the darkness, then comes the corrosion of members in member,
et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper,	And thus after the darkness, then comes the corrosion of members in member,
et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans,	and grasps all the body; if you hurry to uncover,
se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	and if there is corrosion at the head of the shoulder, if the limb is dislocated, and you do not give it space to come down to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes up to the hand, if the socket at the joint is such that the corrosion does not reach the forearm;
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors,	if it reaches the forearm, if the socket at the wrist is loose; and if the corrosion passes the wrist, that is death.
et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	it is worth nothing against the quantity of its [disease’s] virulence.
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	and all that you do when the corrosion comes or goes: if it comes in the first joint, if the socket after the other joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	And if it comes or if it befalls, if you seize it all;
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	And if it comes or if it befalls, if you seize it all;
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	And if it comes from below the elbow, if there is no other ailment but that the patient is dead;
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz,	and you must cover or bind the limb if you wish to keep it in place.</start_of_turn
et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont,	And extend one minister from the lower limb, and another minister from the upper limb,
et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les .ij. liiens a .i. spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	And you shall separate the flesh that is between the two limbs at a breadth of one span, until the bone is exposed.

et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	and I will tell you that there was once a man in our home who suffered from this.
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	He had a blackness that seemed to burn with fire.
et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	and that corruption first arose in his armpit, so that it consumed the whole limb.
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when we saw the corruption, if we covered the limb, and it became well;
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi,	and long after it returned the corruption or the limb, and it came to me,
et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	And I put upon him things that rebound after the softening of the disease, and I cannot cease the corrosion;
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	And he swears that I must hold his hand, and I do not wish, for I avoid any hope of rebounding the matter.
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist,	I also doubt that if I cut off his hand, he will not die.
car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre,	for the strength of the man was weak; and he awoke all, and returned to his land,
et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	And so he covered his hand, and was healed;
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	I have heard of nothing like this except for this occasion, when we had to do something about it.</start_of_turn>
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Blood often escapes from an opening in the vein, and remains for a long time, causing great swelling;
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	Then it turns back and breaks, and in doing so breaks the vessel;
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	And the skin which is below is also as subtle as a silken drape that hangs down.
et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	and does not reach the bone or the nerve, and such a condition is called "sanity".
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	it is not called "fistula".
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it is so prolonged that it reaches the bone embedded in the marrow, it is called "fistula".

et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Do not yield to its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont,	When the leather is thick, hold it firmly as if it were a drape.

regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	Look at him, if his face is swollen and his nose is puffed up like a blow of foul air.

prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu,	Take alum, oil, and pitch, equally, and mix them together in a vessel over a fire,

fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	Do this treatment until the swelling is reduced and the bone is solid;
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres,	And never is the spleen clustered with water of amber.
quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus,	when this remedy is not present, and you take amber from the must of grapes, and drink water from above,

et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	And if he is feverish, sweating, and feels great pain, if you can, make him vomit first.
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus,	then grasp the spleen with the thumb and index finger and cut through under it.</start_of_turn>
et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	and guard that the cut does not reach up to the rib which is below the spleen, because the patient would feel too great pain.</start_of_turn
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	and if there is any, put something above which calms it.</start_of_turn>
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain of the hand comes from the wrist.
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	The two joints that arise in the hands of some people by chance are all fleshy,
et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle,	and sometimes there is bone there, and never is there a nail,
et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	and no nails are born at the root of the joint, or are born elsewhere on the limb.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet,	He who is born in no place of doubt shall not move.
et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	He who is born at the joint of doubt, by chance shall move.
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	the size of that which is fleshed is light, in part only:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	size like the root of a broad spatula
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born at the root of the joint is grieved to cure: if you hold him tight.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os,	If he is born or must at the rear not, if you must first bend the limb round to the bone,
puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then bend the bone to a convenient degree, and then cure it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The wounds that come from this must be assembled come from birth, or from a wound, or from the burning of fire, or from similar things.

puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	then put between two bands or cloths soaked in rose oil, that they do not adhere.</start_of_turn>

Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	When the swelling comes from neither of its two ends with the palm, if you can restore the dislocation if it is possible.</start_of_turn>
Des vils	Des vils
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	The veins are swollen and filled with dark, melancholic fluid that comes with pain in many limbs.
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and more often in the limbs that are at rest and working and bearing weight, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is therefore necessary that you do not give any purgatives, and then repeat the poultice.
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The iron cure is as follows: two methods. One is with the tongs, and treat the black blood.
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	And the other method is to tie up the vein, and then treat it forcefully.</start_of_turn>
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The size is as follows: first raise the affected limb high and warm, until the swelling is reduced.</start_of_turn>
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	Then strain the limb from the hip down to the knee joint.</start_of_turn
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	Then grasp the vein in one, two, or three places, of a large size,
puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	Then grasp the vein in one, two, or three places, of a large size, and immediately ligate and pull out the black blood from your hand from one end to the other, as much as the patient can tolerate;
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then bind it, and instruct the patient to keep pressure on the black blood with meat;
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and resume the evacuation and the bleeding as soon as the veins are full, and do no harm to the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	The ailment of this one is as follows: open the limb of the patient, and if there is hair,
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	then take out the hair or shave it off, and make the limb limp until the limb turns red and swells the veins.
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	if there is no bath, if the fire burns, and then hold the limb over the fire and when the skin is long over the elbow or on the ankle of the foot;
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then cover the skin with ointment and press the limb from the heel to the buttock until it turns white when you touch it;
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	And on the wound there is redness and black spots, and when it enters or leather seems just like a white cord.
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	Then stretch the wound outwards, until it is level with the leather, and then bind it with a thin bandage.</start_of_turn>
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	Then fold the edges inwards twice; then cut the leather over the wound as much as it opens,
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	Then keep the wound closed, if you have done so, and bind it with another bandage, as you did before.</start_of_turn>
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	Then grasp another size, or several if you are dealing with them, then hold the thumb and index finger together,
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	Then grasp another size, or several if you are dealing with them, then hold the thumb and index finger together;
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	and if you do not draw it out and lift it, if there is a strong double thread at all times,
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and bind and draw it out, and if there are nails there, grasp them with your hand from both sides, until it is gone;
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	Keep her still, for if she moves, she will not be able to be treated or lifted, and this will bring harm to the patient.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	When you have finished treating her, if you take out the foreign body from the wound, soak it in wine and rose oil; and cure it until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	And if her limb is contracted and twisted and bound together, and it is not straight, as we have said,
si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	Then you must break it [the dislocation] violently, but do not cover it; and treat it as we have said before.</start_of_turn>
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The form of fire from which we take the hook is curved, and does not tear me, but only grasps the vein.
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	it is of great curvature, for if it were slight, it would grasp the vein; but let it be large as we have said, and this is the form:
De la voinne civile	of the civil vein.
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is found in the limb, in the hot parts or where there are no herbs or trees, and in the earth where there is no moisture;
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	And by chance it happens elsewhere except in the leg, and this comes from the decay that comes from under the skin.
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	if it comes from the serpents in the flesh and towards, grasp between skin and bone.</start_of_turn>
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	And if there is a sign of swelling in this vein that comes in the leg, a very great inflammation,
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	then the limb is chained, and the vein becomes strong like a plant root.</start_of_turn
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When the arm is broken, if it is certain that you must wrap around a piece of lead from one and a half inches to one and a third, and the knot,
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	When the arm is broken, if it is certain that you must wrap around a piece of lead from one and a half inches to one and a third, and the knot, leave the lead in place on the limb, and every time that it points downwards, if you wrap around the lead, and the new knot.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, if you must break off a part, and wrap around the remainder, and do not cover it in its root, until it is completely healed
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	because if you break it off, if it returns into the bone, and makes come abscess or infection or wound, and makes worse the disease.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	For this reason, it is necessary that everything be treated promptly and thoroughly, and that nothing be left undone or neglected.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	and never is this vein sound when treated with five palms of length, or ten,
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	and once has come to me, from which it was taken out in ten palms of length, and when you seize it, if there be any bruise or fracture, and you pierce it through to the marrow,
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	if it is all right; and either evacuate the matter which is within, and apply to the place medicines which are soothing, so as to cause no further pain, and then cure as with abscesses.

et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And it comes out of the wound, and from there it slips out; cure it then as we said before.
Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	From the veins that arise between skin and bone.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This disease is called in our land "beef disease", because it often causes swelling.
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	And it is a little vessel that is born between skin and bone, and runs throughout the body, ascending and descending.
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	and it is often perceived on the alert of a limb, from the time it breaks the skin or it is moving, and leaps forward
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and it is filled with the humors of blood, such as comes towards and serpens and worms and fat; or belly
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	and there is doubt of its malice, for when it goes through the body, and it reaches the head, and comes to the marrow,
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	By chance he enters, and breaks the oil; and this often happens.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it healed and treated, if one cannot force it until it goes away, except when it wishes to.
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	then you must certainly tie up the limb above and below with a strong and well-stitched ligature,
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	then you must go up and draw it out, and if you see that it is pierced in the flesh, and you do not find it,
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	If the fire cautery is above, while it burns;
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	And the greatest harm that it makes is when it burns the fat, as we have said before.
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	If you see it coming or close to the oil, immediately grasp its bristles and pull them out forcefully.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	and you must use the patient various means of physical and medicinal treatment for the bad humors that cause it
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	And if there is swelling of the flesh under the skin, it must be drained away with a porcupine.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	And if there is swelling of the flesh under the skin, it must be drained away with a porcupine.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This disease is called in our land "vakirir," and is a pain that comes in the joints,
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and thus it moves from limb to limb; and I have seen this happen.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sickly woman, and discovered a small swelling in her armpit.
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	and when I lifted her arm, it rose up like a worm on the shoulder
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	more swollen than anything, like silver that has been cut from its root
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	the pain came from there, and settled in the shoulder,
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	And then a little afterwards corrected by the whole body, so that it came into the other arm.
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	Then he told me that it twisted back towards the body, as I saw it.</start_of_turn>
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I wondered how he managed to move about without wanting this sickness in this way.</start_of_turn>
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	although I know that I must keep in mind that it is good to move without causing pain to others.</start_of_turn
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	But I do not wish to tell it, if as I see it in the woman.
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	and I thought that it was because the woman had dry hair and her veins were exposed.
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	because of that appeared that windstorm constraint;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and I do not see it according to this reason to those who have moist hair and veins covered.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	When you see the cure for this ailment and the patient feels that pain, if it breaks open as we have said,
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	if the swelling above and below has increased, and then becomes soft as soon as that constraint is overcome.
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	cauterize the limb; and if you do not see it with your eyes,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	if the treatment for that which brings out the swelling, such as foul pills and serapins, and the like.
Des saiettes	Des saiettes
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The towels are various, according to their appearance and the nature of the wound or the pain they soak up.</start_of_turn>
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	There are various towels, some with large points, some with small points, some with curls, and some smooth.</start_of_turn
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	some with angles, some with long ends, and some with pieces.</start_of_turn
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	And that which breaks in no limb breaks in like manner: or in the primary limb it breaks,
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	or if it breaks in the skull, the brain, the liver, the spleen, the kidneys, the bladder, and the like members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it breaks in no limb, then the sign of death is that which I shall tell you later, I will teach you:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	because the death comes afterwards in many ways;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	And when such a bad sign does not deceive me, and the arrow does not enter my body, if you delay, cure the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And the sign of the brain when the arrow pierces the bone, and leaps up the substance that is above the brain,
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	is when scooping and soiling and vomiting and redness in the eyes, inflammation and redness of the tongue, spasm and mixture of senses, and vomiting of bile;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and by chance it is without fever, or pain; and by chance it loses speech and voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	And from the wound, white moisture like pus, and in like manner with burnt hair;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And if this sign appears to you, if you are to take care of it, draw out the arrow if it is not embedded.</start_of_turn>
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the arrow when it is pricked or broken, is that it is close to the left breast, and feels as though it were embedded in something hard, do not open it.</start_of_turn
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and sometimes the arrow moves like pus, and in dark blood, and comes cold sweat and cold sweat, and fainting.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The wounds therefore suggest doubt that the patient will survive.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	The mark of the wound suggests that whenever it does not burst, it swells up and the patient turns blue, his face turns pale, and he sighs with open mouth.</start_of_turn>
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the wound bursts open on the covering of the bone, if there are many little bones; it causes great swelling and great pain and sighs; and the limb moves stiffly.</start_of_turn
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the wound bursts or breaks open, by chance anything indigestible from the meat is not left in the wound.</start_of_turn
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the sponge is split or the belly burst, and in leaping at any point of dung through the intestine root, if there is no hope of cure, do not attempt to extract the sponge.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the sponge breaks in the bladder, and the urine spurts out and comes out in bursts, and the patient feels great pain: such wounds are deadly.</start_of_turn>
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	As for the other limb, if the face, the neck, the chest, the armpit, the groin, the shoulder, the elbow, the wrist, the hand, the foot, and the limb in general are affected by numerous disorders.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the sponge is in the nerve or the artery, and it is not venomous, as I have already told you, because of what you have done otherwise.</start_of_turn>
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	There was once a case where an arrow pierced the root of the nose.
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I grasped it [the arrow] and it slipped from the other side through the fat of the ear, and it was cured without any harm
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And there was another case where an arrow pierced the fat of the oil from the socket of the ear,
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	and the arrow was removed, and did not reach beyond the tip towards the head.
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And it was the great arrow of a Turkish archer, with all its weight towards the ear; the wound was sound, and there was no bad accident.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And it went from the throat to a Christian, and the Arabic arrow was towards the ear:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I saw the beards, and I plucked them out as long as I could, and the Christians were sound.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And I pulled out an arrow from a woman who was sitting or crouched, and I thought she was going to die;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	And then, if he does not pass .xxx. days, if he does not mend his condition;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	and then, if he does not pass .xxx. days, if he does not mend his condition, I will cut on the armpit, the groin, the back, and there will be no further mishap.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if thus a home with a wound that has burst open or has become infected, and it has been treated with dressing;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	and if thus a home with a wound that has burst open or has become infected, and it has been treated with dressing, and if it does not improve his condition,
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	He finds no rest in any of his natural works.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And thus another man, who had an arrow stuck in his face, and was sewn up the wound;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	and thereupon suffered great pain; and there were other similar things.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	and thus an arrow was shot at a prince of the king, who was sitting among the nobles,
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	And it was a downward slope to the right side; and the arrow was entirely withdrawn.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	And I was called to the treatment after it had been closed for two days. If I found the wound very wide, it would be very painful
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I saw her quite pale and limp, and did not feel her;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and there was no longer any pulse or pain in her right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought it was the tip of the arrow.
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I placed upon the wound a soothing plaster to prevent inflammation
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and appeared to me the wound of the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I put on the bandage again, closed the wound, and held the patient’s hand for a long time
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	As long as he feels the arrow still inside his knee; and he told me so.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I put on the wound medicine an acrid ointment with hands, as long as it was overdone,
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	and held it, feeling the tip of the arrow which was still inside;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I closed the wound opening with that medicine again, until the tip of the arrow was visible to me.
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	And beyond that, the ending of this month has passed the three moons,
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	And thus, when the ailment that I bound with nails at one end and at the other had stretched out, I could no longer bear it;
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	so that I was forced to make other implements of steel to subdue it.
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	according to what its form will be at the end of this chapter, as soon as I have treated it, I will restore the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the physician judges that the cartilage of the nose cannot restore itself:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And he restored it immediately, and the wound healed, and the patient was completely healed.</start_of_turn>
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	Or as you have said concerning the quality of the extraction of some arrows,
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	if you put your cure on that which I do not understand, because the book does not teach me that;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	But the wisest masters know well of many great things, and of what is present and lacking.
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Truly nine works, and nine instruments, in descending order of things that are strange which arise in this art
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that the sponges do not arise from members or that they are woven for that matter in various ways.
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or by liquid or by any other means;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	And that which leaps forth by itself or enters, that is an arrow transfixed in the flesh, and it leaps nevermore.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not leap now, if you leave it as long as the flesh is swollen, and rejoice in the issue;
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	And if it is fixed in the bone, and it cannot be extracted, if you leave it there for a while, and it moves every day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And then it leaps, and if it does not leap, if you pierce through all of its substance, as long as the flesh is swollen, and then you will pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	If the splinter is fixed in the bone of the shoulder, and goes up to one of the ventricles of the brain,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	If the splinter is fixed in the bone of the shoulder, and goes up to one of the ventricles of the brain, and if no other accidents occur which I have mentioned to the patient: if you do not treat it immediately, but leave it until it is even again after some days,
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	because if the splinter reaches the marrow, that is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	and if the splinter is only fixed in the bone and does not reach the marrow,
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And remains the patient lying without moving for several days, if the fire of treatment should depart.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And remains the patient lying without moving for several days, if the fire of treatment should depart. If it has been moistened and cannot be stirred, if it is administered with tar, as I have said; then cure the limb until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the scab has been placed in the limb if it cannot be seen, if the hand has all its might;
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you sense it, if the hand has no visible support;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	And if you do not grasp firmly the wound, and the depth of the arrow,
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and there is no bone, nerve or vein, if the wound is great as the wound itself.
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	pull out the arrow if you grasp it, and if there is an ear in the arrow that holds it,
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	if the bone which is stuck in the flesh comes out with the grasp.
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	Then break or bend the arrow's ears as much as you can, until you can pull it out.
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And take great care that you do not break the arrow, but that you grasp it more firmly.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	If you do not manage it once, if the blood has clotted around the wound, then pull it out, for it is an alleviation.</start_of_turn>
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	If it bleeds too much, do as we have said in the chapter about the cure.</start_of_turn
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	And beware of cutting into the nerves and the vein, and put on something to hold the arrow in place without risk.
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	Or twist or tear, or firmly or gently; and hold the patient in the position in which he was when the arrow was shot inwards.</start_of_turn>
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	for this is the greatest help that there is, and if you do not do so, if he moves according to what it shows him, you will know.</start_of_turn>
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another place, or he opens nothing of it, or the skin is swollen in the place where it is seen or felt:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	Tailes donc sur, tant que les tenailles puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut durer maintenant.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	Therefore take hold of it immediately, as long as the nails can grasp it, and then extract it: if it leaps out now.</start_of_turn>
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	If it cannot be loosened, if you leave it embedded, and then resume the extraction until it comes out;
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if there is any remaining bone, if the bone has become loose at the root.</start_of_turn
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	And if he cries out, and you see him administer violently, if he administers with a biting instrument,
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	if he bites with the point of the needle between the teeth of the instrument; and then you must force out,
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and if the needle is bitten, then you must hold the instrument so that the point enters, in order to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	and if the wound is surrounded, you must believe that you have cauterized all the fat or the venom is there, if you please,
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	Then treat the wound if it is appropriate.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	Then if the wound has split or burst open on the belly or the side or the groin or the chest, and it is close, you must cover it over, if you cover it over.</start_of_turn>
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and keep covering the wound and the nerves, and then extract it, and then sew up the wound, if necessary.</start_of_turn>
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and treat it until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the tenailles used for extracting arrows is similar to the beak of an eel, and thus is this form.
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the arrow
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape of the socket is also like the quill of a bird,
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	the handle of the tenailles is made of wood, and its length is eight lines.
