li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The form of the teeth is such that they can bite and scratch if it is thus:
des voinnes dou cors communes	the common teeth are blunt
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	almost all of them have a root or a head of sixteen,
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	namely the two that are behind the ears, which are blunt-tipped.
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	And the blood vessels which are in the temples appear.
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	And the veins which are in the armpits, which are called "aspirations".
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	And the vein that is under the forehead; and the vein that is at the back of the neck.
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	And the armpits which are at the collarbone;
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	And the veins which are on the lips from the mouth, these are the veins which are called "augeherich".
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	And the veins which are under the tongue
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The veins which are usually seen in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	The one is the cephalic vein, which runs alongside the left rib, and is called the great vein.
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	And the marrow is called "fat," and is composed of the cephalique and basilique.
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	and they call it the marrow of the head "brain"; and the basilique is when the rib is either too high or too low,
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	and they call it the marrow of the belly, and is above the navel,
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and is that which we see, which appears openly on the belly.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	And the salvation is the vein that is between the auriculaire and the anulaire, and if there is only a little rain.
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	and in the limb or where the feet are, there are two veins: one if it is outside the cubitus of the left side coasting,
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the second is below which is at the ankle of the right side coasting; and the vein which is called the “nesse,” which is in the ankle of the other side coasting.
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other limb are two veins besides those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The blood of veins that are behind the ears helps to expel old blood and evacuate;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	and the quality of the blood, as I have said, is that you must raise the head of the patient.</start_of_turn>
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	and wipe the limb or the veins are rough; then hold the patient’s head still with a pin,
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	until the veins behind the ears open behind the ears depend on the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	Why do you linger here, when at your duty, or where you feel the pulse of your lord throbbing? If so, take hold of your spear.
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	Then take the lancet and pierce through the vein until you reach the bone, then hold your hand over the upper part of the vein.</start_of_turn>
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	and hold the skin and the vein firmly in place. Two should suffice to traverse, and make blood flow until you see;
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then strain and bind it, until it is healed.</start_of_turn
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	And I have already spoken of incision and cautery, or the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The blood of the two temples, if it is like an ancient emigration,
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	and swelling, and boils accustomed, and at the root of tears of water has eyes;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the quality of the sick person is like that which I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	And it is that the patient strains his neck, so that the veins open wide;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feels the pulse throbbing down his throat, and then turns pale.</start_of_turn>
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	then take hold of the limb above the vein at your index finger, and insert the lancet downwards.</start_of_turn>
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	and keep the vein elevated, and apply pressure, as you have done with other veins, and draw out blood according to your need.</start_of_turn
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	Then loosen the patient, and place your thumb on the vein for an hour, then put on cotton.
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	Then loosen the bandage, and leave it until it is healed; as we have already spoken of its application and its management and its extraction, or its beginning from the book.</start_of_turn>
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The blood of the forearm is worth as much as the blood of the cephalic vein has old diseases of the face, and has migraine, and redness.</start_of_turn
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and if the patient feels pain in his neck while rotating, while the vein opens;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	Then take the instrument which is called the "fosseur," which is like this:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	Then take the instrument which is called the "fosseur," which is like this. Place the point on the vein, and press with your hand, or something else, and let blood spurt out as much as you see fit;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then deliver to the patient the collar, and ligate the vein until it is well sealed and never do anything with a large flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not permitted that the flames be too strong; and the same with the air, for the bone is near, and by chance the flames break the bones when they are subtle.
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The blood of the armpits that are in the armpits helps with the swelling, and with the swelling of the spleen, and with the redness, and with the swelling of the armpits, and with diseases of the face.
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and if the patient’s blood is of poor quality, that is if the patient twists the cord of any vessel, as before;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	then, the physician must take hold of the limb, and make the burn of a long flame, for there is no fat.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flame is slight, by chance if it breaks; then make blood flow, as much as you are able, and then tie up tightly, and bind well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The blood of the vein does not boil if it is cold, and is soothed by thirst, and by diseases of the face.
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	if it comes with migraine and redness that comes on the face, and even when it is old;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	and if the patient has a stiff neck, then strain his hand to your left side,
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	and take the fire slowly and long, and insert it between the two nostrils,
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	For the vein does not open easily for me, and without beginning, I must now correct it.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	I do not open the vein easily, and I must not linger any longer. Correct the blood immediately as you deem necessary, and then bind it for the night, for it is still too swollen to restore
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	This is the form of flame:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The blood of the veins helps to loosen stiffness, and to commence the blending of medicines, and for moisture, and for diseases, and for corruptions, and for herpes, and for tumours;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	And if the patient pulls out his collar bone with one hand and with the other, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	and the master should be standing over the patient's head, and the patient should sit up on his seat.</start_of_turn>
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	then take the vein long and wide, and then draw blood temperately, or as much as is necessary;
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	then repeat the procedure on the other vein, and loosen the ligature, and gently restrain the veins,
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The patient must not strangle; and let him stay until morning, when the wound is healed.
De la sainie des leivres	When the blood of the veins has been let out.
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The blood of the veins of the arms above helps to cause bloating in the mouth, and corruption of the gums, and wounds of the lips, and toothaches and fevers.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And you must make the patient sit before you, and strain his neck as I have said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	Then turn the palm of your hand, and look at your two veins, one of which is on the right side of the hand and the other on the left.
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	and you will know them by this, that they are black, and that around them there are small black veins.
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	then take hold of both of them, and if you do not know them and are in doubt,
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	if the larger one is at the armpit, and also do the two veins which are under and above, for this is a similar method.
De la sainie desoz la lengue	From the blood of the veins, the tongue is nourished.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The blood of the veins which are nourished from the tongue helps after the blood of the cephalic vein, and this is at the stretching of the throat, and with eye diseases, and with mouth diseases.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the quality of the blood is that if the patient lies between your hands before the sun, and he holds the tongue, and looks from each cheek towards a black vein:
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	then both the one and the other are pale, and do not move too much, for these are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The veins which are commonly known to cause pain are usually healed in two ways:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	or by pricking with a blunt needle at all times, or with a fine lancet as with cuts in trenches, and is called "anesil".
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and are large and subtle according to the size and strength of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the blunt needle is well known, and is large as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it is necessary to open the large veins which are filled with thick blood and contain much blood and trouble.
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the form of the olive flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and is more pointed, and is for healthier the small veins, or there is small yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The blood of the basilisk, which is one of these veins, helps with the diseases that are swelling of the throat, and the swelling of the cheek, and of the belly;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	And it is fitting for the patient to remain calm and quiet, and to restrain the artery which is below.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he seizes the artery, and blood flows from it, if it is held firmly as I have said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and must not be tormented by the flame, but should be clipped as with an anesil.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the fleshy tumor does not appear obviously, if you must remove it, and bind another in its place;
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	or you desire no rain from it, or you hold in its place the vein which fills the arm: it opens manifestly.
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and the burn of the flame is silent, as we have said before
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	and if you see that the blood vessel is known, if you must indeed remove the arm, that you touch the root as long as you know the pulse;
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then sign the limb, and then bind the arm, and burn the vein silently;
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And beware that you do not pierce the artery when you see the limb inflamed, for it is the artery: stop immediately.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it swell up like the urine of a child, and it is neither red nor pale, quit until it is not an artery: stop immediately.
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	hurry up and put your thumb on its length, then hold your thumb if it does not bleed, for many times it has happened;
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	keep your arm still, and leave it alone, and do not move the patient; and if there is doubt or fear, do not move until it is safe
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if it is not stained, and it is painful, and the medicine is not present, if the artery bursts open, because the head of the retractor is withdrawn; staunch it immediately.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a bundle of sponges, and press, and take one of the halves and bind it firmly to the other;
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	if it is not stained, that is good; but if not, if the physician, as we have said, prescribes powders which staunch blood
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	and the staunching is not complete in many cases by reason of the small size of the wound and the weakness of the limb.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	The blood in the vein helps to cure the pain at the root of the head and the swelling below.
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	because it is composed of the basilar and cephalic veins, as we have said before.
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	and it is useful for the health that it flows through the nerve that is below, and if it does not flow too deeply, and finds the nerve,
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and it swells and the patient either suffers or is cured; by chance it cannot be cured.
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	And this nerve often opens several times, and if it does not open in some home by its subtlety, it is certain that you must take care of its safety from the anesthetic instrument; and keep the nerve still at your will.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a bundle between the two nerves, if it is long enough.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The blood of the cephalic vein helps, that it attracts blood towards the head, and helps the eyes;
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	and it is more convenient to pierce with the olive or myrtle flame, because it is the safest of all veins, because it has neither nerves nor arteries.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	Whatever be the case, it is better to ask for help at the beginning, and do not grieve if it does not work the first time, and we begin again.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	and sometimes the head of the limb swells up at home, so that it cannot be done the first time, but do not grieve.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the blood is as you think
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing you must know about health is that blood must be kept only for the purpose of preserving health,
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	And thus avoid future ailments.
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	And let the blood be drawn from one of the two veins which are or should be: namely, the cephalic, the facial, or the basilar;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	If one must draw blood in the commencement of prayer, and in fasting and after eating, when the sign of repletion appears;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	If one must draw blood immediately or later, after one or two hours or two hours
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The blood which is administered for diseases has no set dose, but whenever need be for fear or for nourishment, at all hours and in all conditions;
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	it is not permissible to give medicine to children under twelve and a half years of age, or to women who are pregnant for more than seven months.</start_of_turn>
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	It is not permitted to give medicine to those who have passed sixty years.</start_of_turn>
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	and when anyone sees that he is sick, in whatever way, it is permitted that he can defend himself by emptying the intestines of a lesser hernia.</start_of_turn
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	If there is a tooth of madness retained, so that the veins do not draw intestines with the surplus of blood that flows from the principal members;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	if there is too much blood in the body, or if it is vomited, or if there is diarrhea, or if there is sweating;
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and if one has suffered from colic passion, vomiting, and abdominal pain, and has had many women in childbirth, and has journeyed, and has fasted and abstained from food, and all his power, or from a wound or illness;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then subtilize the humors, if they are not great, by foods and by drinks and by medicines, if you can;
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	Then between or in water, if nothing hinders, to subtilize the blood,
et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	and you will save from the vein just inside or outside, as we have said before.
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and you will keep this work, and from pricking, and from luxury, and from similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	and so be bound and joyous, and let the blood be higher than it should be, and wipe away the tears once or twice.
puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	Then it is strange that the limb hangs loose below the middle, for when it is too tight or loose, it cannot be corrected without;
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then the hand grasps the limb, as long as the veins swell and are felt.</start_of_turn>
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	then moisten the limb with a little oil, then put the thumb of your left hand on that vein below the limb a little or as much as you see is better.</start_of_turn>
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	so that the vein does not swell and crack.</start_of_turn>
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	For there are veins that flee like cords from the body of the patient, and if there are some that are full of windiness,
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	if when one sets the flame on them, they recoil from the flame, and cannot be opened, and thus are these.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	if the vein bursts, the wound is too wide, for in this case it is necessary that the surgeon be advised in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein bursts the first time, that is good; but if it bursts again, it must be stopped once and for all, or it will not be healed.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the limb is inflamed and the patient feels faint, let him rest for one or two days and do not bind his arm.
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	Then indeed, after that will come abscesses; do not enter or bathe, then restart the bleeding if it stops;
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	And if the blood vessel is small, or if there is doubt that there will not be enough blood to justify the fire, if you fear that the limb itself will be scorched by the flame,
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And the work itself is often violent, even when the limb is inflamed; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the limb swollen, do not commence to bleed again; put on a bandage of oil, for it softens the flesh of blood, and is soothing in this limb the oil that is on it.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and give the oil bandage in the wound to stop the blood flow and keep the blood in its veins.</start_of_turn>
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	and thus makes a tingling and swelling of the flesh, when it is put on the limb; if it is left too long and escapes when it is too large.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite,	and if there comes a large abscess, which happens many times, even when the vein is only slightly injured or the wound is small.</start_of_turn
si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	If you are in a hurry, put on the wet and soiled sponge immediately and hold a fist of charcoal; restrain for an hour.
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	And know that you must do this after the evacuation of blood from the vein, and if it remains in place after a few days, no black or green mark, if there is no other cause for it.</start_of_turn>
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if you see, do not put anything of aloe or mastic root in juice of calamus, mustard, or anything similar.</start_of_turn>
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times there is swelling and appearance at the blood of the basilisk: put your hand on it, and if you feel the limb soft under the compression of the hand, if that is the bad appearance.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Leave it be that you put nothing more of this on me, for by chance in court without an artery; but make it do indeed. Emplace the dry earth firmly to harden the limb, then treat it with another treatment, until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	Treat each wound according to the quantity of its virtue, and the color of the blood.</start_of_turn>
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if it is dark red, leave it as long as it is dark; and if you see it thick, leave it as long as it is thin; and if it is too pale, leave it cool.</start_of_turn
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it is fitting for the prudent and strong person, who has the skill of bloodletting, to make the wound larger and the flames greater;
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	And for the weak person, do the opposite; keep the wound small and the flames small, and do it cautiously, do not prick it.</start_of_turn>
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And this method of bleeding saves life from excessive bleeding and damage to nerves, and is better than to bleed too much.</start_of_turn>
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc .iij. fois ou .iiij.	And for the one who has a cold, it is fitting to give soft bread soaked in pomegranate juice; if he is faint, give him two or three mouthfuls of blood.</start_of_turn
Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And if it is of cold complexion, if he drinks before the blood thick broth of soft bread in honeyed syrup, or in aromatic honey syrup with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, and a fragrant syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil,	And if he drinks at the blood, after the issue of blood vessels, it is recommended that he drink broth of barley and fragrant syrup.
et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	and use other things that we have said in the division or chapter of fainting, for the evacuation of the vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he sees his arm swollen, and is made well another time, if it is soaked by great blood, it is recommended that he rise up and rise up again, according to the quantity of his continuous virtue.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever has seen his arm swollen after the first bleeding, and he has strong pain, if he be well, within fifteen hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever has seen himself recover in another place, if he must recover on the second day or the third
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	For there is much blood in the body that has already been excreted, and brings fever; if you can remove a great quantity, and widen the opening so that it bleeds into pieces.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson,	then that you restore all the conditions of the bleeding, and put your hand on your pulse when it is well, that there is no more bleeding in place of the blood,
et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	And this often happens when the patient is negligent;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	And you must not trust them when you see them loosen their arm, and do not permit them to do it a second time, for the wound is closed, that you must press firmly upon it.</start_of_turn>
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	if it is crooked, extend the arm fully, for this would be bad.</start_of_turn
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer,	but leave it until the second time; or you touch the tip of the flame, until the blood that is frozen at the wound has escaped.</start_of_turn>
et met sus .i. poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	And put upon one hand a little piece of silk and press gently.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein has fled, if you leave it and do not restrain it, as long as the incision is calm.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if necessary is to drain blood a second time, if the same vein is still bleeding, or in another vessel, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein which is in the arm is blue instead of red because it is composed of blood.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And if the patient has his hand in hot water, until the blood vessel is red;
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then grasp it moderately, so that the vein opens well, and do not leave it too wide or too long;
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and if it cannot be passed, leave the hand in hot water, and let the blood flow in the water until enough has bled out;
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if it is in this state, do not put the hand back in the hot water, for more is put into the water than in this state.
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the blood of this vein is more precious than all the arteries and nerves.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The blood of the main vein is worth more than all diseases of the liver, and this is the way:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	strain the hand, and immerse it in hot water, until the vein escapes, if we see it;
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and if its blood escapes through the whole, and if you press it in every way, if nothing is damaged;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char,	And do not be too hasty, for the nerves are delicate and exposed without covering.
et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	Then reattach the limb gently, if it is not frozen in the wound, and do not move it.</start_of_turn>
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as well as you can, if you put oil and lint on the wound, it will help to heal quickly, and make a soft dressing.</start_of_turn
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The blood from the left hand is useful for the disease of the mouse, and do the same as I have said concerning the right side.</start_of_turn
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	The blood of the Sophene is worth for all the diseases that are in the bosom.
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	if like maladies of the marrow, and retention of blood, and disease of the veins, and of the spleen and legs old, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere,	And the quality of its blood is that if the patient has suffered with acute pain in the abdomen, and has froted on the belly until it blanches,
et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and the belly is swollen, and there comes out from under the joint pain; and the belly is at the ankle, and from under the pain there comes out drops of urine.
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	Healthy is the shoulder or more large rain, or at the ankle, that muscle values.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you keep it healthy on the bone, if you keep it warm from the cold that comes from outside, and the health of the passage is as if you were cutting; and be careful not to burn it.</start_of_turn>
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if it cannot be put back, if you reset the bone in the water, and let the vein drain well.</start_of_turn>
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if you must do it a second time, because the first time did not succeed, because it is salty;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	Do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and do the same with the other side equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The pulse of the sciatic vein is at the ankle of the foot, and its color is like the color of blood when it is hot.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	Its color is such that when the patient walks or bathes, it is strained under the ankle for three fingers of the hand
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	otherwise it does not open; and if it opens, in all the ways that you can imagine, and through the heel,
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And it is better to leave it alone, for its root is deep and it is easily returned by hand.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not find it, if you see neither hair nor skin broken, towards the little toe, and you guard against nerves;
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And do as much for the blood as you see, and then loosen the ligature, and put on cotton and pressure; it is now healed.
Des sainies de ventouse	Vacuum therapy
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	Balloons are made of horns, or silk, or wool; and the dressing should be performed in two ways: either by cutting and drawing out blood, or by cutting alone.
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	and the dressing which is made by cutting and drawing out blood if it is done in twelve ways,
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	for in this way one is all in the head; and the other is at the collar.
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	And thus with others in the armpits of both arms; and the wind of the spleen descends upon the stomach.
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	And the wind of the spleen descends upon the flanks; and the wind above the navel.
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	And the winds fill both arms; and the winds of both legs.
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	and the wind of the calves; and the circulation does not care about blood, except for small veins that are scattered in the flesh,
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	And therefore let no one fear it, as when we take blood from a vein.
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And therefore let no one fear it, as when we take blood from a vein.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if by necessity of disease it is necessary to administer it, or for custom, if the medicine is administered at the beginning of the month or at the end, and in every tension;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	for there are some who, when they must administer it, suffer from a heavy head;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	And if such people experience swelling and redness on their face, head, and neck, and their eyes are bloodshot;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and those who have a swelling of blood in their mouth, and have lost their tongue, and vomit blood.
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and if someone is conscious, and sees blood and foam and mucus and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and even when the patient has swallowed for two hours, we command them to vomit.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The blood from the wound helps to soothe the pain of the chief … that comes from these eyes, and it can only be done after the evacuation of all the hair;
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	and this evacuation of blood is better than the blood of the head.
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and it can only be done by one who has a cold complexion or who has catarrh, for this makes them suffer greatly;
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and for this reason it can only be done when used by those who have a cold head or who have a cold illness.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And he who remains silent after that, if he becomes suspicious, must therefore put the suction tube one place further down due to the doubt of suspicion.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	The suction tube at the nape of the neck is in lieu of the blood of the head and the bile, and for this reason it is worth at the utmost extent.</start_of_turn>
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	and there is a fissure of the channel of the beard, and throughout, and distension;
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and one must push it back, for if it is held too firmly, it causes suspicion or pain of the belly or the side.</start_of_turn>
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	The windsings cause as much pain in the chest as in the head, and pain in the belly, and vomiting, and strangulation, and pain in the root of the teeth.
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	It is in lieu of the blood of the basilisk; and it is commanded that the patient should express his hand to put it [i.e. the hand over the affected area], that he does not cut the artery, and does not cause blood to flow excessively.</start_of_turn>
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The windsings cause such diseases of the mouth as disease of the gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and it is in lieu of the remedies of the two upper teeth.</start_of_turn>
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The winds of the spleen are harmful to health, as they arise from heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	The winds of the spleen are as harmful as two veins of the arms,
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	because they draw blood from these large veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and commands the patient that he should not fear too much pain, for it is a sign of heat, and knows that nerves and arteries are not injured.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The wound on the buttocks is very painful, causing swelling of the underlying tissues and various diseases. It is therefore necessary that the dressing be large and of fine mesh, that it should adhere well; and by chance, if it should be too tight, it may burst, causing great damage.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The dressings on the legs swell widely, for they draw blood from all over the body, causing old wounds of the groin, of the kidneys, and the bladder, and bring swelling of the flowers; and are in the place of the groin bones, and the calves, and all of them cause the body to swell after a long time, and bring vomiting in various positions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to apply the dressing is that you must first empty it thoroughly, and then apply it steadily, and hold it firmly in place, and move it equally, and do not cease doing so until you see the flesh red and swollen, and open up the blood; then rest, and put the dressing back on, and take care of the body, for there are some who have had their share of suffering, and who have open pores: if you must cut once only, and you must make large wounds, and a deep wound; and do so gently
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if it is not large, it is sufficient to wound it three times: the first time to open the way for the large blood vessel.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if it is not very thick, it is sufficient to wound it three times: the first time to open the way for the large blood vessel. And when we want to drain blood somewhat and somewhat, we suffice with one wound only.</start_of_turn>
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	And if our veins burst with blood, if we repeat this often; and if the wound is large, if the patient is pierced through and through, then it is finished if the wound is perceived immediately.</start_of_turn>
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and it is suitable for those who have thick and tough skin and who have large pores, that you wipe away the swellings of oily aperitif and dissolvent:
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	If it is in this state, with violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or pumpkin seed oil;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	If it is in this state, with ivy oil, or rosemary oil, or chamomile, or something similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the swelling is large and cold, if you take marigold oil, or balsam oil, or angelica oil, and the like.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile,	And if there is a wound with sharp edges and large pores, it is not advisable to apply oil,
mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	But it is to be bathed afterwards with vinegar of roses, or cold vinegar, or vinegar of pomegranate, or vinegar of cucumber, or vinegar of porcelain, or anything similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And he who has moisture in his mouth, if he rises easily, or with rose water, or elderberry, and sumac, or similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And he who has thick drool raises it from old wine, or from strong ale, or from chamomile decoction or camomile, or other things like that.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou .ij.; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion,	and does not take care to be cured of the wind before or during the bath, but rather after the bath an hour or two; and does not sleep after the ventosation.
et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And it is fitting that he rests when he must vent and when he is vented.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	When he is rested who is sick is calmed, and if he is not too strong and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	he can then take cold things, such as grapes and fennel and lettuce at ease, and similar things;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	he should eat barley broth, and soft meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And he who has a cold complexion, if he takes syrup of honey, and wine fragrant mean, which is between old and new, and broth of herbs, and broth of physicians and petty birds and worms;
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and he must drink more than eat when he feels a draft;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and must give to others no food for a while neither garlic nor mustard before or after, for to comfort the main parts;
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and be discreet about it, but do not abstain from it except for those who are hot;
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	The wounds which are inflicted by the pointed instruments are those which are made on the liver, and on the spleen, and under the heel, and on the belly and the buttocks and the thighs and the elbow, for in no other member do wounds suffer from these instruments.
et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre,	and are only made to draw blood from one limb to another.
si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus lou ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	if as put them on the muscles when they do not wish to bleed; to overcome the viscosity which is in the limb, as when we put wounds on the belly and the buttocks to strengthen the limb.
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and relieve the pain, when there is an abscess or a fracture, if it is by its attractive virtue that it attracts the abscess, or displaces the fracture from its place;
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue,	And thus he must be held up when placed on the liver and on the side when there is retained air.
et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	And these blisters are administered empty so that they may be sucked out so soon; and never are they administered together with fire, and never full of cold water
si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	if there is swelling from pleurisy, and in such a manner we fill the blister with hot water, or with wine or herbs that are coveyed with this.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the blister administered with fire is like this:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	And he has twice the palm of his hand and a half of barley, or about the cost of a thousand small beads, as much as to push out an arrow.
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	Or if it is from the marrow, sweat before him if he does not bleed the patient on placing it on the limb;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	and he has in the middle a stick of bone or iron, to put on a bandage of lead,
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and should be large and small according to the diseases and the degree of these things that take them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	For the bubbles of the stomach are other than intestines, and fats are not like grease.
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	... grasp the collar of the gown or linen, and place it between the edge of the bubble and the skin of the limb.
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	If the burn is at the root of the bandage, let it not burn the patient.
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	Then place it on the limb, and keep it either above or below the hole we mentioned. If we see that it is about to burst, and the vapor is rising, grasp the bandage with the tweezers.</start_of_turn>
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And mark the surrounding area as before, and repeat the process often if necessary.</start_of_turn>
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the ventouse which is administered in the case of pleural disease, at all times, there is no thread or hole, and it is only administered when it is filled with water, and is placed on the limb only for a moment.</start_of_turn
et c’est li forme:	And thus is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Except in limbs or where we cannot apply a bandage due to their small size, such as the lips and gums, and similar things.
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	And in the naked parts of the body, such as the groin or the nipples, and others of a similar nature;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the quality of the patient if, when you discover wounds that are fresh and clean without any wound-covering, take them;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	And put one nut of soft water on them, until they are familiar, and do not have anything in their stomachs.
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	And then, either cauterize the vein and the abscess, then rub the limb until it is red, and put on the compresses.</start_of_turn>
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	When they are full and ache, and if it is possible to put on a vacuum, put it on, for this is better afterwards.</start_of_turn>
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If this is not the case, if you lift the limb easily, and then with water, moist well, and then squeeze it;
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	And if the limb is too long after the swelling subsides, if moist, like a drape of flax in cold water, place over it until the limb is stretched out.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	And if the limb is swollen, if put on broken glass, or splints, and similar things, until it is stretched out.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or you take out half of the marrow bones, and leave them until they burn out, if you stop it now.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you have more marrow, take out other bones.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse,	If the swelling does not subside, if you rub the limb with fresh blood, or if you insert a needle into it until the swelling is gone,
et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	then hold them up, and as soon as they feel some blood, if they bleed,
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see that they bleed, if you see blood oozing from the wound, cover with a little piece of aloes and hemp or charcoal, for it will stop now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This is the end of the text.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is frequently necessary in the art of medicine, and is restoration of fracture and displacement.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Listen carefully, my son, for this chapter concerns a matter that is not found in any of the old books or in any letter
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and for this reason is strange in our land, for I have never found anything like it before
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	I know of nothing like it, except for the learning from the old books, or I have studied it so much that I have become accustomed to its methods through experience and observation of my life;
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	And thus I have described in this chapter what is contained within, and I have abridged it at the end, and I have made clear the forms of the instruments which are mentioned, as I have done in the preceding chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say or prologue to this book should be the sum of words and the chapters or the learned men put their understanding into them, and remain steadfast on the truth, so that those who are proved to know and learn this noble art, and learn from others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when a break or dislocation or torsion or swelling comes to any, if it is known that the patient must be healed on one side and on the other, without anything hindering, such as weakness of the limb, or youth, or old age;
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	If the head of the shoulder is not too taut or too loose; and eat cold broth, that is to say cold juices, fat of eel and almond, and drink no wine, eat no oily foods, and do not eat too much meat which fills the veins of blood; until you have certainty of postoperative stability, not of expansion of the limb.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	When the bones break start to restore, if you think that one must nourish the patient with foods that make great nourishment, or if there is viscosity, as with flour mixed in water, and peas, and testicles, and spleen, and spleenic pain, and fish, and great wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For a part of nourishment, rest and more the fracture will mend.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that bones that are fractured in marrow and decrepit do not mend well neither join according to their nature because of the drying out of the limbs, nor those that are too tender, like bones of young children.
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet .i. gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	but there is no cure, leave the fractured bone [in place], that is to say, firm grasp which has appeared and joins the limb whole, until it strengthens as before; and do not move it in any way, for this is what is recommended for large wounds.</start_of_turn>
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are of various kinds in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that go to the marrow, and others by bending, as with the size of a pen to write.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture with a small fissure.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And at the shoulder blade there is its engine, and its own instrument in its restoration, as it comes to mind to him in its place.
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and it is known that the fracture of the bone is known by that which twists the limb, and opens well by driving, and some by pressure of the hand.
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and when there is no swelling nor pain, the patient does not feel great pain, if there is no break;
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	for it is good to keep the limb immobile while it is soft and warm, and to apply a bandage of liniment that is beneficial;
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If it is impossible for me to move the limb, but you bring medicines that come after, then restrain it now cautiously.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les .ij. parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	If the fracture that is going downwards breaks the vessels that are in the joint, and if the two parts of the joint are unequal, then you must put them back in place evenly, so that the abscesses that remain will live peacefully;
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if there is an abscess remaining, if you leave it without attention, while the abscess is still painful;
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	then put it back gently and steadily, and if there is any fracture that remains, that is more painful than if you left it whole; then restrain it cautiously as before.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de .ij. pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a .ij. cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if there are broken bones in the limb, if they extend over three parts, whether of hand or foot, or at the wrist or elbow if it is a small limb, or over two strings or a string and a limb;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and set the limb in its natural position, so that when the broken parts of the limb are separated, if you rejoin them by all means, keep that in your work there should be no further damage or pain to the patient.
et ajoste bien les .ij. chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and adjust the joints of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And he feels well in the hand if it seems to him that it is not well: if the swelling is good and does not constrain him too much, do not press so much as they do who make it come by their work an abscess and contraction of the limb, as we have often seen.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	When the limb is stiff, if the patient is very painful that he does not move it, neither watching nor sleeping, neither turning nor otherwise;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and take care that the limb is so secure that he does not feel any pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when he feels no pain, if it is not at a point, and you command him to put himself in a state of composure that he feels no pain.
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and make sure that he remains upright, for pain does not arise until he is restored.</start_of_turn>
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the quality of the limb is as I have told you.</start_of_turn>
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	The limbs are of various sizes in their breadth and length and shape.</start_of_turn
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	For there are small members, such as arms and legs and the like: if you cover them with soft linen cloths, it will suffice.
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	And for those that are large, such as hips and thighs: if you cover them with a wide and hard cloth, for the large cloths embrace the whole great limb, and constrain it everywhere equally, so that there is no tension;
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, .iij. tours ou iiij. selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	then you must support the lower limbs, i.e. two or three as the limb requires, and constrain your hand one inch from the break, then go below the break and constrain less, than the break will then move forward;
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren .i. autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and soften the limb somewhat and somewhat, until you take a great part of the limb sound, then take another limb, and turn the bandage back over the broken limb;
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	Then reapply at the lower part of the fracture, and strain moderately, not too strong nor too weak, as we said at the beginning of this chapter.
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus .i. bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Then put between the broken bones some strips of linen or cloth, so that they are all even, and then bind all around with thread, and then put your pins well made above, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or an abscess, put above something soothing the abscess, which will harden the swelling, and leave it for several days.
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	Then strain above your pins, and let them be half the width of a broad needle resting firmly, or of wire of which we make nails, or of barley groats, and let them be like this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	But it is necessary that when one sets the fracture, the tube which is placed over the break should be larger and wider than the others.
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and should be as long as it is appropriate for the small or large limb.</start_of_turn>
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then is strained on the bones just as you did at the beginning, and then bind under a thread immediately, as in the first instance on the break;
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	more is tight and less is better; and it is necessary that the thread should be medium, neither too thick nor too thin, and should be of linen wool.</start_of_turn>
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	For if the threads are thick, as I would have wished of the fools who make their knots with hemp cord, it is a great error, for the knot will not be even if it is too fine, and it will not hold but with a space between the nails.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	If the patient is bruised by the nails after the stripping in the flesh, if you put on stockings of linen or coarse cloth, so that it does not bleed.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When there is a wound with a broken bone, and the marrow is broken, I will speak of the cure later on
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And soaks that he cannot otherwise restrain must be stripped from these bones to break them at first hand.
