Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés .v. jors ou .vij., ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the limb is large, he cannot put these bones in except after five or seven days, or more as you deem necessary for the emergence of the wound;
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	And thus when the old wounds have healed, to restore the fracture, dislocation, and torsion: take flour that is held as by the walls of a mill, and mix it with eggs, and make this confection, not too fine nor too coarse, and use it.  This is the common method for restoring a fracture in various situations, and the same for women and young children, for there is neither too much pressure nor too much cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of dressing that restores the fracture and dislocation and torsion: take three barley grains, linseed, alum, saffron, and Arabic gum, and mix them with vinegar; mix mirra and aloes, with vinegar; mix alechil with vinegar; and grind them up, and mix them with eggs; if the patient’s complexion is hot, use this dressing, for it is made of good materials and will restore the fractured bones quickly, and is worth more than many homes.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .viiij. З.; acaice vi. З.; bolic armenic .x. З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Other means of displacement worth considering: take mugwort and viscum, each in quantity of .x. of a barleycorn; mirra and aloes, each in quantity of .viiij. of a barleycorn; acacia in quantity of vi. of a barleycorn; and arnica in quantity of .x. of a barleycorn; mix well, and confirm with water or the juice of an egg, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu. Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Other means of displacement for joints and bones loosened from their place: soothe pain that comes out, and reduce swelling using oil; take new linen cloth, soak it in oil and put it on the affected area. These poultices do not restore health, but they are good for soothing post-cautery pain and reducing swelling.</start_of_turn>
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another means of displacement that restores fractured bones: take dried fig leaves and terrestrial poppy leaves, grind them together, and make a poultice.</start_of_turn>
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme. Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Other methods for restoring the fracture of the bone are to remove any remaining abscess. Take root of chamomile, camomile flowers, violets flowers, wheat flour, and from cheese a part; and grind, and mix with wine, and if the limb is swollen, mix with vinegar of coriander moist or plain vinegar, and use.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre. Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Other methods for restoring the fracture are more forceful than the first. When a hard abscess comes with the restoration of the limb. Take root of vismalve, flaxseed, barley, melilot, and angelica, violets flowers and chamomile flowers, all an equal part; and grind, and mix with salt water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	In his book, Hippocrates does not put anything on the broken limb to restore its force except some wax and oil, and nothing else, and he says that it should be between soft and hard
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen deems that one must put something warm upon the broken limb to restore it, such as wax and aloe and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way of dressing that is worth for pain and swelling: take mugwort and chopped onions, or poème oil, and gum arabic, and mix them evenly, and grind them, and make a dressing of it and bind it.</start_of_turn>
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors	And then loosen a little afterwards, and take care that the patient feels no pain, that the bone is not displaced; if not, loosen it by hand every day.</start_of_turn
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	And if pain comes to the limb, or swelling, sense rest or inflammation, if you hurry, and loosen it, and place the limb in its proper position now; and take light clothing, and a sponge of moist sea-foam, and plunge into water, and lift up the limb, until the swelling ceases, and the pain is calmed.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	Then let the limb rest for an hour, then put on dry linen, soaked in water or rose oil, and bind on a bandage, until you are certain of the healing of the wound
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And rest the inflamed limb, and if there is pain, then renew the bandage tightly, and a little displacement, and do not bind too tightly; and be discreet until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see swelling, redness, pain and swelling around the bone, and that it is renewed, as you did the first time, you must provide support and lian, if necessary.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vij.; et aucune fois le laisse .xx. jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	And if it does not happen to the limb anything of what we have said, if it does not come loose for two or three or five or seven days; and in no case leave it for twenty days, according to what we have seen, until the fracture has healed, and approach the dressing of the limb above.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	Therefore greater restraint than before is needed, and nourish the limb; as I said before; and if you see the limb dry more than usual, its juices do not flow; they cannot come out.
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	The hair grows long and even; whenever you prick them at their root, keep your eyes still until they grow.
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	When the limb has been cut off by moisture, and is reset but will not stay in place, this is wrong, and if there is any doubt or fear, I see nothing else but to leave it alone and open it thoroughly.</start_of_turn>
des diverses manieres de brisure	various methods of fracture
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	There are many ways to break bones, and various figures, and the causes are diverse;
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	For there are fractures which are made by percussion of a spear, and the bone is cracked throughout its length as far as the sypha, which is the socket of the bone, as if made by a chisel or fist; and for this reason this kind of fracture is called a «haichure».
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	For when the spear pierces the bone from beneath in a forward direction, and is called this kind of fracture «absolue»; and the wound of these fractures is great or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is an embedded percussion, or fracture or displacement of the bone, or swelling on the bone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a fracture of bone that approaches the skin, which is under the skin or on the skin, this wound is great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if a wound is closed by the bone as closely as a nail, and the break is small, it is called a "capillary" fracture.
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if a wound is made by a nail, or by a thorn, or by something similar, and if it causes the bone to split inwards, and if the bone is flexible as when heated over a cauldron; if between the fragments there is a piece of bone.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	This is more serious in those who have soft bones, as in children;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And thus, in all these ways, small pieces are torn away if like these; and I shall speak of it in detail.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And thus, we know of all these breaks by the tearing above them, the questioning of tensions, and the corrupt matter which is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The capillary appearance is known by that which when we have discovered the bone, and we wipe on it above, if the black break is opened
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the break, take care of the patient’s pain, and if you see no bad accident, as vomiting of bile, emission of understanding, extension, and swelling, and fever, and the eyes grow pale and flushed, and other similar things in various positions, if not cured without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see an imminent accident, and you hope for health, if so, begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	When the limb comes first to you, and it is in the armpit, if so, it is right to remove the bone from its fourteenth part from the muscle that you must touch.</start_of_turn>
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in this state, if you are hasty to remove the bone from its seventh part from the bone that you must touch, then the tissue of the bone will be corrupted, and there will come the accident that we have mentioned.</start_of_turn>

Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is strong and tough, if you must pierce through, even though you administer nails with washers, do not pierce through anything other than the outer surface of the bone; and must have under the point a margin or circle, that does not allow the point to pass beyond the bone; and you must have several of these, so that if the nails are withdrawn from the depth of the bone, if you have washers for all tests, this is the form of two nails.
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing through a brittle bone is that you put one washer on the bone, and turn your thumbs until you feel that the bone is pierced; then put the washer back in another place a little later, and do everything around, and close the incisors of the space between the holes, and do this more subtly than you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you have reached the bone in your hand, or to any of the instruments that you have like pliers, pincers; and keep that you do not touch the brain or the jaw.

et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus. de la routure de la mandibule	Of the root of the mandible
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement. de la forcele	because of force.</start_of_turn>

The forceful rupture has occurred several times previously in this area, near the shoulder, and if it is broken in two places, there are pieces, and it is more light to restore; or if there is a break with a wound.

de la brisure de l’espaule	Then resume the manipulation, if you see that it is necessary, and hold and support it firmly until it is restored; and it is usually restored in about twenty-six days, and less in most homes.
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus .i. drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en .xx. jors ou en xxv,  Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	When the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture or has become loose in its place, it should not be forced out by any means other than touch; if the limb is repositioned according to the shape of the dislocation, and it is immobilized in its natural position in all its movements; then put on coarse powder of wheat with abundant eggshells, and put on light covers, and put on a broad and firm support, a little wider than the shoulder, and as the support is loosened, if necessary, use the support of hemp ropes, so that the support lies evenly; and then stretch the limb with a firm bend, so that the support does not move from its place, and look at the limb regularly; and every time that it relaxes, if you stretch it, and put the support back in its place if it has been forced from its place, and put the patient down on his side; and the shoulder is restored in about twenty or twenty-five days.  And when this number of days has elapsed, if the dislocation has cleared, and the limb has been plastered, for it is not the bone that is easily fractured.

And if a piece of the bone thrust forward, and not a little like before, if it stays there, and the bone, do as we said at the fracture of the forceps to appease the afterburn.

de la brisure des costes	Of the fracture of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	The ribs that break from the breast only come from the back, at the shoulder and do not bend except because they are slimy; and the pain is well known at the inquiry of two.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient. Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And the restoration is that if you put the fracture back in place, if it is right. And then put the dressing in place and bind it with a bandage, if you have need of it.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the fracture of the ribs is downward, if it causes great pain, and swelling, as if of pleura, for the bone is pressing on the gut; and there is vomiting, and all together there is great loss of blood, and that is a great grief, and many have died from it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if any of those who say it must administer food that swells the belly, to push out the pain at its departure.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, for after these chills have passed, life does not come again if it has not already begun.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	If it has already begun, then well.</start_of_turn
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they say that no one has ever put a bandage on the body to stop the fever, for it is like reason; however, there is doubt that the bandage will not draw out the superfluous humours from the body by the disposition of weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say that on must not cover the wound with coarse linen soaked in oil, but put on tents between the ribs to make equal the hour around, then either cure with the treatment for pleurisin, meat and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz .i. estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear from the bone that points to the loin, and there is doubt for the patient, if you must cut on the bone of the broken rib, and you must put in place an instrument to hold the skin; then you must also break the bone, treat gently, and then suture the two layers of the wound, if it is large, and treat with sponges, until it is healed. And if an abscess comes, if you put on wet cloths soaked in rose oil, and put on the wound; and treat while the bone that you must break is at a distance from the abscess, and do not leave it until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
de la brisure dou col	of the fracture of the collar bone.</start_of_turn>
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Never comes a sudden break of a bone in the neck, or indeed at the spine in the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent. Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	And when this happens to anyone, and you see that he is whole or not, if you take notice that his hands are limp and fleeing and dead, and that you cannot move or extend them, and when you prick them with a needle, if he does not groan. Such is death in many cases, and if you move them and he feels well when you strain and prick them, such is that the bone joint is saved, and the patient will be healed, if you put in cure.</start_of_turn>
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit. And if the same thing happens at the spine in the back, and you see that he is whole or not, if you take notice that his limbs are softened, and that his accidents are in his hands and on his back there is a violent vomiting and evacuation without will; and when we have treated him on his belly, there is a violent vomiting without will. And when he is treated on his back and he looks to his side, if he cannot vomit. Such is death: if he does not work in his cure.</start_of_turn>
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	If this mishap does not occur, then the matter is less serious.
