de la brisure de l’ajutoire	De la brisure de l’ajutoire.
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	From the dislocation of the shoulder
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And there are two methods for restoring it: one is to take a fistful of moist earth and shape it like this:
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is that one should order the attendants to hold the limb firmly at its collar and to grasp the limb above the elbow with the fist of the hand that is not supporting it, and to hold down the forearm with the other hand, and to extend the forearm to its greatest extent.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint .i. liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part. Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes .i. liien moien desoz l’assele, et .i. autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre .i. liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the extraction is too strong, if it strains [the shoulder], hold the bone at the base of the bone; and on the bone, extend the thumbs of the attendants to their part. And if the bone is close to the head of the shoulder, if you must put in [a ligature] the middle of the bone at the shoulder, and the other towards the elbow, grasp the bone; and just as if the bone is towards the elbow, if you must put in [a ligature] the lesser, with some labor, until the bone is even on both sides, and on the shoulder; then put the bone straight, if it is possible, and strain, for the wound does not come out.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if the wound does not come out, do not strain for more than thirteen days; put on a soft bandage and oil of rose, until the wound is calmed; then strain, and put the support on the bone, then assemble the limb on the aid, and put your hand on the shoulder or on the breast; and put on the bandage, strain on the aid, and on the limb, so that the limb is in its place, without anything hindering it, or without displacing the bone.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone is not displaced, if you use pins, put on the bone a pin wider and stronger than the others, and leave between the pins a space equal to twice the thickness of the bone; then strain on the pins, as I have said at the beginning of this chapter, more strongly and less loosely.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns .iij. jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois. Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If you see the sitting of the stars and the tightening, as we have said, in the hour when you restore the limb, if you doubt the incision, let it stay closed until the seventh day, as we have said; then look carefully for two days, that the wound does not swell or become infected, or that the nerves do not become numb in the limb because of its tension. If it is necessary, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire .i. cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse. Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en .xl. jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.  Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier .l. jors ou .ij. mois.	If no such thing happens, if more than two days have passed, and the patient lies down on his back, with his hands on his stomach; put a dressing on the shoulder with wool equal in size, and look for an hour or two to see if the limb is not moving or if the ligaments are not softened; if it is necessary, by the power of medicine, and do as I have said before, partly as a remedy. And when it begins to recover, if it is large. It is customary that the shoulder and limb must be taken off for forty days in total; and then it must be loosened and a bath and ointment applied to the affected part. And if the dislocation is difficult and involves blood clots, it should be left to loosen for one or two months.
de la brisure du bras	... for a fracture of the arm.
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm consists of three bones, which are called the "radius" and the "ulna". One is small and is close to the pouch, and the other is large and is close to the little finger; by chance the large bone only breaks sometimes, or the small one, and sometimes both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble. Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	When the small bone is broken, the restoration is easy and the healing; but when the large bone is broken, if the healing is bad, it is more painful than when they are broken together. If only the small bone is broken, if the limb is gently extended, and made even.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus .i. cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et .i. cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a .i. liien, et uns autres ministres a .i. autre au desus. Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And if it is the large bone that is broken, if the limb must be drawn more strongly; and hold the pouch of the hand higher than the others, and keep the small one lower than the others, and let the patient cross his arm over himself, and the pouch in front of him higher than the patient suffers no pain; then extend the limb slowly from the shoulder to the wrist, or from the elbow, and another assistant from the other side. And then put it back in its place, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	If in the fracture it is broken into pieces, if you put something into its place, and if there is none that pricks it now, and you do not manage to restore it to its place, if you leave it and the bone, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	If in the fracture it is broken into pieces, as I have mentioned in the singular concerning this chapter; take the cure.</start_of_turn>
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue .i. drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie .i. drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez. Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir vj. esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en .ij.; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit. Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	If at the commencement of restoration blood comes out through the incisions, if you glue them with a bandage made of rose oil and white wax, that it be neither too tight nor too loose; and bind them securely with strips so that the incisions are appeased. And then bone the wax, and put in place the plaster of molin with abundance of eggshell, because put the pins in, and let the pin of the fracture be more firm, and a space wider than the others; and that there be a space between the pins that must have at least as many holes as there are bones or arms in multiple positions: either that the fracture is in one of the bones or in two places; and is more strained above the fracture than elsewhere, and is most painful on the first day, less so on subsequent days, as I have said at the commencement of this chapter; and let the bandages that are above the fracture be soft and moist, and neither too hard nor brittle; and let the thread that is used for tying be neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said. And reinforce the limb and the tendon afterwards for several days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer. Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And if any evil accident befalls the limb, as for example a wound which befalls the limb, then shalt thou raise the limb with warm water, until such time as the itching ceaseth; and let the limb rest undisturbed. And then commence the treatment anew, and if the ligament be torn and the bone be fractured, or things of like nature, if need be.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the swelling does not depart from the limb, because it is too great, then shalt thou soften it, namely by fomentation, and let it remain for some days, until the swelling depart, and then restrain it.</start_of_turn>
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a .xx. jors. ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en .xxx. jors ou en .xxxv., et par aventure en .xx. jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	And if none of these things which we have said doth avail the patient, if not until after .xx. days, or more, then thou shalt bind up his hands to his neck, and let his neck be even, and shalt guard against movement and eating, and he shall sleep on his back; and give him nourishment every .xxx. days or every .xxxv., or every .xx. days, according to the composition and temperament of the remedies.</start_of_turn>
de la brisure de la main	Of the breaking of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	The bones at the back of the hand and two together cause many fractures, and only rain comes more often.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the hand is broken or rained on, if it is to be known that the patient should sit cross-legged, and sit upright in front of him equally; then put his hand on the extended cloth, and extend the physician the broken bones, and put them equal with the eyes; and put on the plaster and the bandage, if there is no opening; then put on a splint as much as is necessary; and be covered with a cloth of linen.</start_of_turn>
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is at the shoulder blade under the belly of the limb, if you make a ball of cloth, and command the patient to hold his broken limb against his side; then strain from a long cloth, and be the splint as great as the limb, and strain it, as it is commanded.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the break is downwards, if you command me to place a splint above and another below, so that the hand is overspread and straight, then I will bind it tightly around the hand, and hold it between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the break does not come from either side, if it is in the palm, if you command me to make it even, as it should be; and I will restrain it with the splint, and if you see that I must place a right-angle splint to raise the break, and it does not move; and if the break is in another place, as in the index or one of the others, if you make it even, and I will bind it with the two fingers which follow; or you will bind them all together, holding them close together, as much as he wants, or you will place a splint above, as with a pouch; and take care of the restoration and the arrangement of the wound, and cure whatever comes of it, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	And if the break does not come from either side, if it is in the palm, if you command me to make it even, as it should be; and I will restrain it with the splint, and if you see that I must place a right-angle splint to raise the break, and it does not move; and if the break is in another place, as in the index or one of the others, if you make it even, and I will bind it with the two fingers which follow; or you will bind them all together, holding them close together, as much as he wants, or you will place a splint above, as with a pouch; and take care of the restoration and the arrangement of the wound, and cure whatever comes of it, as I have said.
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bones of the hip are often fractured, and one can see it when it turns frontward and backward; and the restoration is when it is bound together again.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	The patient lies on his face, then extends his limbs symmetrically; and it is when the fracture is at the root of the bone
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure. Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses .ij. mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if the fracture is close to the root of the thigh, if either of the ligaments above the knee is torn, and the other ligament below the fracture; and in the same way if it is close to the knee, and then either the ligament above the knee or the extension below; then put the limb in its natural position with both hands, until it is parallel to its natural position, and then put on the dressing and bind it, if necessary.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a wound close to the eye, if you leave it calm for a while and then return to your work and your cure, the binding is made in part for safety.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure .i. bendeil dur doublé en .ij. ou .iij., et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute .i. fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment .iij. tors ou iiij. sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as .ij. chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie .iij. esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary to wrap around the edge of the wound, that is, a double bandage about two or three fingers in length, and hold the excess, then bend the limb until the nails reach the root of the nail; then pass one thread long between the hip and the limb, below the knee, and bring it up to the top; then bend the limb and the hip together with the bandage, and put on the edge of the wound the stars, and put a star on the bone of the limb; then put eight threads between the limb and the hip of coarse gauze to make even the tension, and begin to tie in pairs or threes on the edge of the wound; and the more you go up the wound, and less the strain; then take out two or three threads that you have passed between the limb and the hip, and tie two stars that are below, and put back the thread to the top, until you see that the wound has healed; and the strain, if it does not move from its place, then leave it alone, and it will not cause any wound or swelling or anything like that.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if there is pain, if it comes loose, and address what has come, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that prick, it is necessary to cauterize, as we have said; and if we cannot, it is necessary to cut the bone, and drain; and cure as we have said, when it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And never is the bone broken in this case when it is set in place, as in the shoulder and arm; nevertheless, in the restoration made in this way, I do not cause pain to the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And if the bone is set in place in one or two days, or less or more, according to the variety of temperaments.</start_of_turn>
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the rue of Genoa</start_of_turn>
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois. Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou .i. pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	There are often breaks in the street of Genoa, but they happen many times. And if it breaks, it is not more than a tear, or a hole, and there is pain, and sense of pain, and this is well known.</start_of_turn>
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And thus, if you put everything that is round back to its place, as long as it is put together firmly, then put the dressing on and place a round cushion there if you have need of it, and hold it firmly, then restore all the other things that we have mentioned before, such as an abscess incision and other similar things; if you put each accident in its place that it deserves, as long as it is sane.
de la brisure de la jambe	And thus, if you put everything that is round back to its place, as long as it is put together firmly, then put the dressing on and place a round cushion there if you have need of it, and hold it firmly, then restore all the other things that we have mentioned before, such as an abscess incision and other similar things; if you put each accident in its place that it deserves, as long as it is sane.
Saiches que en la jambe ait .ij. os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i.	And thus, if you put everything that is round back to its place, as long as it is put together firmly, then put the dressing on and place a round cushion there if you have need of it, and hold it firmly, then restore all the other things that we have mentioned before, such as an abscess incision and other similar things; if you put each accident in its place that it deserves, as long as it is sane. Saiches that are in the limb have two bones; one is called the "mustelz" and the other is called the "foscile"; and there is a fracture in the limb as it comes to the arm, and for this the restoration is the same as that of the arm, and the work is whole again.
Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	If two bones are fractured together, twist the limb from all sides.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	If the bone is fractured in two, twist the limb forward.</start_of_turn>
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz. Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	If a great bone is fractured, if one feels great pain and sees it clearly; and twist the limb downwards. Immediately apply extension, and make it equal, and bind the bones equally; but always remember that if the fracture is serious, and there are many pieces, that the extension should be less violent and lighter; and adjust accordingly.</start_of_turn
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Once you have completed your work, if you take two strips of coarse cloth that reach from under the armpit to under the knee of the limb, and bind the limb from one end to the other; then cover with two layers of bandage from under and over, and bind firmly in the middle, and with this binding the limb will not be able to move forward or backward; and that is good; and no one should administer anything that will lengthen the limb, and if there is swelling, and it is a fracture, and there are many pieces, that the extension should be less violent and lighter; and adjust accordingly.
de la brisure des os dou piet	Of the fracture of bones it is known.
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	As for the ankle, there is no fracture in it; but in the bones of the foot there is never a fracture and two are enough, and there is no other cause of death except for great swelling of the limb.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is a fracture in the bones of the foot, and you see these bones pressing against one another, if you put the limb so that it appears to be floating in the air, as if a bird were flying by, and then put the limb back in its place, the bones will rise up; then put the bandage in place and bind the limb firmly, and put a little bandage under the foot at the joint, and strain the limb gently, and when the swelling has gone down cover the limb with cloth and other things as you think is necessary.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when two or three days have passed, if the limb is still swollen, because you will find the bones whole, whether fractured or not.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	If there are two breaks, if you restore them as we have said must be done with the hand; then put at the break a support according to the length of the break, and make it somewhat wider; and put on the thumb that which I have mentioned, and strain immediately; and if there are three or more breaks, break them, and put on over each break a support according to its quantity, enveloped in one layer of linen, and strain the thumb from the bone. Make sure that the thumb remains above the break of the bone as much as possible, if it remains well-held.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	Remember also the other things that I have said about other breaks; and secure each accident as it should be secured.</start_of_turn>
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the clavicle bone</start_of_turn>
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com .i. sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice .vij. jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the natural woman's bone is broken, if she sits enlarged, then incline towards the part of her backbone; be held by behind; then fill the belly of the nature with wool, and put as much as a sto at will; then evacuate the woman, and hold her loin from front and back; and immediately jump the wool, until it comes to the entrance of the nature, and return the bone with the sto; and when she sees pissing, if the bone is grasped by the wool, and when she has pissed, she will recover, and thus make seventy-two days or more: if the fracture is restored, and if you see that, take a bladder of elderberry, and tie a string to the belly, and empty all the bladder into the nature; then blow through the string until the bladder is emptied: the nature will then restore the fracture; then fill with wool, and leave it for a few days, until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre. Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	And when the wrist bone of a man or woman is broken, if you restore it as we have said concerning the thigh bone; and these fractures that happen to the forearm do not hide from the one who studies and uses them, and understand my book. For the fracture signifies in many cases the right way of restoration: understand that then
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the arm, when it is broken, take a goose neck and put it on the arm; then wrap around it with cloths, and leave it for two days or until it is healed, and it will be completely healed.
de brisure avec plaie	Of sudden with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	In case of sudden fracture with wound, even if it is great, as for the bones of the thigh or the shoulder or similar, that it be set immediately, as the things we have said prove.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is clean, if the restoration of vitriol suffice, if you have nothing else, then begin to restore the fracture in the same hour, or the next, if there is no coming of the after-effects.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if there comes swelling, if you must leave the restoration until next day, as long as the swelling is appeased, and do not touch neither the third nor the fourth part, for you will bring about other evils.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the bone is fractured is appears above like a wound discovered, then you must know that you must touch it lightly with your hands, slightly extended.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension does not appear to you to set your hands equal, if the limb has this instrument which is of iron, which is two or three inches long, and its breadth is according to the quantity of the wound; for this reason it is necessary at the middle that it grasps three or four lines, according to what is necessary in the bruise; and be round and somewhat large, so that it does not swell to the compression on the limb at your work, and be above and forward, and large from the middle forward, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre. Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	It is called "palainche" because it must be known that when the limb is bent, it must be placed upon the visible part of the bone; and once it has been placed, it must be equal, so that one meets the other. And if the fracture is subtle, and the instrument does not well grasp the bone, if you must bend the chief of the bone, as long as the instrument has possession of it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	If you cannot restore the bone as we have said, if you see that the handle of an instrument that can be covered over is to be used, or to pierce or suture, to your poorness; then take away that which is remaining in the bone, rough and scaly.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil. Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille .i. drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	When the bone is restored, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, swelling that it is not in its natural position. If you do too much and it remains in its place, then moisten it with black vinegar; and if it is in this state; do not put anything on the wound except cerate or oil, for it will cause decay and corruption; then administer stars when the bone has been restored, and leave the wound uncovered, and cover the dressing all around, according to the quantity of the wound, and take good care that the wound is not strained with the bursting; for many times this has been the cause of death among fools, and has caused the patient to die or become lame or corrupt countless times; and let the itching be milder and less severe than other breaks.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie. Et quant tu vois aprés .i. jor ou .ij. enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And if the wound is small or large, and you doubt that the accident will suffice, as we have said, and you feel pain in the limb, if it does not suffice to put on stars; but cover it around, instead of stars, with firm cloths, and bind them. And when you see afterwards that there is blood seeping through the wound, if the thing that you put on the wound has become soft, put an astringent ointment on the wound, like an ointment of four medicines and the like.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you stretch the limb three times a day, in the morning and in the evening, while it is soldered and healthy.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be gently flexed and straightened part by part like a bow that corrects itself lightly.</start_of_turn>
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if the limb persists in displacement, and cannot be soldered but returns almost to its place, with small pieces of bone, for it is necessary that you reduce the wound with all your might, and that you extract all these broken pieces which cause this pain.</start_of_turn
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant. Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés .xx. jors ou .xxx., puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And if a fistula arises in the limb, or any other form of corruption, it is necessary that you treat it, according to what is stated in this chapter above. And when a bone is broken, and is exposed on the limb, as the bone of the shoulder or the arm, and other similar bones of the great limbs, if you do not treat it, for many times death results, but leave it until it has healed; by chance it will go away by itself within twenty or thirty days, and then cure the wound if you wish; or if you do not wish, leave it.</start_of_turn
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	The hairs which come out of the beard.
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	The hairs which come out of the beard often follow the breaking of the wind, even when it is close to the joint; and it is a helpful thing to see the figure of the limb; for by chance one cannot make the limb do its natural work.</start_of_turn>
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care therefore that we are aware: if he gives astringent medicines, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocollus, acaice, and others, that you take neither of these things, or all together, and mix them with stiff wine or with eggs or with oil; and put them on the wound in bandages, and bind it well, and do not move it from hand to hand until it is set; and then reset it, and begin again, until the nodation is bony; or you bind it on a piece of well-made leather; for the property of leather is that it hardens all the swellings under the limb; and if the nodation has already hardened as much as a stone, and it is necessary to harden it, if the swelling above has burst, and make the excess apparent; or you must leave it alone, until it is bony, and treat it until it is healed.</start_of_turn
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	The limb that is weak after the treatment.
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture is restored and remains weak afterwards, if there is any discomfort: because sometimes it is caused by the limb having been too tightly bound and not properly relaxed; or because there are too many bands, and they prevent the limb from moving smoothly; or because of many bruises; or because of too great a movement, not even in its place; or because there is blood in the tissue, if it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is to feed the patient and make the limb firm, until the pain is multiplied in him; and give him baths, and make him merry and comfortable; then put a poultice on the limb, so that the poultice attracts the great restoration, and the blood often boils fiercely, until the limb returns to its natural position; and return to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	The limb is bent after the disease.
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is bent after restoration, and the bone is broken open, and the limb is deformed, although it retains its natural work: if one does not believe the fools who say that the limb must be broken anew, and many have acted thus in our land; this work is blamed, and many evils result from it, and by chance the patient; although if the swellings and torture are fresh, if one covers them with hot water, or softens them with herbs such as rue, meadowsweet, and melilot, and similar things; and makes an emollient plaster, like aquaint well made, and takes the muscle of rue, and confirms it with gelatine grease or oil of poppy seed, and makes plaster over; or one takes fat figs, and pounds them with horse dung, and similar medicines that appease the swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes. Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And never is the bone displaced by continuous rubbing and for a long time with wet hands. And keep the limb in motion for an hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the dislocation is swollen and hardened, like a stone, and requires iron, if it is covered with skin up to the bone, make a slight incision; and apply cushion and dressing to the wound.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	And thus begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes about, if it can now be corrected in its original position
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	For if it is late, if by chance he remembers it and comes to pinch it again, do not move it because it is swollen; for many times it has caused swelling and other pains.
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	Indeed, when this happens, if he makes the patient comfortable, then let him go; until the swelling subsides. Then raise the limb high and liberally, and support it gently, and treat each limb as it comes to its place.</start_of_turn>
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have commanded the chapters on dislocations of the shoulder joint from the head to the wrist.</start_of_turn>
des mandibules	Des mandibules.
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	The teeth are loosened and the jaw is dislocated in two ways: either the jawbone is fractured from its socket and softened, or it is loosened completely and hangs downwards, causing the tongue to hang out of the mouth, unable to be held in place, unable to close the mouth, and to be enveloped by speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it often returns by itself in various positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	and if it is complete and accompanied, you must immediately immobilize it, and do not touch it;
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de .ij. pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And in such a manner that the minister grasps the head of the patient, and holds the gaze fixed on the pocket of one of his hands at the root of the dislocation of the mandible in the mouth, if the dislocation is three-quarters gone; and the other hand must be freed, so that they are even; and command the patient to soften his mandibles and move them from all sides.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And keep the eye fixed even, until it returns to its place.</start_of_turn>
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it returns grasped, even if both mandibles are together, if they arise with hot oil, as long as they remain lightly; do not attempt to force it back, as we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are brought back even, and the patient's mouth is closed with the tongue properly clotted, if you put on moist cloths in a circle made of rose oil and beeswax, then bind them lightly with threads.
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre .ij. cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	And the patient should sleep on their back, with the arms resting between two cushions, so that they do not move towards the chest or to the sides, without making any effort to raise them up, but take some gentle nourishment, as long as the pain subsides, and keep the jaw closed
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	and then eat only lightly, and do not open your mouth wide while eating or drinking, until the jaw is well closed and healed.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two mandibles do not manage to be reset at a single hour, and are not made firm at their roots, if in comes fever and swelling accustomed, and by chance vomiting of pure bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, know that it is a loss; and many times death follows in eight days.</start_of_turn>
de la forcelle	from the forceps.
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forceps cannot pull out a wound that is deeply seated, and is always damaged when it is driven out, and it is always felt.</start_of_turn
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	And if the patient lies prone on his back and extends his arms; then press the limb towards your palm, and it will return; then put on the bandage and bind it tightly, and strain it.
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if the limb which is beside the cuticle cannot be loosened; if it does loosen once, if you leave it in its place, as we have said; then put on the bandage and bind it tightly, and strain it, and command the patient to rest until he is well again.
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And thus the limb is brought back to its place, when it is loosened from its bone.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	De la dislocation de l’espaule.
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc .iij. manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	From the dislocation of the shoulder.
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	and does not damage further behind for the shoulder, and does not damage further from the nerves; and many times dislocates downwards towards the armpit, just as when there is much hair, for at these leaps there is great pain; at those who have little hair, the leaps are painful, and return painful.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes there occurs in some households a percussion or cracking, and it engulfs the swelling of an abscess with a thick discharge, and care must be taken that it is not damaged by this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Therefore it is necessary that you suspend it until you are certain; and then begin the treatment.</start_of_turn>
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And it is known that a dislocation occurs when it is twisted towards the shoulder, and it makes a difference between the painful and the sound shoulder, and you will find between their difference the cause of the pain.</start_of_turn
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	and at the head of the shoulder you will find a pit, and the shoulder is dislocated from the touch of the head of the shoulder, as if it were a bone; and it cannot move in any way, neither to move the hand to the elbow, nor to move anything else.</start_of_turn
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	And thus, if it is displaced upwards and is not hidden, for you will find it clearly on touching.
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And this kind of dislocation is not forced to restore, when it is new, or when the limb is painful.</start_of_turn>
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is that the physician grasps the painful limb upwards, then puts the thumbs downwards on the buttocks, and grasps the joint firmly upwards to the bone; and the physician grasps the limb and extends it upwards, since it is put downwards.</start_of_turn
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	And if it does not come as we have said before, if it is to be believed that the patient is to be bathed in warm water; and it is to be administered mild and soothing nourishment, such as decoction of elderberry and fenugreek and honey in water, and to be administered.</start_of_turn
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	Then either soothe the patient on his back, and place on his seat a cushion of linen even, not too soft nor too hard, then place his hand on the cushion, and keep the shoulder joint firmly in place, and treat the hand of the patient.

And another minister treats the patient's hand downwards towards the belly. And if the patient is too weak, if he can hold nothing heavy, the dislocation will return immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche .i. lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com .i. pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	And thus it is also done in another way: and if the bone is long like a nail in the earth, which the head of the shoulder must be as round as a ball, and not too thick or too thin;

et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren .i. tison de .ij. bras de grant et .iiij. dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	If these things do not suffice to restore it, if you perform this cure: take one fistful of three fingers and two palms of large size, which has the thumb bent forward to enter into the armpit, as in this fashion:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then place the thumb of the fist over the base of the arm, so that it does not move the patient; put it into the armpit; extend your arms above the arm of the patient; and hold the shoulder joint above the arm, and the arm at the wrist; put one elbow on one inch of the palm of the hand, and stretch out the hands backwards, or leave the forearm hanging down: the dislocation will now be regained.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is regained, in whatever way, if you put a ball of wool of equal size under the armpit, then put the plaster on the abscess with powdered oatmeal, with incense and egg-white, on the whole shoulder and around, and strain the armpit outwards again, and bind the limb over the plaster, and embrace the hand at its collar, and keep the hands still.</start_of_turn>
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is commanded that he should move his arm until it is comfortable, for it will heal more quickly; and then move it more after five or six days, and it will be healed.  If it is stiff and is not softened, it is healed.

And if the joint is forced from its place by moisture or for some other reason, if it is commanded that you administer cautery twice as deep as it is placed before or as a chapter of cautery.

And if you do all this, and it does not heal after twenty-five days, and the limb cannot be lifted, then know that the nerves of the shoulder are crushed or stretched or softened; and that the joint will never be fixed in its place again
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The shoulder dislocation that is at the side of the arm, and the arms, or behind, if it is done by impulse, and extension of the hands, and has received another support; and it heals as long as it is sound.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And when the healing has passed, if there is stiffness in the limb and late mobility, if the patient uses the limb many times, as long as the stiffness is relieved, and returns to its first nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	because of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	The joint of the shoulder has been damaged at several points, and has returned to its normal position; but it has been damaged throughout, both frontally and laterally, and the dislocation has not been corrected, as it is well seen and felt; and it is damaged in a certain way.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement. Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	And when you join the patient with the limb, if he can see it openly. For the joint is shut, and cannot bend the arm, touch his shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And you must keep it still in this way even after you have pulled it out, for if you pull it out again, if it comes out once more, it will be more painful to bring it back. And by chance it will not be able to be brought back at all, even if it is behind; for it is better to leave it as it is than to cause further dislocation, which is more painful and can lead to death.</start_of_turn>
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And if it can be restored, when it is like this that you can bring it back, you must extend your hand with both hands; and let your arms be spread out, and your hands down toward your belly according to the patient’s situation, front and back, and hold the joint together with your thumbs and index fingers until it returns to its place.</start_of_turn>
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	If the dislocation is in front, if it returns when the hand doubles over its hand, and the thumb is firm at the root that is deshydrated.

When it is in place, if you put on dry plaster with an egg-shaped weight, and the strain forms, and you bend the arm at the shoulder of the patient, and leave it for a while, then you can release it.

li dislocation de la main	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut. des dislocations de la hainche	hip dislocation
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	The joints of the hip and shoulder only dislocate; it does not happen with other joints; and the hip joint is damaged in three parts: front and back, and top and bottom; the more it is damaged from the front, the more it is damaged from the back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	And if you know of a dislocation, that is when, if you join the painful limb with the flesh, if it is longer, and if the patient’s knee is wider than the normal, and he cannot double his knee at the fire.

And the sign of this is that if it is well placed, the limb is well placed in accordance with the completion; however, do not double the knee excessively in pain, and if you see that it is suffering, do not delay, and retain the urine, and swell the limb, and when he walks, let him pass over the heel.

et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche .i. passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide;	If it cannot return naturally, if you make the patient lie on his back on the ground, and put a passage firmly in the ground between his thighs, and tie the blanket around him, that he does not move the patient.
puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a .i. liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet;	Then hold the limb at the hip, and another assistant extends the limb with his hands or with a string, which is placed on the collar of the limb;
puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent;	Then extend the legs of the assistants equally, and keep the passage either between the patient’s thighs to hold the patient when extending him;
puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	Then put the thumbs equal to the dislocation at his hands, and another assistant grasps the limb at the shoulder, and the dislocation will return immediately.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois;	And when it [the dislocation] has reached a point, put on the plaster and bandage above, and the strain forms, and bind the limb to the leg, and keep the nerves that are above the ankle behind, so that the bands are not too tight;
puis le laisse .ij. jors ou .iij., et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par .iiij. jors;	Then leave it [the bandage] for one or two days, and if the bands slacken, strain; then take it off at the third or fourth hour, and tell the patient by the third day.
et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	and if it goes before this end, it is not certain that it will not damage further.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the wound bleeds profusely when the vein is opened or the abscess is incised, as we have mentioned before, you must keep the wound still until it has healed.
des dois	If the wound bleeds profusely when the vein is opened or the abscess is incised, as we have mentioned before, you must keep the wound still until it has healed.
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus .i. leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne;	And if the dislocation is not in the back of the shoulder, if you must make the patient sit up straight on a bed or a table, and place your limb on what is open from these joints, then press on your limb firmly until it returns to its place
et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a .ij. chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse .iij. jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When they are even, and nothing is open, if you put a dose of rue plant on a table at a quarter past nine, then the swelling forms, and you leave it for two days, then you remove it; and you rest it until it is healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	When there is wound and dislocation together,
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	When wound comes with dislocation, and it is seen restored, many times it happens that the patient dies.
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	if you are not presumptuous in the cure, if you do not know how to use it for a long time, and if you are not merciful and compassionate and timely, do not be arrogant;
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	And use at the beginning of things tranquil and calm, if you do not see hope of health; leave the patient in the hand of God.
et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne;	And when you see hope, if you now restore the limb to its place, even though the abscess remains;
et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis;	And when the limb is in place, if you administer tranquil things and cauterize the wound, as it should be, with desiccated ointment;
et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples;	And if with dislocation there is fracture, and minor bones are loosened, if the bones, and do what we have said in simple diseases;
et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors. Amen	And keep away from danger, as I have said, for this brings shame upon you according to your Creator, and for the preservation of your arms and your body. Amen.
Explicit le romen de fisique	And keep away from danger, as I have said, for this brings shame upon you according to your Creator, and for the preservation of your arms and your body. Amen.
